10068-8{_}717{_}But Johnnie looked forward to her present enterprise as a soldier going into a new country to conquer it.
10068-8{_}718{_}She was buoyantly certain, and determinedly delighted with everything.
10068-8{_}719{_}When, the next morning after her arrival, Mandy Meacham shook her by the shoulder and bade her get up, the room was humming with the roar of mill whistles, and the gray dawn leaking in at its one window in a churlish, chary fashion, reminded her that they were under the shadow of a mountain instead of living upon its top.
10068-8{_}720{_}"I don't see what in the world could 'a' made me sleep so!"
10068-8{_}721{_}Johnnie deprecated, as she made haste to dress herself.
10068-8{_}722{_}"Looks like I never had nothing to do yesterday, except walking down.
10068-8{_}723{_}I've been on foot that much many a time and never noticed it."
10068-8{_}724{_}The other girls in the room, poor souls, were all cross and sleepy.
10068-8{_}725{_}Nobody had time to converse with Johnnie.
10068-8{_}726{_}As they went down the stairs another contingent began to straggle up, having eaten a hasty meal after their night's work, and making now for certain of the just-vacated beds.
10068-8{_}727{_}Johnnie ran into the kitchen to help Mrs. Bence get breakfast on the table, for Pap Himes was bad off this morning with a misery somewhere, and his daughter was sending word to the cotton mill to put a substitute on her looms till dinner time.
10068-8{_}728{_}Almost as much to her own surprise as to that of everybody else, Mandy Meacham proposed to stay and take Johnnie in to register for a job.
10068-8{_}729{_}When the others were all seated at table, the new girl from the mountains took her cup of coffee and a biscuit and dropped upon the doorstep to eat her breakfast.
10068-8{_}730{_}The back yard was unenclosed, a litter of tin cans and ashes running with its desert disorder into a similar one on either side.
10068-8{_}731{_}But there were no houses back of the Himes place, the ground falling away sharply to the rocky creek bed.
10068-8{_}732{_}Across the ravine half a dozen strapping young fellows were lounging, waiting for breakfast; loom-fixers and mechanics these, whose hours were more favourable than those of the women and children workers.
10068-8{_}733{_}"It's lots prettier out here than it is in the house," she returned smilingly, when Mavity Bence offered to get her a chair.
10068-8{_}734{_}"I do love to be out-of-doors."
10068-8{_}735{_}"Huh," grunted Mandy with her mouth full of biscuit, "I reckon a cotton mill'll jest about kill you.
10068-8{_}736{_}What makes you work in one, anyhow?
10068-8{_}737{_}I wouldn't if I could help it."
10068-8{_}738{_}Johnnie eyed the tall girl gravely.
10068-8{_}739{_}"I've got to earn some money," she said at length.
10068-8{_}740{_}"Ma and the children have to be taken care of.
10068-8{_}741{_}I don't know of any better way than the mill."
10068-8{_}742{_}"An' I don't know of any worse," retorted Mandy sourly, as they went out together.
10068-8{_}743{_}Johnnie began to feel timid.
10068-8{_}744{_}There had been a secret hope that she would meet Shade on the way to the mill, or that Mrs. Bence would finally get through in time to accompany her.
10068-8{_}745{_}She was suddenly aware that there was not a soul within sound of her voice who had belonged to her former world.
10068-8{_}746{_}With a little gasp she looked about her as they entered the office.
10068-8{_}747{_}The Hardwick mill to which they now came consisted of a number of large, red brick buildings, joined by covered passage-ways, abutting on one of those sullen pools Johnnie had noted the night before, the yard enclosed by a tight board fence, so high that the operatives in the first-and second-floor rooms could not see the street.
10068-8{_}748{_}This for the factory portion; the office did not front on the shut-in yard, but opened out freely on to the street, through a little grassy square of its own, tree-shadowed, with paved walks and flower beds.
10068-8{_}749{_}As with all the mills in its district, the suggestion was dangerously apt of a penitentiary, with its high wooden barrier, around all the building, the only free approach from the world to its corridors through the seemly, humanized office, where abided the heads, the bosses, the free men, who came and went at will.
10068-8{_}750{_}The walls were already beginning to wear that garment of green which the American ivy flings over so many factory buildings.
10068-8{_}751{_}As the two girls came up, Johnnie looked at the wide, clear, plate windows, the brass railing that guarded the heavy granite approach, the shining name "Hardwick" deep-set in brazen lettering on the step over which they entered.
10068-8{_}752{_}Inside, the polished oak and metal of office fittings carried on the idea of splendour, if not of luxury.
10068-8{_}753{_}Back of the crystal windows were the tempering shades, all was spacious, ordered with quiet dignity, and there was no sense of hurry in the well-clad, well-groomed figures of men that sat at the massive desks or moved about the softly carpeted floors.
10068-8{_}754{_}The corridor was long, but cleanly swept, and, at its upper portion, covered with a material unfamiliar to Johnnie, but which she recognized as suited to its purpose.
10068-8{_}755{_}Down at the further end of that corridor, something throbbed and moaned and roared and growled--the factory was awake there and working.
10068-8{_}756{_}The contrast struck cold to the girl's heart.
10068-8{_}757{_}Here, yet more sharply defined, was the same difference she had noted between the Palace of Pleasure on the heights and the mills at the foot of the mountain.
10068-8{_}758{_}Would the people think she was good enough?
10068-8{_}759{_}Would they understand how hard she meant to try?
10068-8{_}760{_}For a minute she had a desperate impulse to turn and run.
10068-8{_}761{_}Then she heard Mandy's thin, flatted tones announcing:  "This hyer girl wants to git a job in the mill.
10068-8{_}762{_}Miz Bence, she cain't come down this morning--you'll have to git somebody to tend her looms till noon; Pap, he's sick, and she has obliged to wait on him--so I brung the new gal."
10068-8{_}763{_}"All right," said the man she addressed.
10068-8{_}764{_}"She can wait there; you go on to your looms."
10068-8{_}765{_}Johnnie sat on the bench against the wall where newcomers applying for positions were placed.
10068-8{_}766{_}The man she was to see had not yet come to his desk, and she remained unnoticed and apparently forgotten for more than an hour.
10068-8{_}767{_}The offices were entered from the other side, yet a doorway close by Johnnie commanded a view of a room and desk.
10068-8{_}768{_}To it presently came one who seated himself and began opening and reading letters.
10068-8{_}769{_}Johnnie caught her breath and leaned a little forward, watching him, her heart in her eyes, hands locked hard together in her lap.
10068-8{_}770{_}It was the young man of the car.
10068-8{_}771{_}He was not in white flannels now, but he looked almost as wonderful to the girl in his gray business suit, with the air of easy command, and the quiet half-smile only latent on his face.
10068-8{_}772{_}Shade Buckheath had spoken of Gray Stoddard as the boss of the bosses down at Cottonville.
10068-8{_}773{_}Indeed, his position was unique.
10068-8{_}774{_}Inheritor of large holdings in Eastern cotton-mill stock, he had returned from abroad on the death of his father, to look into this source of his very ample income.
10068-8{_}775{_}The mills in which he was concerned were not earning as they should, so he was told; and there was discussion as to whether they be moved south, or a Southern mill be established which might be considered in the nature of a branch, and where the coarser grades of sheeting would be manufactured, as well as all the spinning done.
10068-8{_}776{_}But Stoddard was not of the blood that takes opinions second-hand.
10068-8{_}777{_}Upon his mother's side he was the grandson of one of the great anti-slavery agitators.
10068-8{_}778{_}The sister of this man, Gray's great-aunt, had stood beside him on the platform when there was danger in it; and after the Negro was freed and enfranchised, she had devoted a long life to the cause of woman suffrage.
10068-8{_}779{_}The mother who bore him died young.
10068-8{_}780{_}She left him to the care of a conservative father, but the blood that came through her did not make for conservatism.
10068-8{_}781{_}Perhaps it was some admixture of his father's traits which set the young man to investigating the cotton-mill situation in his own fashion.
10068-8{_}782{_}To do this as he conceived it should be done, he had hired himself to the Hardwick Spinning Company in an office position which gave him a fair outlook on the business, and put him in complete touch with the practical side of it; yet the facts of the case made the situation evident to those under him as well as his peers.
10068-8{_}783{_}Whatever convictions and opinions he was maturing in this year with the Hardwicks, he kept to himself; but he was supposed to hold some socialistic ideas, and Lydia Sessions, James Hardwick's sister-in-law, made her devoir to these by engaging zealously in semi-charitable enterprises among the mill-girls.
10068-8{_}784{_}He was a passionate individualist.
10068-8{_}785{_}The word seems unduly fiery when one remembers the smiling, insouciant manner of his divergences from the conventional type; yet he was inveterately himself, and not some schoolmaster's or tailor's or barber's version of Gray Stoddard; and in this, though Johnnie did not know it, lay the strength of his charm for her.
10068-8{_}786{_}The moments passed unheeded after he came into her field of vision, and she watched him for some time, busy at his morning's work.
10068-8{_}787{_}It took her breath when he raised his eyes suddenly and their glances encountered.
10068-8{_}788{_}He plainly recognized her at once, and nodded a cheerful greeting.
10068-8{_}789{_}After a while he got up and came out into the hall, his hands full of papers, evidently on his way to one of the other offices.
10068-8{_}790{_}He paused beside the bench and spoke to her.
10068-8{_}791{_}"Waiting for the room boss?
10068-8{_}792{_}Are they going to put you on this morning?"
10068-8{_}793{_}he asked pleasantly.
10068-8{_}794{_}"Yes, I'm a-going to get a chance to work right away," she smiled up at him.
10068-8{_}795{_}"Ain't it fine?"
10068-8{_}796{_}The smile that answered hers held something pitying, yet it was a pity that did not hurt or offend.
10068-8{_}797{_}"Yes--I'm sure it's fine, if you think so," said Stoddard, half reluctantly.
10068-8{_}798{_}Then his eye caught the broken pink blossom which Johnnie had pinned to the front of her bodice.
10068-8{_}799{_}"What's that?"
10068-8{_}800{_}he asked.
10068-8{_}801{_}"It looks like an orchid."
10068-8{_}802{_}He was instantly apologetic for the word; but Johnnie detached the flower from her dress and held it toward him.
10068-8{_}803{_}"It is," she assented.
10068-8{_}804{_}"It's an orchid; and the little yellow flower that we-all call the whippoorwill shoe is an orchid, too."
10068-8{_}805{_}Stoddard thrust his papers into his coat pocket and took the blossom in his hand.
10068-8{_}806{_}"That's the pink moccasin flower," Johnnie told him.
10068-8{_}807{_}"They don't bloom in the valley at all, and they're not very plenty in the mountains.
10068-8{_}808{_}I picked this one six miles up on White Oak Ridge yesterday.
10068-8{_}809{_}I reckon I haven't seen more than a dozen of these in my life, and I've hunted flowers all over Unaka."
10068-8{_}810{_}"I never had the chance to analyze one," observed Stoddard.
10068-8{_}811{_}"I'd like to get hold of a good specimen.
10068-8{_}812{_}"I'm sorry this one's broken," Johnnie deprecated.
10068-8{_}813{_}Then her clouded face cleared suddenly with its luminous smile.
10068-8{_}814{_}"If it hadn't been for you I reckon it would have been knocked over the edge of the road," she added.
10068-8{_}815{_}"That's the flower I had in my handkerchief yesterday evening."
10068-8{_}816{_}Stoddard continued to examine the pink blossom with interest.
10068-8{_}817{_}"You said it grew up in the mountains--and didn't grow in the valley," he reminded her.
10068-8{_}818{_}She nodded.
10068-8{_}819{_}"Of course I'm not certain about that," and while she spoke he transferred his attention from the flower to the girl.
10068-8{_}820{_}"I really know mighty little about such things, and I've not been in the valley to exceed ten times in my life.
10068-8{_}821{_}Miss Baird, that taught the school I went to over at Rainy Gap, had a herbarium, and put all kinds of pressed flowers in it.
10068-8{_}822{_}I gathered a great many for her, and she taught me to analyze them--like you were speaking of--but I never did love to do that.
10068-8{_}823{_}It seemed like naming over and calling out the ways of your friends, to pull the flower all to pieces and press it and paste it in a book and write down all its--its--ways and faults."
10068-8{_}824{_}Again she smiled up at him radiantly, and the young man's astonished glance went from her dusty, cowhide shoes to the thick roll of fair hair on her graceful head.
10068-8{_}825{_}What manner of mill-girls did the mountains send down to the valley?
10068-8{_}826{_}"But I--" began Stoddard deprecatingly, when Johnnie reddened and broke in hastily.
10068-8{_}827{_}"Oh, I don't mean that for you.
10068-8{_}828{_}Miss Baird taught me for three years, and I loved her as dearly as I ever could any one.
10068-8{_}829{_}You may keep this flower if you want to; and, come Sunday, I'll get you another one that won't be broken."
10068-8{_}830{_}"Why Sunday?"
10068-8{_}831{_}asked Stoddard.
10068-8{_}832{_}"Well, I wouldn't have time to go after them till then, and the ones I know of wouldn't be open before Sunday.
10068-8{_}833{_}I saw just three there by the spring.
10068-8{_}834{_}That's the way they grow, you know--two or three in a place, and not another for miles."
10068-8{_}835{_}"You saw them growing?"
10068-8{_}836{_}repeated Stoddard.
10068-8{_}837{_}"I should like to see one on its roots, and maybe make a little sketch of it.
10068-8{_}838{_}Couldn't you just as well show me the place Sunday?"
10068-8{_}839{_}For no reason that she could assign, and very much against her will, Johnnie's face flushed deeply.
10068-8{_}840{_}"I reckon I couldn't," she answered evasively.
10068-8{_}841{_}"Hit's a long ways up--and--hit's a long ways up."
10068-8{_}842{_}"And yet you're going to walk it--after a week's work here in the mill?"
10068-8{_}843{_}persisted Stoddard.
10068-8{_}844{_}"You'd better tell me where they grow, and let me go up in my car."
10068-8{_}845{_}"I wish't I could," said Johnnie, embarrassed.
10068-8{_}846{_}"But you'd never find it in the world.
10068-8{_}847{_}They isn't one thing that I could tell you to know the place by: and you have to leave the road and walk a little piece--oh, it's no use--and I don't mind, I'd just love to go up there and get the flowers for you."
10068-8{_}848{_}"Are you the new girl?"
10068-8{_}849{_}inquired a voice at Johnnie's shoulder.
10068-8{_}850{_}They turned to find a squat, middle-aged man regarding them dubiously.
10068-8{_}851{_}"Yes," answered Johnnie, rising.
10068-8{_}852{_}"I've been waiting quite a while."
10068-8{_}853{_}"Well, come this way," directed the man and, turning, led her away.
10068-8{_}854{_}Down the hall they went, then up a flight of wooden stairs which carried them to a covered bridge, and so to the upper story of the factory.
10068-8{_}855{_}"That's an unusual-looking girl."
10068-8{_}856{_}Old Andrew MacPherson made the comment as he received the papers from Stoddard's hands.
10068-8{_}857{_}"The one I was speaking to in the hall?"
10068-8{_}858{_}inquired Stoddard rather unnecessarily.
10068-8{_}859{_}"Yes; she seems to have an unusual mind as well.
10068-8{_}860{_}These mountain people are peculiar.
10068-8{_}861{_}They appear to have no idea of class, and therefore are in a measure all aristocrats."
10068-8{_}862{_}"Well, that ought to square with your socialistic notions," chaffed MacPherson, sorting the work on his desk and pushing a certain portion of it toward Stoddard.
10068-8{_}863{_}"Sit down here, if you please, and we'll go over these now.
10068-8{_}864{_}The girl looked a good deal like a fairy princess.
10068-8{_}865{_}I don't think she's a safe topic for susceptible young chaps like you and me," the grizzled old Scotchman concluded with a chuckle.
10068-8{_}866{_}"Your socialistic hullabaloo makes you liable to foregather with all sorts of impossible people."
10068-8{_}867{_}Gray shook his head, laughing, as he seated himself at the desk beside the other.
10068-8{_}868{_}"Oh, I'm only a theoretical socialist," he deprecated.
10068-8{_}869{_}"Hum," grunted the older man.
10068-8{_}870{_}"A theoretical socialist always seemed to me about like a theoretical pickpocket--neither of them stands to do much harm.
10068-8{_}871{_}For example, here you are, one of the richest young fellows of my acquaintance, living along very contentedly where every tenet you profess to hold is daily outraged.
10068-8{_}872{_}You're not giving away your money.
10068-8{_}873{_}You take a healthy interest in a good car, a good dinner, the gals; I'm even told you have a fad for old porcelains--and yet you call yourself a socialist."
10068-8{_}874{_}"These economic conditions are not a pin," answered Gray, smiling.
10068-8{_}875{_}"I don't have to jump and say 'ouch!'
10068-8{_}876{_}the minute I find they prick me.
10068-8{_}877{_}Worse conditions have always been, and no doubt bad ones will survive for a time, and pass away as mankind outgrows them.
10068-8{_}878{_}I haven't the colossal conceit to suppose that I can reform the world--not even push it much faster toward the destination of good to which it is rolling.
10068-8{_}879{_}But I want to know--I want to understand, myself; then if there is anything for me to do I shall do it.
10068-8{_}880{_}It may be that the present conditions are the best possible for the present moment.
10068-8{_}881{_}It may be that if a lot of us got together and agreed, we could better them exceedingly.
10068-8{_}882{_}It is not certain in my mind yet that any growth is of value to humanity which does not proceed from within.
10068-8{_}883{_}This is true of the individual--must it not be true of the class?"
10068-8{_}884{_}"No doubt, no doubt," agreed MacPherson, indifferently.
10068-8{_}885{_}"Most of the men who are loud in the leadership of socialism have made a failure of their own lives.
10068-8{_}886{_}We'll see what happens when a man who is a personal and economic success sets up to teach."
10068-8{_}887{_}"If you mean that very complimentary description for me," said Gray with sudden seriousness, "I will say to you here and now that there is no preacher in me.
10068-8{_}888{_}But when I am a little clearer in my own mind as to what I believe, I shall practise.
10068-8{_}889{_}The only real creed is a manner of life.
10068-8{_}890{_}If you don't live it, you don't really believe it."
10068-8{_}891{_}CHAPTER VI  WEAVERS AND WEFT  The Hardwick mill was a large one; to the mountain-bred girl it seemed endless, while its clamour and roar was a thing to daunt.
10068-8{_}892{_}They passed through the spinning department, in which the long lines of frames were tended by children, and reached the weaving-rooms whose looms required the attention of women, with here and there a man who had failed to make a success of male occupations and sunk to the ill-paid feminine activities.
10068-8{_}893{_}In a corner of one of these, Johnnie's guide stopped before two silent, motionless looms, and threw on the power.
10068-8{_}894{_}He began to instruct her in their operation, all communication being in dumb show; for the clapping thunder of the weaving-room instantly snatches the sound from one's lips and batters it into shapelessness.
10068-8{_}895{_}Johnnie had been an expert weaver on the ancient foot-power looms of the mountains; but the strangeness of the new machine, the noise and her surroundings, bewildered her.
10068-8{_}896{_}When the man saw that she was not likely to injure herself or the looms, he turned away with a careless nod and left her to her fate.
10068-8{_}897{_}It was a blowy April day outside, with a gay blue sky in which the white clouds raced, drawing barges of shadow over the earth below.
10068-8{_}898{_}But the necessity of keeping dust out of the machinery, the inconvenience of having flying ends carried toward it, closed every window in the big factory, and the operatives gasped in the early heat, the odour of oil, the exhausted air.
10068-8{_}899{_}There was a ventilating system in the Hardwick mill, and it was supposed to be exceptionally free from lint; but the fagged children crowded to the casements with instinctive longing for the outdoor air which could not of course enter through the glass; or plodded their monotonous rounds to tend the frames and see that the thread was running properly to each spool, and that the spools were removed, when filled.
10068-8{_}900{_}By noon every nerve in Johnnie's body quivered with excitement and overstrain; yet when Mandy came for her at the dinner hour she showed her a face still resolute, and asked that a snack be brought her to the mill.
10068-8{_}901{_}"I don't see why you won't come along home and eat your dinner," the Meacham woman commented.
10068-8{_}902{_}"The Lord knows you get time enough to stay in the mill working over them old looms.
10068-8{_}903{_}Say, I seen you in the hall--did you know who you was talking to?"
10068-8{_}904{_}The red flooded Johnnie's face as she knelt before her loom interrogating its workings with a dexterous hand; even the white nape of her neck showed pink to Mandy's examining eye; but she managed to reply in a fairly even tone:  "Yes, that was Mr. Stoddard.
10068-8{_}905{_}I saw him yesterday evening when I was coming down the Ridge with Shade."
10068-8{_}906{_}"But did you know 'bout him?
10068-8{_}907{_}Say--Johnnie Consadine--turn yourself round from that old loom and answer me, I was goin' a-past the door, and when I ketched sight o' you and him settin' there talkin' as if you'd knowed each other all your lives, why you could have--could have knocked me down with a feather."
10068-8{_}908{_}Johnnie sat up on her heels and turned a laughing face across her shoulder.
10068-8{_}909{_}"I don't see any reason to want to knock you down with anything," she evaded the direct issue.
10068-8{_}910{_}"Go 'long, Mandy, or you won't have time to eat your dinner.
10068-8{_}911{_}Tell Aunt Mavity to send me just a biscuit and a piece of meat."
10068-8{_}912{_}"Good land, Johnnie Consadine, but you're quare!"
10068-8{_}913{_}exclaimed Mandy, staring with bulging light eyes.
10068-8{_}914{_}"If it was me I'd be all in a tremble yet--and there you sit and talk about meat and bread!"
10068-8{_}915{_}Johnnie did not think it necessary to explain that the tremor of that conversation with Stoddard had indeed lasted through her entire morning.
10068-8{_}916{_}"There was nothing to tremble about," she remarked with surface calm.
10068-8{_}917{_}"He'd never seen a pink moccasin flower, and I gave him the one I had and told him where it grew."
10068-8{_}918{_}"Well, he wasn't looking at no moccasin flower when I seed him," Mandy persisted.
10068-8{_}919{_}"He was lookin' at you.
10068-8{_}920{_}He jest eyed you as if you was Miss Lydia Sessions herself--more so, if anything."
10068-8{_}921{_}Johnnie inwardly rebuked the throb of joy which greeted this statement.
10068-8{_}922{_}"I reckon his looks are his own, Mandy," she said soberly.
10068-8{_}923{_}"You and me have no call to notice them."
10068-8{_}924{_}"Ain't got no call to notice 'em?
10068-8{_}925{_}Well, I jest wish't I could get you and him up in front of Miss Sessions, and have her see them looks of his'n," grumbled Mandy as she turned away.
10068-8{_}926{_}"I bet you there'd be some noticin' done then!"
10068-8{_}927{_}When in the evening Mandy came for Johnnie, she found the new mill hand white about the mouth with exhaustion, heavy-eyed, choking, and ready to weep.
10068-8{_}928{_}"Uh-huh," said the Meacham woman, "I know just how you feel.
10068-8{_}929{_}They all look that-a-way the first day or two--then after that they look worse."
10068-8{_}930{_}Nervelessly Johnnie found her way downstairs in the stream of tired girls and women.
10068-8{_}931{_}There was more than one kindly greeting for the new hand, and occasionally somebody clapped her on the shoulder and assured her that a few days more would get her used to the work.
10068-8{_}932{_}The mill yard was large, filled with grass-plots and gravel walks; but it was shut in by a boarding so tall that the street could not be seen from the windows of the lower floor.
10068-8{_}933{_}To Johnnie, weary to the point where aching muscles and blood charged with uneliminated waste spelled pessimism, that high board fence seemed to make of the pretty place a prison yard.
10068-8{_}934{_}A man was propping open the big wooden gates, and through them she saw the street, the sidewalk, and a carriage drawn up at the curb.
10068-8{_}935{_}In this vehicle sat a lady; and a gentleman, hat in hand, talked to her from the sidewalk.
10068-8{_}936{_}"Come on," hissed Mandy, seizing her companion's arm and dragging her forward.
10068-8{_}937{_}"Thar's Miss Lydia Sessions right now, and that's Mr. Stoddard a-talkin' to her.
10068-8{_}938{_}I'll go straight up and give you a knockdown--I want to, anyway.
10068-8{_}939{_}She's the one that runs the Uplift Club.
10068-8{_}940{_}If she takes a shine to you it'll be money in your pocket."
10068-8{_}941{_}She turned over her shoulder to glance at Johnnie, who was pulling vigorously back.
10068-8{_}942{_}There was no hint of tiredness or depression in the girl's face now.
10068-8{_}943{_}Her deep eyes glowed; red was again in the fresh lips that parted over the white teeth in an adorable, tremulous smile.
10068-8{_}944{_}Mandy stared.
10068-8{_}945{_}"Hurry up--he'll be gittin' away," she admonished.
10068-8{_}946{_}"Oh, no," objected the new girl.
10068-8{_}947{_}"Wait till some other time, I--I don't want to--"  But her remonstrance came too late; Mandy had yanked her forward and was performing the introduction she so euphoniously described.
10068-8{_}948{_}Gray Stoddard turned and bowed to both girls.
10068-8{_}949{_}He carried the broken orchid in his hand, and apparently had been speaking of it to Miss Sessions.
10068-8{_}950{_}Mandy eyed him narrowly to see if any of the looks she had apprehended as offensive to Miss Sessions went in Johnnie's direction.
10068-8{_}951{_}And she was not disappointed.
10068-8{_}952{_}Stoddard's gaze lingered long on the radiant countenance of the girl from Unaka.
10068-8{_}953{_}Not so the young women looked after a few months of factory life.
10068-8{_}954{_}He was getting to know well the odd jail-bleach the cotton mill puts on country cheeks, the curious, dulled, yet resentful expression of the eyes, begotten by continuous repetition of excessive hours of trivial, monotonous toil.
10068-8{_}955{_}Would this girl come at last to that favour?
10068-8{_}956{_}He was a little surprised at the strength of protest in his own heart.
10068-8{_}957{_}Then MacPherson, coming down the office steps, called to him; and, with courteous adieux, the two men departed in company.
10068-8{_}958{_}Johnnie was a bit grieved to find that the removal from Miss Sessions of the shrouding, misty veil revealed a countenance somewhat angular in outline, with cheekbones a trifle hard and high, and a lack of colour.
10068-8{_}959{_}She fancied, too, that Miss Sessions was slightly annoyed about something.
10068-8{_}960{_}She wondered if it was because they had interrupted her conversation with Mr. Stoddard and driven him away.
10068-8{_}961{_}Yet while she so questioned, she was taking in with swift appreciation the trim set of the driving coat Miss Lydia wore, the appropriate texture of the heavy gloves on the small hands that held the lines, and a certain indefinable air of elegance hard to put into words, but which all women recognize.
10068-8{_}962{_}"Ain't she swell?"
10068-8{_}963{_}inquired Mandy, as they passed on.
10068-8{_}964{_}"She's after Mr. Stoddard now--it used to be the preacher that had the big church in Watauga, but he moved away.
10068-8{_}965{_}I wish I had her clothes."
10068-8{_}966{_}"Yes," returned Johnnie absently.
10068-8{_}967{_}She had already forgotten her impression of Miss Sessions's displeasure.
10068-8{_}968{_}Gone was the leaden weariness of her day's toil Something intimate and kind in the glance Stoddard had given her remained warm at her heart, and set that heart singing.
10068-8{_}969{_}Meantime, Stoddard and MacPherson were walking up the ridge toward the Country Club together, intending to spend the night on the highlands.
10068-8{_}970{_}The Scotchman returned once more to the subject he had broached that morning.
10068-8{_}971{_}"This is a great country," he opened obliquely, "a very great country.
10068-8{_}972{_}But you Americans will have to learn that generations of blood and breeding are not to be skipped with impunity.
10068-8{_}973{_}See the sons and daughters of your rich men.
10068-8{_}974{_}If the hope of the land lay in them it would be a bad outlook indeed."
10068-8{_}975{_}"Is that peculiar to America?"
10068-8{_}976{_}asked Stoddard mildly.
10068-8{_}977{_}They were coming under the trees now.
10068-8{_}978{_}He took off his hat and ran his fingers through his hair to enjoy the coolness.
10068-8{_}979{_}"My impression was that the youthful aristocracy of every country often made of itself a spectacle unseemly."
10068-8{_}980{_}The Scotchman laughed.
10068-8{_}981{_}Then he looked sidewise at his companion.
10068-8{_}982{_}"I'm not denying," he pursued, again with that odd trick of entering his argument from the side, "that a young chap like yourself has my good word.
10068-8{_}983{_}A man with money who will go to work to find out how that money was made, and to live as his father did, carries an old head on young shoulders.
10068-8{_}984{_}I put aside your socialistic vapourings of course--every fellow to his fad--I see in you the makings of a canny business man."
10068-8{_}985{_}It was Stoddard's turn to laugh, and he did so unrestrainedly, throwing back his head and uttering his mirth so boyishly that the other smiled in sympathy.
10068-8{_}986{_}"You talk about what's in the blood," Gray said finally, "and then you make light of my socialistic vapourings, as you call them.
10068-8{_}987{_}My mother's clan--and it is from the spindle side that a man gets his traits--are all come-outers as far back as I know anything about them.
10068-8{_}988{_}They fought with Cromwell--some of them; they came over and robbed the Indians in true sanctimonious fashion, and persecuted the Quakers; and down the line a bit I get some Quaker blood that stood for its beliefs in the stocks, and sacrificed its ears for what it thought right.
10068-8{_}989{_}I'm afraid the socialistic vapourings are the true expression of the animal."
10068-8{_}990{_}MacPherson grunted incredulously.
10068-8{_}991{_}"I give you ten years to be done with it," he said.
10068-8{_}992{_}"It is a disease of youth.
10068-8{_}993{_}But don't let it mark your affairs.
10068-8{_}994{_}It is all right to foregather with these workingmen, and find out about their trades-unions and that sort of thing--such knowledge will be useful to you in your business.
10068-8{_}995{_}But when it comes to women"--MacPherson paused and shook his gray head--"to young, pretty women--a man must stick to his own class."
10068-8{_}996{_}"You mean the girl in the corridor," said Stoddard with that directness which his friends were apt to find disconcerting.
10068-8{_}997{_}"I haven't classified her yet.
10068-8{_}998{_}She's rather an extraordinary specimen."
10068-8{_}999{_}"Well, she's not in your class, and best leave her alone," returned MacPherson doggedly.
10068-8{_}1000{_}"It wouldn't matter if the young thing were not so beautiful, and with such a winning look in her eyes.
10068-8{_}1001{_}This America beats me.
10068-8{_}1002{_}That poor lass would make a model princess--according to common ideals of royalty--and here you find her coming out of some hut in the mountains and going to work in a factory.
10068-8{_}1003{_}Miss Lydia Sessions is a well-bred young woman, now; she's been all over Europe, and profited by her advantages of travel.
10068-8{_}1004{_}I call her an exceedingly well-bred person."
10068-8{_}1005{_}"She is," agreed Stoddard without enthusiasm.
10068-8{_}1006{_}"And I'm sure you must admire her altruistic ideas--they'd just fall in with yours, I suppose, now."
10068-8{_}1007{_}Stoddard shook his head.
10068-8{_}1008{_}"Not at all," he said briefly.
10068-8{_}1009{_}"If you were enough interested in socialism to know what we folks are driving at, I could explain to you why we object to charitable enterprises--but it's not worth while."
10068-8{_}1010{_}"Indeed it is not," assented MacPherson hastily.
10068-8{_}1011{_}"Though no doubt we might have a fine argument over it some evening when we have nothing better to talk about.
10068-8{_}1012{_}I thought you and Miss Sessions were fixing up a match of it, and it struck me as a very good thing, too.
10068-8{_}1013{_}The holdings of both of you are in cotton-mill property, I judge.
10068-8{_}1014{_}That always makes for harmony and stability in a matrimonial alliance."
10068-8{_}1015{_}Stoddard smiled.
10068-8{_}1016{_}He was aware that Miss Lydia's holdings consisted of a complaisant brother-in-law in whose house she was welcome till she could marry.
10068-8{_}1017{_}But he said nothing on this head.
10068-8{_}1018{_}"MacPherson," he began very seriously, "I wonder a little at you, I know you old-world people regard these things differently; but could you look at Mrs. Hardwick's children, and seriously recommend Mrs. Hardwick's sister as a wife for a friend?"
10068-8{_}1019{_}Old MacPherson stopped in the way, thrust his hands deep in his pockets and stared at the younger man.
10068-8{_}1020{_}"Well!"
10068-8{_}1021{_}he ejaculated at last; "that's a great speech for a hot-headed young fellow!
10068-8{_}1022{_}Your foresight is worthy of a Scotchman."
10068-8{_}1023{_}Gray Stoddard smiled.
10068-8{_}1024{_}"I am not a hot-headed person," he observed.
10068-8{_}1025{_}"Nobody but you ever accused me of such a thing.
10068-8{_}1026{_}Marriage concerns the race and a man's whole future.
10068-8{_}1027{_}If the children of the marriage are likely to be unsatisfactory, the marriage will certainly be so.
10068-8{_}1028{_}We moderns bedeck and bedrape us in all sorts of meretricious togas, till a pair of fine eyes and a dashing manner pass for beauty; but when life tries the metal--when nature applies her inevitable test--the degenerate or neurotic type goes to the wall."
10068-8{_}1029{_}Again MacPherson grunted.
10068-8{_}1030{_}"No doubt you're sound enough; but it is rather uncanny to hear a young fellow talk like his grandfather," the Scotchman said finally.
10068-8{_}1031{_}"Are there many of your sort in this astonishing land?"
10068-8{_}1032{_}"A good many," Stoddard told him.
10068-8{_}1033{_}"The modern young man of education and wealth is doing one of two things--burning up his money and going to the dogs as fast as he can; or putting in a power of thinking, and trying, while he saves his own soul, to do his part in the regeneration of the world."
10068-8{_}1034{_}"Yes.
10068-8{_}1035{_}Well, it's a big job.
10068-8{_}1036{_}It's been on hand a long time.
10068-8{_}1037{_}The young men of America have their work cut out for them," said MacPherson drily.
10068-8{_}1038{_}"No doubt," returned Stoddard with undisturbed cheerfulness.
10068-8{_}1039{_}"But when every man saves his own soul, the salvation of the world will come to pass."
10068-8{_}1040{_}CHAPTER VII  ABOVE THE VALLEY  All week in Johnnie the white flame of purpose burned out every consciousness of weariness, of bodily or mental distaste.
10068-8{_}1041{_}The preposterously long hours, the ill-ventilated rooms, the savage monotony of her toil, none of these reached the girl through the glow of hope and ambition.
10068-8{_}1042{_}Physically, the finger of the factory was already laid upon her vigorous young frame; but when Sunday morning came, though there was no bellowing whistle to break in on her slumbers, she waked early, and while nerve and muscle begged achingly for more sleep, she rose with a sense of exhilaration which nothing could dampen.
10068-8{_}1043{_}She had seen a small mountain church over the Ridge by the spring where her moccasin flowers grew; and if there were preaching in it to-day, the boys and girls scouring the surrounding woods during the intermissions would surely find and carry away the orchids.
10068-8{_}1044{_}There was no safety but to take the road early.
10068-8{_}1045{_}The room was dark.
10068-8{_}1046{_}Mandy slept noisily beside her.
10068-8{_}1047{_}All the beds were full, because the night-turn workers were in.
10068-8{_}1048{_}She meant to be very careful to waken nobody.
10068-8{_}1049{_}Poor souls, they needed this one day of rest when they could all lie late.
10068-8{_}1050{_}Searching for something, she cautiously struck a match, and in the flaring up of its small flame got a glimpse of Mandy's face, open-mouthed, pallid, unbeautiful, against the tumbled pillow.
10068-8{_}1051{_}A great rush of pity filled her eyes with tears, but then she was in a mood to compassionate any creature who had not the prospect of a twelve-mile walk to get a flower for Gray Stoddard.
10068-8{_}1052{_}It was in that black hour before dawn that Johnnie let herself out the front door, finding the direction by instinct rather than any assistance from sight, since fences, trees, houses, were but vague blots of deeper shadow in the black.
10068-8{_}1053{_}She was well on her way before a light here and there in a cabin window showed that, Sunday morning as it was, the earliest risers were beginning to stir.
10068-8{_}1054{_}Her face was set to the east, and after a time a pallid line showed itself above the great bulk of mountains which in this quarter backed up the ramparts of the circling ridges about Watauga.
10068-8{_}1055{_}The furthest line was big Unaka, but this passionate lover of her native highlands gave it neither thought nor glance, as she tramped steadily with lifted face, following unconsciously the beckoning finger of Fate.
10068-8{_}1056{_}It was a dripping-sweet spring morning, dew-drenched, and with the air so full of moisture that it gathered and pattered from the scant leafage.
10068-8{_}1057{_}She was two miles up, swinging along at that steady pace her mountain-bred youth had given her, when the sky began to flush faintly, and the first hint of dawn rested on her upraised countenance.
10068-8{_}1058{_}Rain-laden mists swept down upon her from the heights, and she walked through them unnoting; the pale light from the eastern sky shone on an aspect introverted, rapt away from knowledge of its surroundings.
10068-8{_}1059{_}She was going to get something for him.
10068-8{_}1060{_}She had promised him the flowers, and he would be pleased with them.
10068-8{_}1061{_}He would smile when he thanked her for them, and look at her as he had when she gave him the broken blossom.
10068-8{_}1062{_}A look like that was to the girl in her present mood as the sword's touch on the shoulder of the lad who is being knighted by his king--it made her want to rise up and be all that such a man could ever demand of her.
10068-8{_}1063{_}Twelve miles of walking after a week's toil in the mill was a very small offering to put before so worshipful a divinity.
10068-8{_}1064{_}She sought vaguely to conjecture just what his words would be when next they spoke together.
10068-8{_}1065{_}Her lips formed themselves into tender, reminiscent half-smiles as she went over the few and brief moments of her three interviews with Stoddard.
10068-8{_}1066{_}Johnnie was not inexperienced in matters of the heart.
10068-8{_}1067{_}Mating time comes early in the mountains.
10068-8{_}1068{_}Had her dreams been of Shade Buckheath, or any of the boys of her own kind and class, she would have been instantly full of self-consciousness; but Gray Stoddard appeared to her a creature so apart from her sphere that this overwhelming attraction he held for her seemed no more than the admiration she might have given to Miss Lydia Sessions.
10068-8{_}1069{_}And so the dream lay undisturbed under her eyelashes, and she breasted the slope of the big mountain with a buoyant step, oblivious of fatigue.
10068-8{_}1070{_}She reached the little wayside spring before even the early-rising mountain folk were abroad, found three pink blossoms in full perfection, plucked them and wrapped them carefully in damp cloths disposed in a little hickory basket that Uncle Pros had made for her years ago.
10068-8{_}1071{_}It was a tiny thing, designed to hold a child's play-pretties or a young girl's sewing, but shaped and fashioned after the manner of mountain baskets, and woven of stout white hickory withes shaved down to daintier size and pliancy by the old man's jack-knife.
10068-8{_}1072{_}Life was very sweet to Johnnie Consadine as she straightened up, basket in hand, and turned toward the home journey.
10068-8{_}1073{_}It was nearly nine o'clock when she reached the gap above Cottonville.
10068-8{_}1074{_}She was singing a little, softly, to herself, as she footed it down the road, and wishing that she might see Gray's face when he got her flowers.
10068-8{_}1075{_}She planned to put them in a glass on his desk Monday morning, and of course she would be at her loom long before he should reach the office.
10068-8{_}1076{_}She was glad they were such fine specimens--all perfect.
10068-8{_}1077{_}Lovingly she pulled aside the wet cloth and looked in at them.
10068-8{_}1078{_}She began to meet people on the road, and the cabins she passed were open and thronged with morning life.
10068-8{_}1079{_}The next turn in the road would bring her to the spring where she had rested that evening just a week ago, and where Shade had met her.
10068-8{_}1080{_}Suddenly, she caught the sheen of something down the road between the scant greenery.
10068-8{_}1081{_}It was a carriage or an automobile.
10068-8{_}1082{_}Now, it was more likely to be the former than the latter; also, there were a half-dozen cars in Cottonville; yet from the first she knew, and was prepared for it when the shining vehicle came nearer and showed her Gray Stoddard driving it.
10068-8{_}1083{_}They looked at each other in silence.
10068-8{_}1084{_}Stoddard brought the machine to a halt beside her.
10068-8{_}1085{_}She came mutely forward, a hesitating hand at her basket covering, her eyes raised to his.
10068-8{_}1086{_}With the mountaineer's deathless instinct for greeting, she was first to speak.
10068-8{_}1087{_}"Howdy," she breathed softly.
10068-8{_}1088{_}"I--I was looking for--I got you--"  She fell silent again, still regarding him, and fumbling blindly at the cover of the basket.
10068-8{_}1089{_}"Well--aren't you lost?"
10068-8{_}1090{_}inquired Stoddard with a rather futile assumption of surprise.
10068-8{_}1091{_}He was strangely moved by the direct gaze of those clear, wide-set gray eyes, under the white brow and the ruffled coronet of bright hair.
10068-8{_}1092{_}"No," returned Johnnie gently, literally.
10068-8{_}1093{_}"You know I said I'd come up here and get those moccasin flowers for you this morning.
10068-8{_}1094{_}This is my road home, anyhow.
10068-8{_}1095{_}I'm not as near lost on it as I am at a loom, down in the factory."
10068-8{_}1096{_}Stoddard continued to stare at the hand she had laid on the car.
10068-8{_}1097{_}"It'll be an awfully long walk for you," he said at last, choosing his words with some difficulty.
10068-8{_}1098{_}"Won't you get in and let me take you up to the spring?"
10068-8{_}1099{_}Johnnie laughed softly, exultantly.
10068-8{_}1100{_}"Oh, I picked your flowers before day broke.
10068-8{_}1101{_}I'll bet there have been a dozen boys over from Sunday-school to drink out of that spring before this time.
10068-8{_}1102{_}You wouldn't have had any blooms if I hadn't got up early."
10068-8{_}1103{_}Again she laughed, and, uncovering the orchids, held them up to him.
10068-8{_}1104{_}"These are beauties," he exclaimed with due enthusiasm, yet with a certain uneasy preoccupation in his manner.
10068-8{_}1105{_}"Were you up before day, did you tell me, to get these?
10068-8{_}1106{_}That seems too bad.
10068-8{_}1107{_}You needed your sleep."
10068-8{_}1108{_}Johnnie flushed and smiled.
10068-8{_}1109{_}"I love to do it," she said simply.
10068-8{_}1110{_}"It was mighty sweet out on the road this morning, and you don't know how pretty the blooms did look, standing there waiting for me.
10068-8{_}1111{_}I 'most hated to pick them."
10068-8{_}1112{_}Stoddard's troubled eyes raised themselves to her face.
10068-8{_}1113{_}Here was a royal nature that would always be in the attitude of the giver.
10068-8{_}1114{_}He wanted to offer her something, and, as the nearest thing in reach, sprang down from the automobile and, laying a hand on her arm, said, almost brusquely:  "Get in.
10068-8{_}1115{_}Come, let me help you.
10068-8{_}1116{_}I want to go up and see the spring where these grow.
10068-8{_}1117{_}I'll get you back to Cottonville in time for church, if that's what you're debating about."
10068-8{_}1118{_}Both of them knew that Johnnie's reluctance had nothing to do with the question of church-time.
10068-8{_}1119{_}Stoddard himself was well aware that a factory girl could not with propriety accept a seat in his car; yet when once they were settled side by side, and the car resumed that swift, tireless climb which is the wonder and delight of the mechanical vehicle, it was characteristic that both put aside definitely and completely all hesitations and doubts.
10068-8{_}1120{_}The girl was freely, innocently, exultantly blissful.
10068-8{_}1121{_}Stoddard noticed her intent examination of the machine, and began explaining its workings to her.
10068-8{_}1122{_}"Was that what you were doing," she asked, alluding to some small item of the operating, "when you stopped by the side of the road, Sunday night, when Miss Lydia was with you?"
10068-8{_}1123{_}He looked his astonishment.
10068-8{_}1124{_}"You were right under my window when you stopped," Johnnie explained to him.
10068-8{_}1125{_}"I watched you-all when you started away.
10068-8{_}1126{_}I was sure you would beat."
10068-8{_}1127{_}"We did," Stoddard assured her.
10068-8{_}1128{_}"But we came near missing it.
10068-8{_}1129{_}That connection Buckheath put in for me the evening you were with him on the Ridge worked loose.
10068-8{_}1130{_}But I discovered the trouble in time to fix it."
10068-8{_}1131{_}Remembrance of that evening, and of the swift flight of the motors through the dusk moonlight, made Johnnie wonder at herself and her present position.
10068-8{_}1132{_}She was roused by Stoddard's voice asking:  "Are you interested in machinery?"
10068-8{_}1133{_}"I love it," returned Johnnie sincerely.
10068-8{_}1134{_}"I never did get enough of tinkerin' around machines.
10068-8{_}1135{_}If I was ever so fortunate as to own a sewing machine I could take it all apart and clean it and put it together again.
10068-8{_}1136{_}I did that to the minister's wife's sewing machine down at Bledsoe when it got out of order.
10068-8{_}1137{_}She said I knew more about it than the man that sold it to her."
10068-8{_}1138{_}"Would you like to run the car?"
10068-8{_}1139{_}came the next query.
10068-8{_}1140{_}Would she like to!
10068-8{_}1141{_}The countenance of simple rapture that she turned to him was reply sufficient.
10068-8{_}1142{_}"Well, look at my hands here on the steering-wheel.
10068-8{_}1143{_}Get the position, and when I raise one put yours in its place.
10068-8{_}1144{_}There.
10068-8{_}1145{_}No, a little more this way.
10068-8{_}1146{_}Now you can hold it better.
10068-8{_}1147{_}The other one's right."
10068-8{_}1148{_}Smilingly he watched her, like a grown person amusing a child.
10068-8{_}1149{_}"You see what the wheel does, of course--guides.
10068-8{_}1150{_}Now," when they had run ahead for some minutes, "do you want to go faster?"
10068-8{_}1151{_}Johnnie laughed up at him, through thick, fair lashes.
10068-8{_}1152{_}"Looks like anybody would be hard to suit that wanted to go faster than this," she apologized.
10068-8{_}1153{_}"But if the machine can make a higher speed, there wouldn't be any harm in just running that way for a spell, would there?"
10068-8{_}1154{_}It was Stoddard's turn to laugh.
10068-8{_}1155{_}"No manner of harm," he agreed readily.
10068-8{_}1156{_}"Well, you advance your spark and open the throttle--that speeds her up.
10068-8{_}1157{_}This is the spark and this the gas, here.
10068-8{_}1158{_}Then you shove your shifting lever--see, here it is--over to the next speed.
10068-8{_}1159{_}Remember that, any time you shift the gears, you'll have to pull the clutch.
10068-8{_}1160{_}The machine has to gain headway on one speed before it can take the next."
10068-8{_}1161{_}Johnnie nodded soberly.
10068-8{_}1162{_}Her intent gaze studied the mechanism before her intelligently.
10068-8{_}1163{_}"We're going a heap faster now," she suggested in a moment.
10068-8{_}1164{_}"Can I move that--whatever it is--over to the third speed?"
10068-8{_}1165{_}"Yes," agreed Stoddard.
10068-8{_}1166{_}"Here's a good, long, straight stretch of road for us to take it on.
10068-8{_}1167{_}I'll attend to the horn when we come to the turn up there.
10068-8{_}1168{_}We mustn't make anybody's horse run away."
10068-8{_}1169{_}So the lesson proceeded.
10068-8{_}1170{_}He showed her brake and clutch.
10068-8{_}1171{_}He gave her some theoretical knowledge of cranking up, because she seemed to enjoy it as a child enjoys exploiting the possibilities of a new toy.
10068-8{_}1172{_}Up and up they went, the sky widening and brightening above them.
10068-8{_}1173{_}Hens began to lead forth their broods.
10068-8{_}1174{_}Overhead, a hawk wheeled high in the blue, uttering his querulous cry.
10068-8{_}1175{_}"I'm mighty glad I came," the girl said, more to herself than to the man at her side.
10068-8{_}1176{_}"This is the most like flying of anything that ever chanced to me."
10068-8{_}1177{_}From time to time Stoddard had sent swift, sidelong glances at his companion, noting the bright, bent head, the purity of line in the profile above the steering-wheel, the intelligent beauty of the intent, down-dropped eyes, with long lashes almost on the flushed cheeks.
10068-8{_}1178{_}He wondered at her; born amid these wide, cool spaces, how had she endured for a week the fetid atmosphere of the factory rooms?
10068-8{_}1179{_}How, having tested it, could she look forward to a life like that?
10068-8{_}1180{_}Something in her innocent trust choked him.
10068-8{_}1181{_}He began some carefully worded inquiries as to her experience in the mill and her opinion of the work.
10068-8{_}1182{_}The answers partook of that charm which always clung about Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1183{_}She told him of Mandy and, missing no shade of the humour there was in the Meacham girl, managed to make the description pathetic.
10068-8{_}1184{_}She described Pap Himes and his boarding-house, aptly, deftly, and left it funny, though a sympathetic listener could feel the tragedy beneath.
10068-8{_}1185{_}Presently they met the first farm-wagon with its load of worshippers for the little mountain church beyond.
10068-8{_}1186{_}As these came out of a small side road, and caught sight of the car, the bony old horses jibbed and shied, and took all the driver's skill and a large portion of his vocabulary to carry them safely past, the children staring, the women pulling their sunbonnets about their faces and looking down.
10068-8{_}1187{_}Something in the sight brought home to Johnnie the incongruity of her present position.
10068-8{_}1188{_}On the instant, a drop of rain splashed upon the back of her hand.
10068-8{_}1189{_}"There!"
10068-8{_}1190{_}she cried in a contrite voice.
10068-8{_}1191{_}"I knew mighty well and good that it was going to rain, and I ought to have named it to you, because you town folks don't understand the weather as well as we do.
10068-8{_}1192{_}I ought not to have let you come on up here."
10068-8{_}1193{_}"We'll have to turn and run for it," said Stoddard, laughing a little.
10068-8{_}1194{_}"I wish I'd had the hood put on this morning," as he surveyed the narrow way in which he had to turn.
10068-8{_}1195{_}"Is it wider beyond here, do you remember?"
10068-8{_}1196{_}"There's a bluff up about a quarter of a mile that you could run under and be as dry as if you were in the shed at home," said Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1197{_}"This won't last long.
10068-8{_}1198{_}Do you want to try it?"
10068-8{_}1199{_}"You are the pilot," Stoddard declared promptly, resigning the wheel once more to her hands.
10068-8{_}1200{_}"If it's a bad place, you might let me take the car in."
10068-8{_}1201{_}Rain in the mountains has a trick of coming with the suddenness of an overturned bucket.
10068-8{_}1202{_}Johnnie sent the car ahead at what she considered a rapid pace, till Stoddard unceremoniously took the wheel from her and shoved the speed clutch over to the third speed.
10068-8{_}1203{_}"I'm mighty sorry I was so careless and didn't warn you about the rain," she declared with shining eyes, as her hair blew back and her colour rose at the rapid motion.
10068-8{_}1204{_}"But this is fine.
10068-8{_}1205{_}I believe that if I should ever be so fortunate as to own an automobile I'd want to fly like this every minute of the time I was in it."
10068-8{_}1206{_}As she spoke, they swept beneath the overhanging rocks, and a great curtain of Virginia creeper and trumpet-vine fell behind them, half screening them from the road, and from the deluge which now broke more fiercely.
10068-8{_}1207{_}For five minutes the world was blotted out in rain, with these two watching its gray swirls and listening to its insistent drumming, safe and dry in their cave.
10068-8{_}1208{_}Nothing ripens intimacy so rapidly as a common mishap.
10068-8{_}1209{_}Also, two people seem much to each other as they await alone the ceasing of the rain or the coming of the delayed boat.
10068-8{_}1210{_}"This won't last long," Johnnie repeated.
10068-8{_}1211{_}"We won't dare to start out when it first stops; but there'll come a little clearing-up shower after that, and then I think we'll have a fair day.
10068-8{_}1212{_}Don't you know the saying, 'Rain before seven, quit before eleven?'
10068-8{_}1213{_}Well, it showered twice just as day was breaking, and I had to wait under a tree till it was over."
10068-8{_}1214{_}The big drops lengthened themselves, as they came down, into tiny javelins and struck upon the rocks with a splash.
10068-8{_}1215{_}The roar and drumming in the forest made a soft, blurring undertone of sound.
10068-8{_}1216{_}The first rain lasted longer than Johnnie had counted on, and the clearing-up shower was slow in making its appearance.
10068-8{_}1217{_}The two talked with ever-growing interest.
10068-8{_}1218{_}Strangely enough Johnnie Consadine, who had no knowledge of any other life except through a few well-conned books, appreciated the values of this mountain existence with almost the detached view of an outsider.
10068-8{_}1219{_}Her knowledge of it was therefore more assorted and available, and Stoddard listened to her eagerly.
10068-8{_}1220{_}"But what made you think you'd like to work in a cotton mill?"
10068-8{_}1221{_}he asked suddenly.
10068-8{_}1222{_}"After all, weren't you maybe better off up in these mountains?"
10068-8{_}1223{_}And then and there Johnnie strove to put into exact and intelligent words what she had possessed and what she had lacked in the home of her childhood.
10068-8{_}1224{_}Unconsciously she told him more than was in the mere words.
10068-8{_}1225{_}He got the situation as to the visionary, kindly father with a turn for book learning and a liking for enterprises that appealed to his imagination.
10068-8{_}1226{_}Uncle Pros and the silver mine were always touched upon with the tender kindness Johnnie felt for the old man and his life-long quest.
10068-8{_}1227{_}But the little mother and the children--ah, it was here that the listener found Johnnie's incentive.
10068-8{_}1228{_}"Mr. Stoddard," she concluded, "there wasn't a bit of hope of schooling for the children unless I could get out and work in the factory.
10068-8{_}1229{_}I think it's a splendid chance for a girl.
10068-8{_}1230{_}I think any girl that wouldn't take such a chance would be mighty mean and poor-spirited."
10068-8{_}1231{_}Gray Stoddard revolved this conception of a chance in the world in his mind for some time.
10068-8{_}1232{_}"I did get some schooling," she told him.
10068-8{_}1233{_}"You wouldn't think it to hear me talk, because I'm careless, but I've been taught, and I can do better.
10068-8{_}1234{_}Yet if I don't see to it, how am I to know that the children will have as much even as I've had?
10068-8{_}1235{_}Mountain air is mighty pure and healthy, and the water up here is the finest you ever drank; but that's only for the body.
10068-8{_}1236{_}Of course there's beauty all about you--there was never anything more sightly than big Unaka and the ridges that run from it, and the sky, and the big woods--and all.
10068-8{_}1237{_}And yet human beings have got to have more than that.
10068-8{_}1238{_}I aim to make a chance for the children."
10068-8{_}1239{_}"Are you going to bring them down and let them work in the mills with you?"
10068-8{_}1240{_}Stoddard asked in a perfectly colourless tone.
10068-8{_}1241{_}Johnnie looked embarrassed.
10068-8{_}1242{_}Her week in the cotton mill had fixed indelibly on her mind the picture of the mill child, straggling to work in the gray dawn, sleepy, shivering, unkempt; of the young things creeping up and down the aisles between the endlessly turning spools, dully regarding the frames to see that the threads were not fouled or broken; of the tired little groups as they pressed close to the shut windows, neglecting their work to stare out into a world of blue sky and blowing airs--a world they could see but not enter, and no breath of which could come in to them.
10068-8{_}1243{_}And so she looked embarrassed.
10068-8{_}1244{_}She was afraid that memory of those tired little faces would show in her own countenance.
10068-8{_}1245{_}Her hands on the steering-wheel trembled.
10068-8{_}1246{_}She remembered that Mr. Stoddard was, as Shade had said, one of the bosses in the Hardwick mill.
10068-8{_}1247{_}It seemed too terrible to offend him.
10068-8{_}1248{_}He certainly thought no ill of having children employed; she must not seem to criticize him; she answered evasively:  "Well, of course they might do that.
10068-8{_}1249{_}I did think of it--before I went down there."
10068-8{_}1250{_}"Before you went to work in the mills yourself," supplied Stoddard, again in that colourless tone.
10068-8{_}1251{_}"Ye--yes," hesitated Johnnie; "but you mustn't get the idea that I don't love my work--because I do.
10068-8{_}1252{_}You see the children haven't had any schooling yet, and--well, I'm a great, big, stout somebody, and it looks like I'm the one to work in the mill."
10068-8{_}1253{_}She turned to him fleetingly a countenance of appeal and perplexity.
10068-8{_}1254{_}It seemed indeed anything but certain that she was one to work in the mill.
10068-8{_}1255{_}There was something almost grotesque in the idea which made Stoddard smile a little at her earnestness.
10068-8{_}1256{_}"I'd like to talk it over with you when you've been at work there longer," he found himself saying.
10068-8{_}1257{_}"You see, I'm studying mill conditions from one side, and you're studying them from the opposite--perhaps we could help each other."
10068-8{_}1258{_}"I sure will tell you what I find out," agreed Johnnie heartily.
10068-8{_}1259{_}"I reckon you'll want to know how the work seems to me at the side of such as I was used to in the mountains; but I hope you won't inquire how long it took me to learn, for I'm afraid I'm going to make a poor record.
10068-8{_}1260{_}If you was to ask me how much I was able to earn there, and how much back on Unaka, I could make a good report for the mill on that, because that's all that's the matter with the mountains--they're a beautiful place to live, but a body can't hardly earn a cent, work as they may."
10068-8{_}1261{_}Johnnie forgot herself--she was always doing that--and she talked freely and well.
10068-8{_}1262{_}It was as inevitable that she should be drawn to Gray Stoddard as that she should desire the clothing and culture Miss Lydia possessed.
10068-8{_}1263{_}For the present, one aspiration struck her as quite as innocent as the other.
10068-8{_}1264{_}Stoddard had not yet emerged from the starry constellations among which she set him, to take form as a young man, a person who might indeed return her regard.
10068-8{_}1265{_}Her emotions were in that nebulous, formative stage when but a touch would be needed to show her whither the regard tended, yet till that touch should come, she as unashamedly adored Gray as any child of five could have done.
10068-8{_}1266{_}It was not till they were well down the road to Cottonville that she realized the bald fact that she, a mill girl, was riding in an automobile with one of the mill owners.
10068-8{_}1267{_}She was casting about for some reasonable phrase in which to clothe the statement that it would be better he should stop the car and let her out; she had parted her lips to ask him to take the wheel, when they rounded a turn and came upon a company of loom-fixers from the village below.
10068-8{_}1268{_}Behind them, in a giggling group, strolled a dozen mill girls in their Sunday best.
10068-8{_}1269{_}Johnnie had sight of Mandy Meacham, fixing eyes of terrified admiration upon her; then she nodded in reply to Shade Buckheath's angry stare, and a rattle of wheels apprized her that a carriage was passing on the other side.
10068-8{_}1270{_}This vehicle contained the entire Hardwick family, with Lydia Sessions turning long to look her incredulous amazement back at them from her seat beside her brother-in-law.
10068-8{_}1271{_}It was all over in a moment.
10068-8{_}1272{_}The loom-fixers had debouched upon the long, wooden bridge which crossed the ravine to their quarters; the girls were going on, Mandy Meacham hanging back and staring; a tree finally shut out Miss Sessions's accusing countenance.
10068-8{_}1273{_}"Please stop and let me out here," said Johnnie, in a scarcely audible voice.
10068-8{_}1274{_}When Stoddard would have remonstrated, or asked why, his lips were closed by sight of her daunted, miserable face.
10068-8{_}1275{_}He knew as well as she the mad imprudence of the thing which they had done, and blamed himself roundly with it all.
10068-8{_}1276{_}"I'll not forget to bring the books we were talking of," he made haste to say.
10068-8{_}1277{_}He picked up the little basket from the floor of the car.
10068-8{_}1278{_}"You'd better keep the flowers in that," Johnnie told him lifelessly.
10068-8{_}1279{_}Her innocent dream was broken into by a cruel reality.
10068-8{_}1280{_}She was struggling blindly under the weight of all her little world's disapprobation.
10068-8{_}1281{_}"You'll let me return the basket when I bring you the books," Gray suggested, helplessly.
10068-8{_}1282{_}"I don't know," Johnnie hesitated.
10068-8{_}1283{_}Then, as a sudden inspiration came to her, "Mandy Meacham said she'd try to get me into a club for girls that Miss Sessions has.
10068-8{_}1284{_}She said Miss Sessions would lend me books.
10068-8{_}1285{_}Maybe you might just leave them with her.
10068-8{_}1286{_}I'm sure I should be mighty proud to have them.
10068-8{_}1287{_}I know I'll love to read them; but--well, you might just leave them with her."
10068-8{_}1288{_}A little satiric sparkle leaped to life in Stoddard's eyes.
10068-8{_}1289{_}He looked at the innocent, upraised face in wonder.
10068-8{_}1290{_}The most experienced manoeuverer of Society's legion could not have handled a difficult situation more deftly.
10068-8{_}1291{_}"The very thing," he said cheerily.
10068-8{_}1292{_}"I'll talk to Miss Sessions about it to-morrow."
10068-8{_}1293{_}CHAPTER VIII  OF THE USE OF WINGS  "I told you I'd speak a good word for you," shouted Mandy Meacham, putting her lips down close to Johnnie's ear where she struggled and fought with her looms amid the deafening clamour of the weaving room.
10068-8{_}1294{_}The girl looked up, flushed, tired, but eagerly receptive.
10068-8{_}1295{_}"Yes," her red lips shaped the word to the other's eyes, though no sound could make itself heard above that din except such eldritch shrieks as Mandy's.
10068-8{_}1296{_}"I done it.
10068-8{_}1297{_}I got you a invite to some doin's at the Uplift Club a-Wednesday."
10068-8{_}1298{_}Again Johnnie nodded and shaped "Yes" with her lips.
10068-8{_}1299{_}She added something which might have been "thank you"; the adorable smile that accompanied it said as much.
10068-8{_}1300{_}Mandy watched her, fascinated as the lithe, strong young figure bent and strained to correct a crease in the web where it turned the roll.
10068-8{_}1301{_}"They never saw anything like you in their born days, I'll bet," she yelled.
10068-8{_}1302{_}"I never did.
10068-8{_}1303{_}You're awful quare--but somehow I sorter like ye."
10068-8{_}1304{_}And she scuttled back to her looms as the room boss came in.
10068-8{_}1305{_}A weaver works by the piece, but Mandy had been reproved too often for slovenly methods not to know that she might be fined for neglect.
10068-8{_}1306{_}Her looms stood where she could continually get the newcomer's figure against the light, with its swift motion, its supple curves, and the brave carriage of the well-formed head.
10068-8{_}1307{_}The sight gave Mandy a curious satisfaction, as though it uttered what she would fain have said to the classes above her.
10068-8{_}1308{_}Hers was something the feeling which the private in the ranks has for the standard-bearer who carries the colours aloft, or the dashing officer who leads the charge.
10068-8{_}1309{_}Johnnie was the challenge she would have flung in the face of the enemy.
10068-8{_}1310{_}"I'll bet if you'd put one of Miss Lyddy's dresses on her she'd look nobby," Mandy ruminated, addressing her looms.
10068-8{_}1311{_}"That's what she would.
10068-8{_}1312{_}She'd have 'em all f--fa--faded away, as the feller says."
10068-8{_}1313{_}And so it came about that the next day Johnnie Consadine did not go to the mill at all, but spent the morning washing and ironing her one light print dress.
10068-8{_}1314{_}It was as coarse almost as flour-sacking, and the blue dots on it had paled till they made a suspicious speckle not unlike mildew; yet when she had combed her thick, fair hair, rolled it back from the white brow and braided it to a coronet round her head as she had seen that of the lady on the porch at the Palace of Pleasure; when, cleansed and smooth, she put the frock on, one forgot the dress in the youth of her, the hope, the glorious expectation there was in that eager face.
10068-8{_}1315{_}The ladies assisting in Miss Lydia Sessions's Uplift  Club for work among the mill girls, were almost all young and youngish women.
10068-8{_}1316{_}The mothers in Israel attacked the more serious problems of orphanages, winter's supplies of coal, and clothing for the destitute.
10068-8{_}1317{_}"But their souls must be fed, too," Miss Lydia asserted as she recruited her helpers for the Uplift work.
10068-8{_}1318{_}"Their souls must be fed; and who can reach the souls of these young girls so well as we who are near their own age, and who have had time for culture and spiritual growth?"
10068-8{_}1319{_}It was a good theory.
10068-8{_}1320{_}Perhaps one may say that it remains a good theory.
10068-8{_}1321{_}The manner of uplifting was to select a certain number of mill girls whom it was deemed well to help, approach them on the subject, and, if they appeared amenable, pay a substitute to take charge of their looms while those in process of being uplifted attended a meeting of the Club.
10068-8{_}1322{_}The gathering to which Johnnie was bidden was held in honour of a lady from London who had written a book on some subject which it was thought ought to appeal to workingwomen.
10068-8{_}1323{_}This lady intended to address the company and to mingle with them and get their views.
10068-8{_}1324{_}Most of those present being quite unfurnished with any views whatever on the problem she discussed, her position was something that of a pick-pocket in a moneyless crowd; but of this she was fortunately and happily unaware.
10068-8{_}1325{_}Mandy Meacham regarded Johnnie's preparation for the function with some disfavour.
10068-8{_}1326{_}"Ef you fix up like that," she remonstrated, "you're bound to look too nice to suit Miss Lyddy.
10068-8{_}1327{_}They won't be no men thar.
10068-8{_}1328{_}I'm goin' to wear my workin' dress, and tell her I hadn't nary minute nor nary cent to do other."
10068-8{_}1329{_}Johnnie laughed a little at this, as though it were intended for a joke.
10068-8{_}1330{_}"But I did have time," she objected.
10068-8{_}1331{_}"Miss Sessions would pay a substitute for the whole day though I told her I'd only need the afternoon for the party.
10068-8{_}1332{_}I think it was mighty good of her, and it's as little as I can do to make myself look as nice as I can."
10068-8{_}1333{_}"You ain't got the sense you was born with!"
10068-8{_}1334{_}fretted Mandy.
10068-8{_}1335{_}"Them thar kind ladies ain't a-carin' for you to look so fine.
10068-8{_}1336{_}They'll attend to all the fine lookin' theirselves.
10068-8{_}1337{_}What they want is to know how bad off you air, an' to have you say how much what they have did or give has helped you."
10068-8{_}1338{_}Such interchange of views brought the two girls to the door of the little frame chapel, given over for the day to Uplift work.
10068-8{_}1339{_}Within it rose a bustle and clatter, a hum of voices that spoke, a frilling of nervous, shrill laughter to edge the sound, and back of that the clink of dishes from a rear room where refreshments were being prepared.
10068-8{_}1340{_}Miss Sessions, near the door, had a receiving line, quite in the manner of any reception.
10068-8{_}1341{_}She herself, in a blouse of marvellous daintiness and sweeping skirts, stood beside the visitor from London to present her.
10068-8{_}1342{_}To this day Johnnie is uncertain as to where the wonderful blue silk frock of that lady from abroad was fastened, though she gave the undivided efforts of sharp young eyes and an inquiring mind to the problem a good portion of the time while it was within her view.
10068-8{_}1343{_}The Englishwoman was called Mrs. Archbold, and on her other hand stood a tall, slim lady with long gray-green eyes, prematurely gray hair which had plainly been red, and an odd little twist to her smile.
10068-8{_}1344{_}This was Mrs. Hexter, wife of the owner of the big woollen mills across the creek, and only bidden in to assist the Uplift work because the position of her husband gave her much power.
10068-8{_}1345{_}These, with the Misses Burchard, daughters of the rector, formed the reception committee.
10068-8{_}1346{_}"I am so charmed to see you here to-day," Miss Lydia smiled as they entered.
10068-8{_}1347{_}It was part of her theory to treat the mill girls exactly as she would members of her own circle.
10068-8{_}1348{_}Mandy, being old at the business, possessed herself of the high-held hand presented; but Johnnie only looked at it in astonishment, uncertain whether Miss Lydia meant to shake hands or pat her on the head.
10068-8{_}1349{_}Yet when she did finally divine what was intended, the quality of her apologetic smile ought to have atoned for her lapse.
10068-8{_}1350{_}"I'm sure proud to be here with you-all," she said.
10068-8{_}1351{_}"Looks like to me you are mighty kind to strangers."
10068-8{_}1352{_}The ineradicable dignity of the true mountaineer, who has always been as good as the best in his environment, preserved Johnnie from any embarrassment, any tendency to shrink or cringe.
10068-8{_}1353{_}Her beauty, in the fresh-washed print gown, was like a thing released and, as Miss Sessions might have put it, rampant.
10068-8{_}1354{_}Gray Stoddard had gone directly to Lydia Sessions, with his proffers of books, and his suggestions for Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1355{_}The explanation of how the girl came to be riding in his car that Sunday morning was neither as full nor as penitent as Miss Lydia could have wished; yet it did recognize the impropriety of the act, and was, in so far, satisfactory.
10068-8{_}1356{_}Miss Sessions made haste to form an alliance with the young man for the special upliftment of Johnnie Consadine.
10068-8{_}1357{_}She would have greatly preferred to interest him in Mandy Meacham, but beggars can not be choosers, and she took what she could get.
10068-8{_}1358{_}"Whom have we here?"
10068-8{_}1359{_}demanded the lady from London, leaning across and peering at Johnnie with friendly, near-sighted eyes.
10068-8{_}1360{_}"Why, what a blooming girl, to be sure!
10068-8{_}1361{_}You haven't been long from the country, I'll venture to guess, my dear."
10068-8{_}1362{_}Johnnie blushed and dimpled at being so kindly welcomed.
10068-8{_}1363{_}The mountain people are undemonstrative in speech and action; and that "my dear" seemed wonderful.
10068-8{_}1364{_}"I come from away up in the mountains," she said softly.
10068-8{_}1365{_}"From away up in the mountains," repeated the Englishwoman, her smiling gaze dwelling on Johnnie's radiant face.
10068-8{_}1366{_}"Why yes--so one would conceive.
10068-8{_}1367{_}Well, you mustn't lose all those pretty roses in the mill down here."
10068-8{_}1368{_}She was a visitor, remember; residents of Cottonville never admitted that roses, or anything else desirable, could be lost in the mills.
10068-8{_}1369{_}"I'll not," said Johnnie sturdily.
10068-8{_}1370{_}"I'm goin' to earn my way and send for Mother and the children, if hard work'll do it; but I'm a mighty big, stout, healthy somebody, and I aim to keep so."
10068-8{_}1371{_}Mrs. Archbold patted the tall young shoulder as she turned to Mandy Meacham whom Miss Lydia was eager to put through her paces for the benefit of the lady from London.
10068-8{_}1372{_}"Isn't that the girl Mr. Stoddard was speaking to me about?"
10068-8{_}1373{_}she inquired in a whisper as Johnnie moved away.
10068-8{_}1374{_}"I think it must be.
10068-8{_}1375{_}He said she was such a beauty, and I scarcely believe there could be two like her in one town."
10068-8{_}1376{_}"Such a type,' were Mr. Stoddard's exact words I believe," returned Miss Sessions a little frostily.
10068-8{_}1377{_}"Yes, John Consadine is quite a marked type of the mountaineer.
10068-8{_}1378{_}She is, as she said to you, a stout, healthy creature, and, I understand, very industrious.
10068-8{_}1379{_}I approve of John."
10068-8{_}1380{_}She approved of John, but she addressed herself to exploiting Mandy; and the lady in the blue silk frock learned how poor and helpless the Meacham woman had been before she got in to the mill work, how greatly the Uplift Club had benefited her, with many interesting details.
10068-8{_}1381{_}Yet as the English lady went from group to group in company with Miss Lydia and T.H.
10068-8{_}1382{_}Hexter's wife, her quick eyes wandered across the room to where a bright head rose a little taller than its fellows, and occasional bursts of laughter told that Johnnie was in a merry mood.
10068-8{_}1383{_}The threadbare attempt at a reception was gotten through laboriously.
10068-8{_}1384{_}The girls were finally settled in orderly rows, and Mrs. Archbold led to the platform.
10068-8{_}1385{_}The talk she had prepared for them was upon aspiration.
10068-8{_}1386{_}It was an essay, in fact, and she had delivered it successfully before many women's clubs.
10068-8{_}1387{_}She is not to be blamed that the language was as absolutely above the comprehension of her hearers as though it had been Greek.
10068-8{_}1388{_}She was a busy woman, with other aims and activities than those of working among the masses; Miss Lydia had heard her present talk, fancied it, and thought it would be the very thing for the Uplift Club.
10068-8{_}1389{_}For thirty minutes Johnnie sat concentrating desperately on every sentence that fell from the lips of the lady from London, trying harder to understand than she had ever tried to do anything in her life.
10068-8{_}1390{_}She put all her quick, young mind and avid soul into the struggle to receive, though piercingly aware every instant of the difference between her attire and that of the women who had bidden her there, noting acutely variations between their language and hers, their voices, their gestures and hers.
10068-8{_}1391{_}These were the women of Gray Stoddard's world.
10068-8{_}1392{_}Such were his feminine associates; here, then, must be her models.
10068-8{_}1393{_}Mandy and her likes got from the talk perhaps nothing at all, except that rich people might have what they liked if they wanted it--that at least was Miss Meacham's summing up of the matter when she went home that night.
10068-8{_}1394{_}But to Johnnie some of the sentences remained.
10068-8{_}1395{_}"You struggle and climb and strive," said Mrs. Archbold earnestly, "when, if you only knew it, you have wings.
10068-8{_}1396{_}And what are the wings of the soul?
10068-8{_}1397{_}The wings of the soul are aspiration.
10068-8{_}1398{_}Oh, that we would spread them and fly to the heights our longing eyes behold, the heights we dream of when we cannot see them, the heights we foolishly and mistakenly expect to climb some day."
10068-8{_}1399{_}Again Johnnie saw herself coming down the ridge at Shade's side; descending into the shadow, stepping closer to the droning mills; while above her the Palace of Pleasure swam in its golden glory, and these who were privileged to do so went out and in and laughed and were happy.
10068-8{_}1400{_}Were such heights as that what this woman meant?
10068-8{_}1401{_}Johnnie had let it typify to her the heights to which she intended to climb.
10068-8{_}1402{_}Was it indeed possible to fly to them instead?
10068-8{_}1403{_}The talk ended.
10068-8{_}1404{_}She sat so long with bent head that Miss Sessions finally came round and took the unoccupied chair beside her.
10068-8{_}1405{_}"Are you thinking it over, John?"
10068-8{_}1406{_}she inquired with that odd little note of hostility which she could never quite keep out of her voice when she addressed this girl.
10068-8{_}1407{_}"Yes'm," replied Johnnie meekly.
10068-8{_}1408{_}Several who were talking together in the vicinity relinquished their conversation to listen to the two.
10068-8{_}1409{_}Mrs. Hexter shot one of her quaint, crooked smiles at the lady from London and, with a silent gesture, bade her hearken.
10068-8{_}1410{_}"I think these things are most important for you girls who have to earn your daily bread," Miss Sessions condescended.
10068-8{_}1411{_}"Daily bread," echoed Johnnie softly.
10068-8{_}1412{_}She loved fine phrases as she loved fine clothes.
