10068-8{_}1413{_}"I know where that comes from.
10068-8{_}1414{_}It's in the prayer about 'daily bread,' and 'the kingdom and the power and the glory.'
10068-8{_}1415{_}Don't you think those are beautiful words, Miss Lydia--the 'power and the glory'?"
10068-8{_}1416{_}Miss Sessions's lips sucked in with that singular, half-reluctant expression of condemnation which was becoming fairly familiar to Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1417{_}"Oh, John!"
10068-8{_}1418{_}she said reprovingly, 'Daily bread' is all we have anything to do with.
10068-8{_}1419{_}Don't you remember that it says 'Thine be the kingdom and the power and the glory'?
10068-8{_}1420{_}Thine, John--Thine."
10068-8{_}1421{_}"Yes'm," returned Johnnie submissively.
10068-8{_}1422{_}But it was in her heart that certain upon this earth had their share of kingdoms and powers and the glories.
10068-8{_}1423{_}And, although she uttered that submissive "Yes'm," her high-couraged young heart registered a vow to achieve its own slice of these things as well as of daily bread.
10068-8{_}1424{_}"Didn't you enjoy Mrs. Archbold's talk?
10068-8{_}1425{_}I thought it very fine," Miss Sessions pursued.
10068-8{_}1426{_}"It sure was that," sighed Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1427{_}"I don't know as I understand it all--every word.
10068-8{_}1428{_}I tried to, but maybe I got some of it wrong."
10068-8{_}1429{_}"What is it you don't understand, John?"
10068-8{_}1430{_}inquired  Miss Lydia patronizingly.
10068-8{_}1431{_}"Ask me.
10068-8{_}1432{_}I'll explain anything you care to know about."
10068-8{_}1433{_}Johnnie turned to her, too desperately in earnest to note the other listeners to the conversation.
10068-8{_}1434{_}"Why, that about stretching out the wings of your spirit and flying.
10068-8{_}1435{_}Do you believe that?"
10068-8{_}1436{_}"I certainly do," Miss Sessions said brightly, as delighted at Johnnie's remembering part of the visitor's words as a small boy when he has taught his terrier to walk on its hind legs.
10068-8{_}1437{_}"Then if a body wants a thing bad enough, and keeps on a-wanting it--Oh, just awful--is that aspiration?
10068-8{_}1438{_}Will the thing you want that-a-way come to pass?"
10068-8{_}1439{_}"We-e-ell," Miss Sessions deemed it necessary to qualify her statement to this fiery and exact young questioner.
10068-8{_}1440{_}"You have to want the right thing, of course, John.
10068-8{_}1441{_}You have to want the right thing."
10068-8{_}1442{_}"Yes'm," agreed Johnnie heartily.
10068-8{_}1443{_}"And I'd 'low it was certainly the right thing, if it was what good folks--like you--want."
10068-8{_}1444{_}Miss Sessions flushed, yet she looked pleased, aware, if Johnnie was not, of the number of listeners.
10068-8{_}1445{_}Here was her work of Uplift among the mill girls being justified.
10068-8{_}1446{_}"I--Oh, really, I couldn't set myself up as a pattern," she said modestly.
10068-8{_}1447{_}"But you are," Johnnie assured her warmly.
10068-8{_}1448{_}"There ain't anybody in this room I'd rather go by as by you."
10068-8{_}1449{_}The fine gray eyes had been travelling from neck to belt, from shoulder to wrist of the lady who was enlightening her, "I think I never in all my life seen anything more sightly than that dress-body you're a-wearin'," she murmured softly.
10068-8{_}1450{_}"Where--how might a person come by such a one?
10068-8{_}1451{_}If you thought that my wishing and--aspiring--would ever bring me such as that, I'd sure try."
10068-8{_}1452{_}There rose a titter about the two.
10068-8{_}1453{_}It spread and swelled till the whole assembly was in a gale of laughter.
10068-8{_}1454{_}Miss Sessions's becoming blush deepened to the tint of angry mortification.
10068-8{_}1455{_}She looked about and assumed the air of a schoolmistress with a room full of noisy pupils; but Johnnie, her cheeks pink too, first swept them all with an astonished gaze which flung the long lashes up in such a wide curve of innocence as made her eyes bewitching, then joined it, and laughed as loud as any of them at she knew not what.
10068-8{_}1456{_}It was the one touch to put her with the majority, and leave her mentor stranded in a bleak minority.
10068-8{_}1457{_}Miss Sessions objected to the position.
10068-8{_}1458{_}"Oh, John!"
10068-8{_}1459{_}she said severely, so soon as she could be heard above the giggles.
10068-8{_}1460{_}"How you have misunderstood me, and Mrs. Archbold, and all we intended to bring to you!
10068-8{_}1461{_}What is a mere blouse like this to the uplift, the outlook, the development we were striving to offer?
10068-8{_}1462{_}I confess I am deeply disappointed in you."
10068-8{_}1463{_}This sobered Johnnie, instantly.
10068-8{_}1464{_}"I'm sorry," she said, bending forward to lay a wistful, penitent hand on that of Miss Sessions.
10068-8{_}1465{_}"I'll try to understand better.
10068-8{_}1466{_}I reckon I'm right dumb, and you'll have to have a lot of patience with me.
10068-8{_}1467{_}I don't rightly know what to aspire after."
10068-8{_}1468{_}The amende was so sweetly made that even Lydia Sessions, still exceedingly employed at being pictorially chagrined over the depravity of her neophyte, could but be appeased.
10068-8{_}1469{_}"I'll try to furnish you more suitable objects for your ambition," she murmured virtuously.
10068-8{_}1470{_}But the lady with the gray hair and the odd little twist to her smile now leaned forward and took a hand in the conversation.
10068-8{_}1471{_}"See here, Lydia," Mrs. Hexter remonstrated in crisp tones, "what's the matter with the girl's aspiring after a blouse like yours?
10068-8{_}1472{_}You took a lot of trouble and spent a lot of money to get that one.
10068-8{_}1473{_}I noticed you were careful to tell me it was imported, because I couldn't see the neck-band and find out that detail for myself.
10068-8{_}1474{_}That blouse is a dream--it's a dream.
10068-8{_}1475{_}If it's good enough aspiration for you or me, why not for this girl?"
10068-8{_}1476{_}"Oh, but Mrs. Hexter," murmured the mortified Miss Sessions, glancing uneasily toward the mill-girl contingent which was listening eagerly, and then at the speaker of the day, "I am sure Mrs. Archbold will agree with me that it would be a gross, material idea to aspire after blouses and such-like, when the poor child needs--er--other things so much more."
10068-8{_}1477{_}"Yes'm, I do that," conceded Johnnie dutifully, those changeful eyes of hers full of pensive, denied desire, as they swept the dainty gowns of the women before her.
10068-8{_}1478{_}"I do--you're right.
10068-8{_}1479{_}I wouldn't think of spending my money for a dress-body like that when I'm mighty near as barefoot as a rabbit this minute, and the little 'uns back home has to have every cent I can save.
10068-8{_}1480{_}I just thought that if beautiful wishes was ever really coming true--if it was right and proper for a person to have beautiful wishes--I'd like--"  Her voice faltered into discouraged silence.
10068-8{_}1481{_}Tears gathered and hung thick on her lashes.
10068-8{_}1482{_}Miss Sessions sent a beseeching look toward the lady from London.
10068-8{_}1483{_}Mrs. Archbold stepped accommodatingly into the breach.
10068-8{_}1484{_}"All aspiration is good," she said gently.
10068-8{_}1485{_}"I shouldn't be discouraged because it took a rather concrete form."
10068-8{_}1486{_}Johnnie's eyes were upon her face, trying to understand.
10068-8{_}1487{_}A "concrete form" she imagined might allude to the fact that Miss Sessions had a better figure than she.
10068-8{_}1488{_}Mrs. Hexter, glad of an ally, tossed that incorrigible gray head of hers and dashed into the conversation once more.
10068-8{_}1489{_}"If I were you, Johnnie, I'd just aspire as hard as I could in that direction," she said recklessly, her mischievous glance upon the flowing lines of Johnnie's young shoulders and throat.
10068-8{_}1490{_}"A blouse like that would be awfully fetching on you.
10068-8{_}1491{_}You'd look lovely in it.
10068-8{_}1492{_}Why shouldn't you aspire to it?
10068-8{_}1493{_}Maybe you'll have one just as pretty before the style changes.
10068-8{_}1494{_}I am sure you're nice enough, and good-looking enough, for the best in the way of purple and fine linen to come to you by the law of attraction--don't you believe in the law of attraction, Mrs.
10068-8{_}1495{_}Archbold?"
10068-8{_}1496{_}Lydia Sessions got up and moved away in shocked silence.
10068-8{_}1497{_}Mrs. Hexter was a good deal of a thorn in her flesh, and she only tolerated her because of Mr. Hexter and his position.
10068-8{_}1498{_}After the retreating and disaffected hostess came Mrs. Archbold's voice, with a thread of laughter in it.
10068-8{_}1499{_}"I believe in the law of such attraction as this girl has," she said kindly.
10068-8{_}1500{_}"What is it your Walt Whitman says about the fluid and attaching character?
10068-8{_}1501{_}That all hearts yearn toward it, that old and young must give it love.
10068-8{_}1502{_}That is, my dear," turning explainingly to Johnnie, "the character which gives much love, takes much interest in those about it, makes itself one with other people and their affairs--do you get my meaning?"
10068-8{_}1503{_}"I think I understand," half whispered Johnnie, glowing eyes on the face of the speaker.
10068-8{_}1504{_}"Do you mean that I am anything like that?
10068-8{_}1505{_}I do love everybody--most.
10068-8{_}1506{_}But how could I help it, when everybody is so good and kind to me?"
10068-8{_}1507{_}The glances of the older women met across the bright head.
10068-8{_}1508{_}"She won't have much use for feet to climb with," Mrs. Hexter summed it up, taking her figure from the talk earlier in the afternoon.
10068-8{_}1509{_}"She's got wings."
10068-8{_}1510{_}And puzzled Johnnie could only smile from one to the other.
10068-8{_}1511{_}"Wings!"
10068-8{_}1512{_}whispered Mandy Meacham to herself.
10068-8{_}1513{_}Mandy was not only restricted to the use of spiritual feet; she was lame in the soul as well, poor creature, "Wings--air they callin' her a angel?"
10068-8{_}1514{_}CHAPTER IX  A BIT OF METAL  In the valleys of Tennessee, spring has a trick of dropping down on the world like a steaming wet blanket.
10068-8{_}1515{_}The season that Johnnie Consadine went to work in the mills at Cottonville, May came in with warm rains.
10068-8{_}1516{_}Stifling nights followed sultry, drenching days, till vegetation everywhere sprouted unwholesomely and the mountain slopes had almost the reek of tropic jungles.
10068-8{_}1517{_}Yet the girl performed the labours of a factory weaver with almost passionate enthusiasm and devotion.
10068-8{_}1518{_}Always and always she was looking beyond the mere present moment.
10068-8{_}1519{_}If tending loom was the road which led to the power and the glory, what need to complain that it--the mere road--was but dull earth?
10068-8{_}1520{_}She tried conscientiously, to do and be exactly what Lydia Sessions seemed to want.
10068-8{_}1521{_}Gray Stoddard's occasional spoken word, or the more lengthy written messages he had taken to putting in the books he sent her, seemed to demand of her nothing, but always inspired to much.
10068-8{_}1522{_}For all his disposition to keep hands off the personal development of his friends, perhaps on account of it, Gray made an excellent teacher, and these writings--the garnered grain, the gist, of his own wide culture--were the very sinews for the race Johnnie was setting out on.
10068-8{_}1523{_}She began to intelligently guard her speech, her manner, her very thoughts, conforming them to what she knew of his ideals.
10068-8{_}1524{_}Miss Session's striving to build up an imitation lady on the sincere foundation Johnnie offered appealed less to the girl, and had therefore less effect; but she immediately responded to Stoddard's methods, tucking in to the books she returned written queries or records of perplexity, which gradually expanded into notes, expressions of her own awakened thought, and even fancies, which held from the first a quaint charm and individuality.
10068-8{_}1525{_}The long, hot days at the foot of the hills did seem to the mountain-bred creature interminable and stifling.
10068-8{_}1526{_}Perspiration dripped from white faces as the operatives stood listlessly at their looms, or the children straggled back and forth in the narrow lanes between the frames, tending the endlessly turning spools.
10068-8{_}1527{_}The Hardwick Mill had both spinning and weaving departments.
10068-8{_}1528{_}Administrative ability is as much a native gift as the poet's voice or the actor's grace, and the managers of any large business are always on the lookout for it.
10068-8{_}1529{_}Before Johnnie Consadine had been two months in the factory she was given charge of a spinning room.
10068-8{_}1530{_}But the dignity of the new position--even the increase of pay--had a cloud upon it.
10068-8{_}1531{_}She was beginning to understand the enmity there is between the soulless factory and the human tide that feeds its life.
10068-8{_}1532{_}She knew now that the tasks of the little spinners, which seemed less than child's play, were deadly in their monotony, their long indoor hours, and the vibrant clamour amid which they were performed.
10068-8{_}1533{_}Her own vigorous young frame resisted valiantly; yet the Saturday half-holiday, the Sunday of rest, could scarcely renew her for the exorbitant hours of mechanical toil.
10068-8{_}1534{_}As she left the mill those sultry evenings, with the heat mists still tremulous over the valley and heat lightnings bickering in the west, she went with a lagging step up the village street, not looking, as had been her wont, first toward the far blue mountains, and then at the glorious state of the big valley.
10068-8{_}1535{_}The houses of the operatives were set up haphazard and the village was denied all beauty.
10068-8{_}1536{_}Most of the yards were unfenced, and here and there a row of shanties would be crowded so close together that speech in one could be heard in the other.
10068-8{_}1537{_}"And then if any ketchin' disease does break out, like the dipthery did last year," Mavity Bence said one evening as she walked home with Johnnie, "hit's sartin shore to go through 'em like it would go through a family."
10068-8{_}1538{_}Johnnie looked curiously at the dirty yards with their debris of lard buckets and tin cans.
10068-8{_}1539{_}Space--air, earth and sky--was cheap and plentiful in the mountains.
10068-8{_}1540{_}It seemed strange to be sparing of it, down here where people were so rich.
10068-8{_}1541{_}"What makes 'em build so close, Aunt Mavity?"
10068-8{_}1542{_}she asked.
10068-8{_}1543{_}"Hit's the Company," returned Mrs. Bence lifelessly.
10068-8{_}1544{_}"They don't want to spend any more than they have to for land.
10068-8{_}1545{_}Besides they want everything to be nigh to the mill.
10068-8{_}1546{_}Lord--hit don't make no differ.
10068-8{_}1547{_}Only when a fire starts in a row of 'em hit cleans up the Company's property same as it does the plunder of the folks that lives in 'em.
10068-8{_}1548{_}You just got to be thankful if there don't chance to be one or more baby children locked up in the houses and burned along with the other stuff.
10068-8{_}1549{_}I've knowed that to happen more than oncet."
10068-8{_}1550{_}Johnnie's face whitened.
10068-8{_}1551{_}"Miss Lydia says she's going to persuade her brother-in-law to furnish a kindergarten and a day nursery for the Hardwick Mill," she offered hastily.
10068-8{_}1552{_}"They have one at some other mill down in Georgia, and she says it's fine the way they take care of the children while the mothers are at work in the factory."
10068-8{_}1553{_}"Uh-uh," put in Mandy Meacham slowly, speaking over the shoulders of the two, "but I'd a heap ruther take care of my own child--ef I had one.
10068-8{_}1554{_}An' ef the mills can afford to pay for it the one way, they can afford to pay for it t'other way.
10068-8{_}1555{_}Miss Liddy's schemes is all for the showin' off of the swells and the rich folks.
10068-8{_}1556{_}I reckon that, with her, hit'll end in talk, anyhow--hit always does."
10068-8{_}1557{_}"Aunt Mavity," pursued Johnnie timidly, "do you reckon the water's unhealthy down here in Cottonville?
10068-8{_}1558{_}Looks like all the children in the mill have the same white, puny look.
10068-8{_}1559{_}I thought maybe the water didn't agree with them."
10068-8{_}1560{_}Mavity Bence laughed out mirthlessly.
10068-8{_}1561{_}"The water!"
10068-8{_}1562{_}she echoed in a tone of amused contempt.
10068-8{_}1563{_}"Johnnie, you're mighty smart about some things; cain't you see that a cotton mill is bound to either kill or cripple a child?
10068-8{_}1564{_}Them that don't die, sort o' drags along and grows up to be mis'able, undersized, sickly somebodies.
10068-8{_}1565{_}Hit's true the Hardwick Mill won't run night turn; hit's true they show mo' good will about hirin' older children; but if you can make a cotton mill healthy for young-uns, you can do more than God A'mighty."
10068-8{_}1566{_}She wiped her eyes furtively.
10068-8{_}1567{_}"Lou was well growed before ever she went in the mill.
10068-8{_}1568{_}I know in reason hit never hurt her.
10068-8{_}1569{_}I mean these here mammies that I see puttin' little tricks to work that ort to be runnin' out o' doors gettin' their strength and growth--well, po' souls, I reckon they don't know no better, God forgive 'em!"
10068-8{_}1570{_}"But if they got sick or anything, there's always the hospital," Johnnie spoke up hopefully, as they passed the clean white building standing high on its green slope.
10068-8{_}1571{_}"The hospital!"
10068-8{_}1572{_}echoed Mandy, with a half-terrified glance over her shoulder.
10068-8{_}1573{_}"Yes, ef you want to be shipped out of town in a box for the student doctors to cut up, I reckon the hospital is a good place.
10068-8{_}1574{_}It's just like everything else the rich swells does--it's for their profit, not for our'n.
10068-8{_}1575{_}They was a lot of big talk when they built that thar hospital, and every one of us was axed to give something for beds and such.
10068-8{_}1576{_}We was told that if we got hurt in the mill we could go thar free, and if we fell sick they'd doctor us for little or nothin'.
10068-8{_}1577{_}They can afford it--considerin' the prices they git for dead bodies, I reckon."
10068-8{_}1578{_}"Now, Mandy, you don't believe any such as that," remonstrated Johnnie, with a half-smile.
10068-8{_}1579{_}"Believe it--I know it to be true!"
10068-8{_}1580{_}Mandy stuck to her point stubbornly.
10068-8{_}1581{_}"Thar was Lura Dawson; her folks was comin' down to git the body and bury hit, and when they got here the hospital folks couldn't tell 'em whar to look--no, they couldn't.
10068-8{_}1582{_}Atlas Dawson 'lows he'll git even with 'em if it takes him the rest of his natural life.
10068-8{_}1583{_}His wife was a Bushares and her whole tribe is out agin the hospital folks and the mill folks down here.
10068-8{_}1584{_}I reckon you live too far up in the mountains to hear the talk, but some of these swells had better look out."
10068-8{_}1585{_}As the long, hot days followed each other, Johnnie noticed how Mandy failed.
10068-8{_}1586{_}Her hand was forever at her side, where she had a stitch-like pain, that she called "a jumpin' misery."
10068-8{_}1587{_}Even broad, seasoned Mavity Bence grew pallid and gaunt.
10068-8{_}1588{_}Only Pap Himes thrived.
10068-8{_}1589{_}His trouble was rheumatism, and the hot days were his best.
10068-8{_}1590{_}Of evenings he would sit on the porch in his broad, rush-bottomed chair, the big yellow cat on his knees, and smoke his pipe and, if he cared to do so, banter unkindly with the girls on the steps.
10068-8{_}1591{_}Early in the season as it was, the upstairs rooms were terribly hot; and sometimes the poor creatures sat or lay on the porch till well past midnight.
10068-8{_}1592{_}Across the gulch were songs and the strumming of banjos or guitars, where the young fellows at the inn waked late.
10068-8{_}1593{_}The rich people on top of the hill were beginning to make their preparations to flit to the seashore or mountains.
10068-8{_}1594{_}Lydia Sessions left for two weeks, promising to return in June, and the Uplift work drooped, neglected.
10068-8{_}1595{_}There seems to be an understanding that people do not need uplifting so much during hot weather.
10068-8{_}1596{_}Gray Stoddard was faithful in the matter of books.
10068-8{_}1597{_}He carried them to Lydia Sessions and discussed with that young lady a complete course of reading for Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1598{_}Lydia was in the position of one taking bad medicine for good results.
10068-8{_}1599{_}She could not but delight in any enterprise which brought Stoddard intimately to her, yet the discussion of Johnnie Consadine, the admiration he expressed for the girl's character and work, were as so much quinine.
10068-8{_}1600{_}Johnnie herself was dumb and abashed, now, in his presence.
10068-8{_}1601{_}She sought vainly for the poise and composure which were her natural birthright in most of the situations of life.
10068-8{_}1602{_}Yet her perturbation was not that of distress.
10068-8{_}1603{_}The sight of him, the sound of his voice, even if he were not saying good morning to her, would cheer her heart for one whole, long, hot day: and if he spoke to her, if he looked at her, nothing could touch her with sadness for hours afterward.
10068-8{_}1604{_}She asked no questions why this was so; she met it with a sort of desperate bravery, accepting the joy, refusing to see the sorrow there might be in it.
10068-8{_}1605{_}And she robbed herself of necessary sleep to read Stoddard's books, to study them, to wring from them the last precious crumb of help or information that they might have for her.
10068-8{_}1606{_}The mountain dweller is a mental creature.
10068-8{_}1607{_}An environment which builds lean, vigorous bodies, is apt to nourish keen, alert minds.
10068-8{_}1608{_}Johnnie crowded into her few months of night reading a world, of ripening culture.
10068-8{_}1609{_}Ever since the Sunday morning of the automobile ride, Shade Buckheath had been making elaborate pretense of having forgotten that such a person as Johnnie Consadine existed.
10068-8{_}1610{_}If he saw her approaching, he turned his back; and when forced to recognize her, barely growled some unintelligible greeting.
10068-8{_}1611{_}Then one evening she came suddenly into the machine room.
10068-8{_}1612{_}She walked slowly down the long aisle between pieces of whirring machinery, carrying all eyes with her.
10068-8{_}1613{_}It was an offence to Buckheath to note how the other young fellows turned from their tasks to look after her.
10068-8{_}1614{_}She had no business down here where the men were.
10068-8{_}1615{_}That was just like a fool girl, always running after--.
10068-8{_}1616{_}She paused at his bench.
10068-8{_}1617{_}"Shade," she said, bending close so that he might hear the words, "I got leave to come in and ask you to make me a thing like this--see?"
10068-8{_}1618{_}showing a pattern for a peculiarly slotted strip of metal.
10068-8{_}1619{_}Buckheath returned to the surly indifference of demeanour which was natural to him.
10068-8{_}1620{_}Yet he smiled covertly as he examined the drawing she had made of the thing she wanted.
10068-8{_}1621{_}He divined in this movement of Johnnie's but an attempt to approach himself, and, as she explained with some particularity, he paid more attention to the girl than to her words.
10068-8{_}1622{_}"I want a big enough hole here to put a bolt through," she repeated.
10068-8{_}1623{_}"Shade--do you understand?
10068-8{_}1624{_}You're not listening to one word I say."
10068-8{_}1625{_}Buckheath turned and grinned broadly at her.
10068-8{_}1626{_}"What's the use of this foolishness, Johnnie?"
10068-8{_}1627{_}he inquired, clinking the strips of metal between his fingers.
10068-8{_}1628{_}"Looks like you and me could find a chance to visit without going to so much trouble."
10068-8{_}1629{_}Johnnie opened her gray eyes wide and stared at him.
10068-8{_}1630{_}"Foolishness!"
10068-8{_}1631{_}she echoed.
10068-8{_}1632{_}"Mr. Stoddard didn't call it foolishness when I named it to him.
10068-8{_}1633{_}He said I was to have anything I wanted made, and that one of the loom-fixers could attend to it."
10068-8{_}1634{_}"Mr. Stoddard--what's he got to do with it?"
10068-8{_}1635{_}demanded Shade.
10068-8{_}1636{_}"He hasn't anything; but that I spoke to him about it, and he told me to try any plan I wanted to."
10068-8{_}1637{_}"Well, the less you talk to the bosses--a girl like you, working here in the mill--the better name you'll bear," Shade told her, twisting the drawing in his hands and regarding her from under lowered brows.
10068-8{_}1638{_}"Don't tear that," cautioned Johnnie impatiently.
10068-8{_}1639{_}"I have to speak to some of the people in authority sometimes--the same as you do.

10068-8{_}1641{_}"There's nothing the matter with me," Buckheath declared wagging his head portentously, and avoiding her eye.

10068-8{_}1643{_}"When I see a girl riding in an automobile with one of these young bosses," he growled, close to her ear, "I know what to think--and so does everybody else."
10068-8{_}1644{_}It was out.
10068-8{_}1645{_}He had said it at last.
10068-8{_}1646{_}He stared at her fiercely.
10068-8{_}1647{_}The red dyed her face and neck at his words and look.
10068-8{_}1648{_}For a desperate moment she took counsel with herself.

10068-8{_}1651{_}she inquired.
10068-8{_}1652{_}"Well, I'm glad you spoke and relieved your mind."
10068-8{_}1653{_}Then she went on evenly, "Mr. Stoddard had been up in the mountains that Sunday to get a flower that he wanted, like the one you stepped on and broke the day I came down.
10068-8{_}1654{_}I was up there and showed him where the things grow.

10068-8{_}1656{_}That's all there was to it."
10068-8{_}1657{_}"Mighty poor excuse," grunted Shade, turning his shoulder to her.
10068-8{_}1658{_}"It's not an excuse at all," said Johnnie.

10068-8{_}1660{_}I've told you the truth about it because we were old friends and you named it to me; but I'm sorry now that I spoke at all.
10068-8{_}1661{_}Give me that drawing and those patterns back.
10068-8{_}1662{_}Some of the other loom-fixers can make what I want."
10068-8{_}1663{_}"You get mad quick, don't you?"
10068-8{_}1664{_}Buckheath asked, turning to her with a half-taunting, half-relenting smile on his face.

10068-8{_}1670{_}And without another word the girl left him.
10068-8{_}1671{_}After Johnnie was gone, Buckheath chewed for some time the bitter cud of chagrin.
10068-8{_}1672{_}He was wholly mistaken, then, in the object of her visit to the mechanical department?
10068-8{_}1673{_}Yet he was a cool-headed fellow, always alert for that which might bring him gain.
10068-8{_}1674{_}Pushing, aspiring, he subscribed for and faithfully studied a mechanics' journal which continually urged upon its readers the profit of patenting small improvements on machinery already in use.
10068-8{_}1675{_}Indeed everybody, these days, in the factories, is on the lookout for patentable improvements.
10068-8{_}1676{_}Why might not Johnnie have stumbled on to something worth while?
10068-8{_}1677{_}That Passmore and Consadine tribe were all smart fools.
10068-8{_}1678{_}He made the slotted strips she wanted, and delivered them to her the next day with civil words.
10068-8{_}1679{_}When, after she had them in use on the spinning jennies upstairs for a week, she came down bringing them for certain minute alterations, his attitude was one of friendly helpfulness.
10068-8{_}1680{_}"You say you use 'em on the frames?
10068-8{_}1681{_}What for?

10068-8{_}1683{_}he asked her, examining the little contrivance lingeringly.

10068-8{_}1685{_}Any boy or girl tending a frame can go to the end of it and see if anything's the matter without walking plumb down.
10068-8{_}1686{_}When you get them fixed the way I want them, I tell you they'll be fine."
10068-8{_}1687{_}The next afternoon saw Shade Buckheath in the spooling room, watching the operation of Johnnie Consadine's simple device for notifying the frame-tender if a thread fouled or broke.

10068-8{_}1690{_}There ought to be a ring of babbit metal around that slot, too--I reckon I could get it in Watauga.
10068-8{_}1691{_}If you'll let me take 'em now, I'll fix 'em up for you soon as I can, so that they'll do fine."
10068-8{_}1692{_}Johnnie remonstrated, half-heartedly, as he gathered the crude little invention from the frames; but his proposition wore a plausible face, and she suffered him to take them.
10068-8{_}1693{_}"They ain't but five here," he said to her sharply.

10068-8{_}1695{_}Where's the other one?"
10068-8{_}1696{_}He looked so startled, he spoke so anxiously, that she laughed.
10068-8{_}1697{_}"I think that must be the one I carried home," she said carelessly.
10068-8{_}1698{_}"I had a file, and was trying to fix it myself one evening, and I reckon I never brought it back."

10068-8{_}1700{_}Wait till we get it all fixed right," he pursued, as he saw the rising wonder in her face.
10068-8{_}1701{_}"No need to tell every feller all you know--so he'll be jest as smart as you are.
10068-8{_}1702{_}Ain't that so?

10068-8{_}1704{_}I don't want it layin' round for somebody to get hold of and--you find me that other strip.
10068-8{_}1705{_}Hunt it up, won't you?"

10068-8{_}1707{_}Johnnie told him.

10068-8{_}1713{_}And Mr.

10068-8{_}1722{_}Two or three times Johnnie reminded Shade of his promise to bring the little strips back, and always he had an excuse ready for her: he had been very busy--the metal he wanted was out of stock--he would fix them for her just as soon as he could.

10068-8{_}1724{_}The loom-fixers and mechanics, belonging, be it remembered, to a trades-union, were out of all the mills by five o'clock.
10068-8{_}1725{_}It was a significant point for any student of economic conditions to note these strapping young males sitting at ease upon the porches of their homes or boarding houses, when the sweating, fagged women weavers and childish spinners trooped across the bridges an hour after.
10068-8{_}1726{_}Johnnie was surprised, therefore, one evening, nearly two weeks later, to find Shade waiting for her at the door of the mill.
10068-8{_}1727{_}"I wish't you'd walk a piece up the Gap road with me, I want to have speech with you," the young fellow told her.
10068-8{_}1728{_}"I can't go far; I 'most always try to be home in time to help Aunt Mavity put supper on the table, or anyway to wash up the dishes for her," the girl replied to him.

10068-8{_}1735{_}'Pears like you won't look at a body."

10068-8{_}1737{_}Johnnie returned, with a deprecating smile.

10068-8{_}1739{_}Seems like I'm tired every minute of the day--and I couldn't tell you why.
10068-8{_}1740{_}I sure don't have anything hard to do.
10068-8{_}1741{_}I think sometimes I need the good hard work I used to have back in the mountains to get rested on."

10068-8{_}1746{_}I wouldn't for the world break down at my work, when I've just begun to earn so much, and am sending money home to mother."
10068-8{_}1747{_}Inside the offices Lydia Sessions stood near her brother's desk.

10068-8{_}1763{_}echoed Stoddard.

10068-8{_}1768{_}Her instinct has proved wholly trustworthy so far.

10068-8{_}1773{_}Stoddard looked a bit blank for an instant.

10068-8{_}1785{_}She is trying hard, I admit; but her speech is--well, it certainly is rather uncivilized."
10068-8{_}1786{_}Stoddard looked as though he might debate that matter a bit.
10068-8{_}1787{_}Then he questioned, instead:  "Did you ever get a letter from her?
10068-8{_}1788{_}She doesn't carry her quaint little archaisms of pronunciation and wording into her writing.
10068-8{_}1789{_}Her letters are delicious."
10068-8{_}1790{_}Miss Sessions turned hastily to the window and looked out, apparently to observe whether her brother was ready to leave or not.
10068-8{_}1791{_}Johnnie Consadine's letters--her letters.
10068-8{_}1792{_}What--when--?
10068-8{_}1793{_}Of course she could not baldly question him in such a matter; and the simple explanation of a little note of thanks with a returned book, or the leaf which reported impressions from its reading tucked in between the pages occurred to her perturbed mind.
10068-8{_}1794{_}"You quite astonish me," she said finally.
10068-8{_}1795{_}"Well--that _is_ good hearing.
10068-8{_}1796{_}Mr. Stoddard," with sudden decision, "don't you believe that it would be well worth while, in view of all this, to raise the money and send John Consadine away to a good school?
10068-8{_}1797{_}There are several fine ones in New England where she might partially work her way; and really, from what you say, it seems to me she's worthy of such a chance."
10068-8{_}1798{_}Stoddard glanced at her in surprise.
10068-8{_}1799{_}"Why, Miss Sessions, doesn't this look like going squarely back on your most cherished theories?
10068-8{_}1800{_}If it's only to bestow a little money, and send her away to some half-charity school, what becomes of your argument that people who have had advantages should give of themselves and their comradeship to those they wish to help?"
10068-8{_}1801{_}There was a boyish eagerness in his manner; his changeful gray-brown eyes were alight; he came close and laid a hand on her arm--quite an unusual demonstration with Gray Stoddard.
10068-8{_}1802{_}"You mustn't discourage me," he said winningly.
10068-8{_}1803{_}"I'm such a hopeful disciple.
10068-8{_}1804{_}I've never enjoyed anything more in my life than this enterprise you and I have undertaken together, providing the right food for so bright and so responsive a mind."
10068-8{_}1805{_}Miss Lydia looked at him in a sort of despair.
10068-8{_}1806{_}"Yes--oh, yes.
10068-8{_}1807{_}I quite understand that," she agreed almost mechanically.
10068-8{_}1808{_}"I don't mean to go back on my principles.
10068-8{_}1809{_}But what John needs is a good, sound education from the beginning.
10068-8{_}1810{_}Don't you think so?"
10068-8{_}1811{_}"No," said Stoddard promptly.
10068-8{_}1812{_}"Indeed I do not.
10068-8{_}1813{_}Development must come from within.
10068-8{_}1814{_}To give it a chance--to lend it stimulus--that's all a friend can do.
10068-8{_}1815{_}A ready-made education plastered on the outside cultivates nobody.
10068-8{_}1816{_}Moreover, Johnnie is in no crying need of mere schooling.
10068-8{_}1817{_}You don't seem to know how well provided she has been in that respect.
10068-8{_}1818{_}But the thing that settles the matter is that she would not accept any such charitable arrangement.
10068-8{_}1819{_}Unless you're tired of our present method, I vote to continue it."
10068-8{_}1820{_}Lydia Sessions had been for some moments watching Johnnie Consadine who sat on her box at the door of the little garage.
10068-8{_}1821{_}She had refrained from mentioning this fact to her companion; but now Shade Buckheath stepped out to join Johnnie, and instantly Lydia turned and motioned Stoddard to her.
10068-8{_}1822{_}"Look there," she whispered.
10068-8{_}1823{_}"Don't they make a perfect couple?
10068-8{_}1824{_}You and I may do what we choose about cultivating the girl's mind--she'll marry a man of her own class, and there it will end."
10068-8{_}1825{_}"Why should you say that?"
10068-8{_}1826{_}asked Stoddard abruptly.
10068-8{_}1827{_}"Those two do not belong to the same class.
10068-8{_}1828{_}They--"  "Oh, Mr. Stoddard!
10068-8{_}1829{_}They grew up side by side; they went to school together, and I imagine were sweethearts long before they came to Cottonville."
10068-8{_}1830{_}"Do you think that makes them of the same class?"
10068-8{_}1831{_}asked Stoddard impatiently.
10068-8{_}1832{_}"I should say the presumption was still greater the other way.
10068-8{_}1833{_}I was not alluding to social classes."
10068-8{_}1834{_}"You're so odd," murmured Lydia Sessions.
10068-8{_}1835{_}"These mountaineers are all alike."
10068-8{_}1836{_}*       *       *       *       *  The village road was a smother of white dust; the weeds beside it drooped powdered heads; evil odours reeked through the little place; but when Shade and Johnnie had passed its confines, the air from the mountains greeted them sweetly; the dusty white road gave place to springy leaf-mould, mixed with tiny, sharp stones.
10068-8{_}1837{_}A young moon rode low in the west.
10068-8{_}1838{_}The tank-a-tank of cowbells sounded from homing animals.
10068-8{_}1839{_}Up in the dusky Gap, whip-poor-wills were beginning to call.
10068-8{_}1840{_}"I'm glad I came," said Johnnie, pushing the hair off her hot forehead.
10068-8{_}1841{_}She was speaking to herself, aware that Buckheath paid little attention, but walked in silence a step ahead, twisting a little branch of sassafras in his fingers.
10068-8{_}1842{_}The spicy odour of the bark was afterward associated in Johnnie's mind with what he had then to say.
10068-8{_}1843{_}"Johnnie," he began, facing around and barring her way, when they were finally alone together between the trees, "do you remember the last time you and me was on this piece of road here--do you?"
10068-8{_}1844{_}He had intended to remind her of the evening she came to Cottonville: but instead, recollection built for her once more the picture of that slope bathed in Sabbath sunshine.
10068-8{_}1845{_}There was the fork where the Hardwick carriage had turned off; to this side went Shade and his fellows, with Mandy and the girls following; and down the middle of the road she herself came, seated in the car beside Stoddard.
10068-8{_}1846{_}For a moment memory choked and blinded Johnnie.
10068-8{_}1847{_}She could neither see the path before them, nor find the voice to answer her questioner.
10068-8{_}1848{_}The bleak pathos of her situation came home to her, and tears of rare self-pity filled her eyes.
10068-8{_}1849{_}Why was it a disgrace that Stoddard should treat her kindly?
10068-8{_}1850{_}Why must she be ashamed of her feeling for him?
10068-8{_}1851{_}Shade's voice broke in harshly.
10068-8{_}1852{_}"Do you remember?
10068-8{_}1853{_}You ain't forgot, have you?
10068-8{_}1854{_}Ever since that time I've intended to speak to you--to tell you--"  "Well, you needn't do it," she interrupted him passionately.
10068-8{_}1855{_}"I won't hear a word against Mr. Stoddard, if that's what you're aiming at."
10068-8{_}1856{_}Buckheath fell back a pace and stared with angry eyes.
10068-8{_}1857{_}"Stoddard--Gray Stoddard?"
10068-8{_}1858{_}he repeated.
10068-8{_}1859{_}"What's a swell like that got to do with you and me, Johnnie Consadine?
10068-8{_}1860{_}You want to let Gray Stoddard and his kind alone--yes, and make them let you alone, if you and me are going to marry."
10068-8{_}1861{_}It was Johnnie's turn to stare.
10068-8{_}1862{_}"If we're going to marry!"
10068-8{_}1863{_}she echoed blankly--"going to marry!"
10068-8{_}1864{_}The girl had had her lovers.
10068-8{_}1865{_}Despite hard work and the stigma of belonging to the borrowing Passmore family, Johnnie had commanded the homage of more than one heart.
10068-8{_}1866{_}She was not without a healthy young woman's relish for this sort of admiration; but Shade Buckheath's proposal came with so little grace, in such almost sinister form, that she scarcely recognized it.
10068-8{_}1867{_}"Yes, if we're going to wed," reiterated Buckheath sullenly.
10068-8{_}1868{_}"I'm willin' to have you."
10068-8{_}1869{_}Johnnie's tense, almost tragic manner relaxed.
10068-8{_}1870{_}She laughed suddenly.
10068-8{_}1871{_}"I didn't know you was joking, Shade," she said good-humouredly.
10068-8{_}1872{_}"I took you to be in earnest.
10068-8{_}1873{_}You'll have to excuse me."
10068-8{_}1874{_}"I am in earnest," Buckheath told her, almost fiercely.
10068-8{_}1875{_}"I reckon I'm a fool; but I want you.
10068-8{_}1876{_}Any day"--he spoke with a curious, half-savage reluctance--"any day you'll say the word, I'll take you."
10068-8{_}1877{_}His eyes, like his voice, were resentful, yet eager.
10068-8{_}1878{_}He took off his hat and wiped the perspiration from his brow, looking away from her now, toward the road by which they had climbed.
10068-8{_}1879{_}Johnnie regarded him through her thick eyelashes, the smile still lingering bright in her eyes.
10068-8{_}1880{_}After all, it was only a rather unusual kind of sweethearting, and not a case of it to touch her feelings.
10068-8{_}1881{_}"I'm mighty sorry," she said soberly, "but I ain't aimin' to wed any man, fixed like I am.
10068-8{_}1882{_}Mother and the children have to be looked after, and I can't ask a man to do for 'em, so I have it to do myself."
10068-8{_}1883{_}"Of course I can't take your mother and the children," Buckheath objected querulously, as though she had asked him to do so.
10068-8{_}1884{_}"But you I'll take; and you'd do well to think it over.
10068-8{_}1885{_}You won't get such a chance soon again, and I'm apt to change my mind if you put on airs with me this way."
10068-8{_}1886{_}Johnnie shook her head.
10068-8{_}1887{_}"I know it's a fine chance, Shade," she said in the kindest tone, "but I'm hoping you will change your mind, and that soon; for it's just like I tell you."
10068-8{_}1888{_}She turned with evident intention of going back and terminating their interview.
10068-8{_}1889{_}Buckheath stepped beside her in helpless fury.
10068-8{_}1890{_}He knew she would have other, opportunities, and better.
10068-8{_}1891{_}He was aware how futile was this threat of withdrawing his proposition.
10068-8{_}1892{_}Hot, tired, angry, the dust of the way prickling on his face and neck, he was persistently conscious of a letter in the pocket of his striped shirt, over his heavily beating heart, warm and moist like the shirt itself, with the sweat of his body.
10068-8{_}1893{_}Good Lord!
10068-8{_}1894{_}That letter which had come from Washington this morning informing him that the device this girl had invented was patentable, filled her hands with gold.
10068-8{_}1895{_}It was necessary that he should have control of her, and at once.
10068-8{_}1896{_}He put from him the knowledge of how her charm wrought upon him--bound him the faster every time he spoke to her.
10068-8{_}1897{_}Cold, calculating, sluggishly selfish, he had not reckoned with her radiant personality, nor had the instinct to know that, approached closely, it must inevitably light in him unwelcome and inextinguishable fires.
10068-8{_}1898{_}"Johnnie," he said finally, "you ain't saying no to me, are you?
10068-8{_}1899{_}You take time to think it over--but not so very long--I'll name it to you again."
10068-8{_}1900{_}"Please don't, Shade," remonstrated the girl, walking on fast, despite the oppressive heat of the evening.
10068-8{_}1901{_}"I wish you wouldn't speak of it to me any more; and I can't go walking with you this way.
10068-8{_}1902{_}I have obliged to help Aunt Mavity; and every minute of time I get from that, and my work, I'm putting in on my books and reading."
10068-8{_}1903{_}She stepped ahead of him now, and Buckheath regarded her back with sullen, sombre eyes.
10068-8{_}1904{_}What was he to do?
10068-8{_}1905{_}How come nearer her when she thus held herself aloof?
10068-8{_}1906{_}"Johnnie Consadine!"
10068-8{_}1907{_}The girl checked her steps a bit at a new sound in his voice.
10068-8{_}1908{_}"I'll tell you just one thing, and you'd better never forget it, neither.
10068-8{_}1909{_}I ain't no fool.
10068-8{_}1910{_}I know mighty well an' good your reason for treating me this-a-way.
10068-8{_}1911{_}Your reason's got a name.
10068-8{_}1912{_}Hit's called Mr. Gray Stoddard.
10068-8{_}1913{_}You behave yo'self an' listen to reason, or I'll get even with him for it.
10068-8{_}1914{_}Damn him--I'll fix him!"
10068-8{_}1915{_}CHAPTER X  THE SANDALS OF JOY  "Come in here, Johnnie," Mavity Bence called one day, as Johnnie was passing a strange little cluttered cubbyhole under the garret stairs and out over the roof of the lean-to kitchen.
10068-8{_}1916{_}It was a hybrid apartment, between a large closet and a small room; one four-paned window gave scant light and ventilation; all the broken or disused plunder about the house was pitched into it, and in the middle sat a tumbled bed.
10068-8{_}1917{_}It was the woman's sleeping place and her dead daughter had shared it with her during her lifetime.
10068-8{_}1918{_}Johnnie stopped at the door with a hand on each side of its frame.
10068-8{_}1919{_}"Reddin' up things, Aunt Mavity?"
10068-8{_}1920{_}she asked, adding, "If I had time I'd come in and help you."
10068-8{_}1921{_}"I was just puttin' away what I've got left that belonged to Lou," said the woman, sitting suddenly down on the bed and gazing up into the bright face above her with a sort of appeal.
10068-8{_}1922{_}Johnnie noticed then that Mrs. Bence had a pair of cheap slippers in her lap.
10068-8{_}1923{_}It came back vividly to the girl how the newspapers had said that Louvania Bence had taken off her slippers and left them on the bridge, that she might climb the netting more easily to throw herself into the water.
10068-8{_}1924{_}The mother stared down at these, dry-eyed.
10068-8{_}1925{_}"She never had 'em on but the once," Mavity Bence breathed.
10068-8{_}1926{_}"And I--and I r'ared out on her for buyin' of 'em.
10068-8{_}1927{_}I said that with Pap so old and all, we hadn't money to spend for slippers.
10068-8{_}1928{_}Lord God!"
10068-8{_}1929{_}--she shivered--"We had to find money for the undertaker, when he come to lay her out."
10068-8{_}1930{_}She turned to Johnnie feverishly, like a thing that writhes on the rack and seeks an easier position.
10068-8{_}1931{_}"I had the best for her then--I jest would do it--there was white shoes and stockin's, and a reg'lar shroud like they make at Watauga; we never put a stitch on her that she'd wore--hit was all new-bought.
10068-8{_}1932{_}For once I said my say to Pap, and made him take money out of the bank to do it.
10068-8{_}1933{_}He's got some in thar for to bury all of us--he says--but he never wanted to use any of it for Lou."
10068-8{_}1934{_}Johnnie came in and sat down on the bed beside her hostess.
10068-8{_}1935{_}She laid a loving hand over Mavity's that held the slippers.
10068-8{_}1936{_}"What pretty little feet she must have had," she said softly.
10068-8{_}1937{_}"Didn't she?"
10068-8{_}1938{_}echoed the mother, with a tremulous half-smile.
10068-8{_}1939{_}"I couldn't more'n get these here on my hand, but they was a loose fit for her.
10068-8{_}1940{_}They're as good as new.
10068-8{_}1941{_}Johnnie, ef you ever get a invite to a dance I'll lend 'em to you.
10068-8{_}1942{_}Hit'd pleasure me to think some gal's feet was dancin' in them thar slippers.
10068-8{_}1943{_}Lou, she never learned to dance--looked like she could never find time."
10068-8{_}1944{_}Louvania, be it remembered had found time in which to die.
10068-8{_}1945{_}So Johnnie thanked poor Mavity, and hurried away, because the warning whistle was blowing.
10068-8{_}1946{_}The very next Wednesday Miss Sessions gave a dance to the members of her Uplift Club.
10068-8{_}1947{_}These gaieties were rather singular and ingenious affairs, sterilized dances, Mrs. Hexter irreverently dubbed them.
10068-8{_}1948{_}Miss Lydia did not invite the young men employed about the mill, not having as yet undertaken their uplifting; and feeling quite inadequate to cope with the relations between them and the mill girls, which would be something vital and genuine, and as such, quite foreign--if not inimical--to her enterprise.
10068-8{_}1949{_}She contented herself with bringing in a few well-trained young males of her own class, who were expected to be attentive to the girls, treating them as equals, just as Miss Lydia did.
10068-8{_}1950{_}For the rest, the members were encouraged to dance with each other, and find such joy as they might in the supper, and the fact that Miss Sessions paid for a half-day's work for them on the morrow, that they might lie late in bed after a night's pleasuring.
10068-8{_}1951{_}Johnnie Consadine had begun to earn money in such quantities as seemed to her economic experience extremely large.
10068-8{_}1952{_}She paid her board, sent a little home to her mother, and had still wherewith to buy a frock for the dance.
10068-8{_}1953{_}She treated herself to a trolley ride in to Watauga to select this dress, going on the Saturday half-holiday which the mills gave their workers, lest the labour laws regulating the hours per week which women and children may be employed be infringed upon.
10068-8{_}1954{_}There was grave debate in Johnnie's mind as to what she should buy.
10068-8{_}1955{_}Colours would fade--in cheap goods, anyhow--white soiled easily.
10068-8{_}1956{_}"But then I could wash and iron it myself any evening I wanted to wear it," she argued to Mandy Meacham, who accompanied her.
10068-8{_}1957{_}"I'd be proud to do it for you," returned Mandy, loyally.
10068-8{_}1958{_}Ordinarily the Meacham woman was selfish; but having found an object upon which she could centre her thin, watery affections, she proceeded to be selfish for Johnnie instead of toward her, a spiritual juggle which some mothers perform in regard to their children.
10068-8{_}1959{_}The store reached, Johnnie showed good judgment in her choice.
10068-8{_}1960{_}There was a great sale on at the biggest shopping place in Watauga, and the ready-made summer wear was to be had at bargain rates.
10068-8{_}1961{_}Not for her were the flaring, coarse, scant garments whose lack of seemliness was supposed to be atoned for by a profusion of cheap, sleazy trimming.
10068-8{_}1962{_}After long and somewhat painful inspection, since most of the things she wanted were hopelessly beyond her, Johnnie carried home a fairly fine white lawn, simply tucked, and fitting to perfection.
10068-8{_}1963{_}"But you've got a shape that sets off anything," said the saleswoman, carelessly dealing out the compliments she kept in stock with her goods for purchasers.
10068-8{_}1964{_}"You're mighty right she has," rejoined Mandy, sharply, as who should say, "My back is not a true expression of my desires concerning backs.
10068-8{_}1965{_}Look at this other--she has the spine of my dreams."
10068-8{_}1966{_}The saleswoman chewed gum while they waited for change and parcel, and in the interval she had time to inspect Johnnie more closely.
10068-8{_}1967{_}"Working in the cotton mill, are you?"
10068-8{_}1968{_}she asked as she sorted up her stock, jingling the bracelets on her wrists, and patting into shape her big, frizzy pompadour.
10068-8{_}1969{_}"That's awful hard work, ain't it?
10068-8{_}1970{_}I should think a girl like you would try for a place in a store.
10068-8{_}1971{_}I'll bet you could get one," she added encouragingly, as she handed the parcel across the counter.
10068-8{_}1972{_}But already Johnnie knew that the spurious elegance of this young person's appearance was not what she wished to emulate.
10068-8{_}1973{_}The night of the dance Johnnie adjusted her costume with the nice skill and care which seem native to so many of the daughters of America.
10068-8{_}1974{_}Mandy, dressing at the same bureau, scraggled the parting of her own hair, furtively watching the deft arranging of Johnnie's.
10068-8{_}1975{_}"Let me do it for you, and part it straight," Johnnie remonstrated.
10068-8{_}1976{_}"Aw, hit'll never be seen on a gallopin' hoss," returned Mandy carelessly.
10068-8{_}1977{_}"Everybody'll be so tuck up a-watchin' you that they won't have time to notice is my hair parted straight, nohow."
10068-8{_}1978{_}"But you're not a galloping horse," objected Johnnie, laughing and clutching the comb away from her.
10068-8{_}1979{_}"You've got mighty pretty hair, Mandy, if you'd give it a chance.
10068-8{_}1980{_}Why, it's curly!
10068-8{_}1981{_}Let me do it up right for you once."
10068-8{_}1982{_}So the thin, graying ringlets were loosened around the meagre forehead, and indeed Mandy's appearance was considerably ameliorated.
10068-8{_}1983{_}"There--isn't that nice?"
10068-8{_}1984{_}inquired Johnnie, turning her companion around to the glass and forcing her to gaze in it--a thing Mandy always instinctively avoided.
10068-8{_}1985{_}"I reckon I've looked worse," agreed the tall woman unenthusiastically; "but Miss Lyddy ain't carin' to have ye fix up much.
10068-8{_}1986{_}I get sort of feisty and want to dav-il her by makin' you look pretty.
10068-8{_}1987{_}Wish't you would wear that breas'-pin o' mine, an' them rings an' beads I borried from Lizzie for ye.
10068-8{_}1988{_}You might just as well, and then nobody'd know you from one o' the swells."
10068-8{_}1989{_}Johnnie shook her fair head decidedly.
10068-8{_}1990{_}Talk of borrowing things brought a reminiscent flush to her cheek.
10068-8{_}1991{_}"I'm just as much obliged," she said sweetly.
10068-8{_}1992{_}"I'll wear nothing but what's my own.
10068-8{_}1993{_}After a while I'll be able to afford jewellery, and that'll be the time for me to put it on."
10068-8{_}1994{_}Presently came Mavity Bence bringing the treasured footwear.
10068-8{_}1995{_}"I expect they'll be a little tight for me," Johnnie remarked somewhat doubtfully; the slippers, though cheap, ill-cut things, looked so much smaller than her heavy, country-made shoes.
10068-8{_}1996{_}But they went readily upon the arched feet of the mountain girl, Mandy and the poor mother looking on with deep interest.
10068-8{_}1997{_}"I wish't Lou was here to see you in 'em," whispered Mavity Bence.
10068-8{_}1998{_}"She wouldn't grudge 'em to you one minute.
10068-8{_}1999{_}Lord, how pretty you do look, Johnnie Consadine!
10068-8{_}2000{_}You're as sightly as that thar big wax doll down at the Company store.
10068-8{_}2001{_}I wish't Lou _could_ see you."
10068-8{_}2002{_}The dance was being given in the big hall above a store, which Miss Lydia hired for these functions of her Uplift Club.
10068-8{_}2003{_}The room was half-heartedly decorated in a hybrid fashion.
10068-8{_}2004{_}Miss Lydia had sent down a rose-bowl of flowers; and the girls, being encouraged to use their own taste, put up some flags left over from last Fourth of July.
10068-8{_}2005{_}When Johnnie and Mandy Meacham--strangely assorted pair--entered the long room, festivities were already in progress; Negro fiddlers were reeling off dance music, and Miss Lydia was trying to teach some of her club members the two-step.
10068-8{_}2006{_}Her younger brother, Hartley Sessions, was gravely piloting a girl down the room in what was supposed to be that popular dance, and two young men from Watauga, for whom he had vouched, stood ready for Miss Sessions to furnish them with partners, when she should have encouraged her learners sufficiently to make the attempt.
10068-8{_}2007{_}Round the walls sat the other girls, and to Johnnie's memory came those words of Mandy's, "You dance--if you can."
10068-8{_}2008{_}Johnnie Consadine certainly could dance.
10068-8{_}2009{_}Many a time back in the mountains she had walked five miles after a hard day's work to get to a dance that some one of her mates was giving, tramping home in the dawn and doing without sleep for that twenty-four hours.
10068-8{_}2010{_}The music seemed somehow to get into her muscles, so that she swayed and moved exactly in time to it.
10068-8{_}2011{_}"That's the two-step," she murmured to her partner.
10068-8{_}2012{_}"I never tried it, but I've seen 'em dance it at the hotel down at Chalybeate Springs.
10068-8{_}2013{_}I can waltz a little; but I love an old-fashioned quadrille the best--it seems more friendly."
10068-8{_}2014{_}Gray Stoddard was talking to an older woman who had come with her daughter--a thin-bodied, deep-eyed woman of forty, perhaps, with a half-sad, tolerant smile, and slow, racy speech.
10068-8{_}2015{_}A sudden touch on his shoulder roused him, as one of the young men from town leaned over and asked him excitedly:  "Who's that girl down at the other end of the room, Gray?--the stunning blonde that just came in?
10068-8{_}2016{_}She's got one of the mill girls with her."
10068-8{_}2017{_}Gray looked, and laughed a little.
10068-8{_}2018{_}Somehow the adjectives applied to Johnnie did not please him.
