10068-8{_}3928{_}He stood staring down at his big, shuffling feet, laboriously sorting in his own mind such phrases as it might do to use.
10068-8{_}3929{_}The difficulty of what he had to say blocked speech for so long that Stoddard, in a curiously quiet voice, finally prompted him.
10068-8{_}3930{_}"Tales?"
10068-8{_}3931{_}he repeated.
10068-8{_}3932{_}"What tales, Mr.
10068-8{_}3933{_}Himes?"
10068-8{_}3934{_}"Why, they ain't a old woman in town, nor a young one neither--I believe in my soul that the young ones is the worst--that ain't been talkin'--talkin' bad--ever since you took Johnnie to ride in your otty-mobile."
10068-8{_}3935{_}Again there came a long pause.
10068-8{_}3936{_}Stoddard stared down on Gideon Himes, and Himes stared at his own feet.
10068-8{_}3937{_}"Well?"
10068-8{_}3938{_}Stoddard's quiet voice once more urged his accuser forward.
10068-8{_}3939{_}Pap rolled his head between his shoulders with a negative motion which intimated that it was not well.
10068-8{_}3940{_}"And lending her books, and all sich," he pursued doggedly.
10068-8{_}3941{_}"That kind o' carryin' on ain't decent, and you know it ain't.
10068-8{_}3942{_}Buck knows it ain't--but he's willin' to have her.
10068-8{_}3943{_}He told her he was willin' to have her, and the fool gal let on like she didn't want him.
10068-8{_}3944{_}He came here to board at my house because she wouldn't scarcely so much as speak to him elsewhere."
10068-8{_}3945{_}By the light of these statements Stoddard read what poor Johnnie's persecution had been.
10068-8{_}3946{_}The details of it he could not, of course, know; yet he saw in that moment largely how she had been harried.
10068-8{_}3947{_}At the instant of seeing, came that swift and mighty revulsion that follows surely when we have misprized and misunderstood those dear to us.
10068-8{_}3948{_}"What is it you want of me?"
10068-8{_}3949{_}he inquired of Himes.
10068-8{_}3950{_}"Why, just this here," Pap told him.
10068-8{_}3951{_}"You let Johnnie Consadine alone."
10068-8{_}3952{_}He leaned even closer and spoke in a yet lower tone, because a number of girls were emerging from the house and starting down the steps.
10068-8{_}3953{_}"A big, rich feller like you don't mean any good by a girl fixed the way Johnnie is.
10068-8{_}3954{_}You wouldn't marry her--then let her alone.
10068-8{_}3955{_}Things ain't got so bad but what Buck is still willin' to have her.
10068-8{_}3956{_}You wouldn't marry her."
10068-8{_}3957{_}Stoddard looked down at the shameful old man with eyes that were indecipherable.
10068-8{_}3958{_}If the impulse was strong in him to twist the unclean old throat against any further ill-speaking, it gave no heat to the tone in which he answered:  "It's you and your kind that say I mean harm to Johnnie, and that I would not marry her.
10068-8{_}3959{_}Why should I intend ill toward her?
10068-8{_}3960{_}Why shouldn't I marry her?
10068-8{_}3961{_}I would--I would marry her."
10068-8{_}3962{_}As he made this, to him the only possible defence of the poor girl, Pap faltered slowly back, uttering a gurgling expression of astonishment.
10068-8{_}3963{_}With a sense of surprise Stoddard saw in his face only dismay and chagrin.
10068-8{_}3964{_}"Hit--hit's a lie," Himes mumbled half-heartedly.
10068-8{_}3965{_}"Ye'd never do it in the world."
10068-8{_}3966{_}Stoddard gathered up his bridle rein, preparatory to moving on.
10068-8{_}3967{_}"You're an old man, Mr. Himes," he said coldly, "and you are excited; but you don't want to say any more--that's quite enough of that sort of thing."
10068-8{_}3968{_}Then he loosened the rein on Roan Sultan, and moved away down the street.
10068-8{_}3969{_}Gideon Himes stood and gazed after him with bulging eyes.
10068-8{_}3970{_}Gray Stoddard married to Johnnie!
10068-8{_}3971{_}He tried to adjust his dull wits to the new position of affairs; tried to cipher the problem with this amazing new element introduced.
10068-8{_}3972{_}Last night's scene of violence when the injured child was brought home went dismally before his eyes.
10068-8{_}3973{_}Laurella had said she would leave him so soon as she could put foot to the floor.
10068-8{_}3974{_}He had expected to coax her with gifts and money, with concessions in regard to the children if it must be; but with a rich man for a son-in-law, of course she would go.
10068-8{_}3975{_}He would never see her face again.
10068-8{_}3976{_}And suddenly he flung up an arm like a beaten schoolboy and began to blubbler noisily in the crook of his elbow.
10068-8{_}3977{_}An ungentle hand on his shoulder recalled him to time and place.
10068-8{_}3978{_}"For God's sake, what's the matter with you?"
10068-8{_}3979{_}inquired Shade Buckheath's voice harshly.
10068-8{_}3980{_}The old man gulped down his grief and made his communication in a few hurried sentences.
10068-8{_}3981{_}"An' he'll do it," Pap concluded.
10068-8{_}3982{_}"He's jest big enough fool for anything.
10068-8{_}3983{_}Ain't you heard of his scheme for having the hands make the money in the mill?"
10068-8{_}3984{_}(Thus he described a profit-sharing plan.)
10068-8{_}3985{_}"Don't you know he's given ten thousand dollars to start up some sort o' school for the boys and gals to learn their trade in?
10068-8{_}3986{_}A man like that'll do anything.
10068-8{_}3987{_}And if he marries Johnnie, Laurelly'll leave me sure."
10068-8{_}3988{_}"Leave you!"
10068-8{_}3989{_}echoed Buckheath darkly.
10068-8{_}3990{_}"She won't have to.
10068-8{_}3991{_}If Gray Stoddard marries Johnnie Consadine, you and me will just about roost in the penitentiary for the rest of our days."
10068-8{_}3992{_}"The patent!"
10068-8{_}3993{_}echoed Pap blankly.
10068-8{_}3994{_}He turned fiercely on his fellow conspirator.
10068-8{_}3995{_}"Now see what ye done with yer foolishness," he exclaimed.
10068-8{_}3996{_}"Nothin' would do ye but to be offerin' the contraption for sale, and tellin' each and every that hit'd been used in the Hardwick mill.
10068-8{_}3997{_}Look what a mess ye've made.
10068-8{_}3998{_}I'm sorry I ever hitched up with ye.
10068-8{_}3999{_}Boy o' yo' age has got no sense."
10068-8{_}4000{_}"How was I to know they'd write to Stoddard?"
10068-8{_}4001{_}growled Shade sulkily.
10068-8{_}4002{_}"No harm did if hit wasn't for him.
10068-8{_}4003{_}We've got the patent all right, and Johnnie cain't help herself.
10068-8{_}4004{_}But him--with all his money--he can help her--damn him!"
10068-8{_}4005{_}"Yes, and he'll take a holt and hunt up about Pros's silver mine, too," said Himes.
10068-8{_}4006{_}"I've always mistrusted the way he's been hangin' round Pros Passmore.
10068-8{_}4007{_}Like enough he's hearn of that silver mine, and that's the reason he's after Johnnie."
10068-8{_}4008{_}The old man paused to ruminate on this feature of the case.
10068-8{_}4009{_}He was pleased with his own shrewdness in fathoming Gray Stoddard's mysterious motives.
10068-8{_}4010{_}"Buck," he said finally, with a swift drop to friendliness, "hit's got to be stopped.
10068-8{_}4011{_}Can you stop it?
10068-8{_}4012{_}"Didn't you tell me that Johnnie promised last night to wed you?
10068-8{_}4013{_}Didn't you say she promised it, when you was goin' up to the Victory with her?"
10068-8{_}4014{_}Shade nodded.
10068-8{_}4015{_}"She promised she would if I'd get you to let the children stay out of the mill.
10068-8{_}4016{_}Deanie's hurt now, and you're afraid to make the others go back in the mill anyhow, 'count of Laurelly's tongue.
10068-8{_}4017{_}I can't hold Johnnie to that promise.
10068-8{_}4018{_}But--but there's one person I want to talk to about this business, and then I'll be ready to do something."
10068-8{_}4019{_}CHAPTER XIX  A PACT  While Himes and Buckheath yet stood thus talking, the warning whistles of the various mills began to blow.
10068-8{_}4020{_}Groups of girls came down the steps and stared at the two men conferring with heads close together.
10068-8{_}4021{_}Mavity Bence put her face out at the front door and called.
10068-8{_}4022{_}"Pap, yo' breakfast is gettin' stone cold."
10068-8{_}4023{_}"Do you have to go to the mill right now?"
10068-8{_}4024{_}inquired the older man, timorously.
10068-8{_}4025{_}He was already under the domination of this swifter, bolder, more fiery spirit.
10068-8{_}4026{_}"No, I don't have to go anywhere that I don't want to.
10068-8{_}4027{_}I've got business with a certain party up this-a-way, and when I git to the mill I'll be there."
10068-8{_}4028{_}He turned and hurried swiftly up the minor slope that led to the big Hardwick home, Pap's fascinated eyes following him as long as he was in sight.
10068-8{_}4029{_}As the young fellow strode along he was turning in his mind Lydia Sessions's promise to talk to him this morning about Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4030{_}"But she'll be in bed and asleep, I reckon, at this time of day," he ruminated.
10068-8{_}4031{_}"The good Lord knows I would if I had the chance like she has."
10068-8{_}4032{_}As he came in sight of the Hardwick house, he checked momentarily.
10068-8{_}4033{_}Standing at the gate, an astonishing figure, still in her evening frock, looking haggard and old in the gray, disillusioning light of early morning, was Lydia Sessions.
10068-8{_}4034{_}Upstairs, her white bed was smooth; its pillows spread fair and prim, unpressed by any head, since the maid had settled them trimly in place the morning before; but the long rug which ran from her dressing table to the window might have told a tale of pacing feet that passed restlessly from midnight till dawn; the mirror could have disclosed the picture of a white, anxious, and often angry face that had stared into it as the woman paused now and again to commune with the real Lydia Sessions.
10068-8{_}4035{_}She was thirty and penniless.
10068-8{_}4036{_}She belonged to a circle where everybody had money.
10068-8{_}4037{_}Her sister had married well, and Harriet was no better-looking than she.
10068-8{_}4038{_}All Lydia Sessions's considerable forces were by heredity and training turned into one narrow channel--the effort to make a creditable, if not a brilliant, match.
10068-8{_}4039{_}And she had thought she was succeeding.
10068-8{_}4040{_}Gray Stoddard had seemed seriously interested.
10068-8{_}4041{_}In those long night watches while the lights flared on either side of her mirror, and the luxurious room of a modern young lady lay disclosed, with all its sumptuous fittings of beauty and inutility, Lydia went over her plans of campaign.
10068-8{_}4042{_}She was a suitable match for him--anybody would say so.
10068-8{_}4043{_}He had liked her--he had liked her well enough--till he got interested in this mill girl.
10068-8{_}4044{_}They had never agreed on anything concerning Johnnie Consadine.
10068-8{_}4045{_}If that element were eliminated to-morrow, she knew she could go back and pick up the thread of their intimacy which had promised so well, and, she doubted not at all, twist it safely into a marriage-knot.
10068-8{_}4046{_}If Johnnie were only out of the way.
10068-8{_}4047{_}If she would leave Cottonville.
10068-8{_}4048{_}If she would marry that good-looking mechanic who plainly wanted her.
10068-8{_}4049{_}How silly of her not to take him!
10068-8{_}4050{_}Toward dawn, she snatched a little cape from the garments hanging in the closet, flung it over her shoulders and ran downstairs.
10068-8{_}4051{_}She must have a breath of fresh air.
10068-8{_}4052{_}So, in the manner of helpless creatures who cannot go out in the highway to accost fate, she was standing at the gate when she caught sight of Shade Buckheath approaching.
10068-8{_}4053{_}Here was her opportunity.
10068-8{_}4054{_}She must be doing something, and the nearest enterprise at hand was to foster and encourage this young fellow's pursuit of Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4055{_}"I wanted to talk to you about a very particular matter," she broke out nervously, as soon as Buckheath was near enough to be addressed in the carefully lowered tone which she used throughout the interview.
10068-8{_}4056{_}She continually huddled the light cape together at the neck with tremulous, unsteady fingers; and it was characteristic of these two that, although the woman had heard of the calamity at the Victory mill the night before, and knew that Shade came directly from the Himes home, she made no inquiry as to the welfare of Deanie, and he offered no information.
10068-8{_}4057{_}He gave no reply in words to her accost, and she went on, with increasing agitation.
10068-8{_}4058{_}"I--this matter ought to be attended to at once.
10068-8{_}4059{_}Something's got to be done.
10068-8{_}4060{_}I've attempted to improve the social and spiritual conditions of these girls in the mill, and if I've only worked harm by bringing them in contact with--in contact with--"  She hesitated and stood looking into the man's face.
10068-8{_}4061{_}Buckheath knew exactly what she wished to say.
10068-8{_}4062{_}He was impatient of the flummery she found it necessary to wind around her simple proposition; but he was used to women, he understood them; and to him a woman of Miss Sessions's class was no different from a woman of his own.
10068-8{_}4063{_}"I reckon you wanted to name it to me about Johnnie Consadine," he said bluntly.
10068-8{_}4064{_}"Yes--yes, that was it," breathed Lydia Sessions, glancing back toward the house with a frightened air.
10068-8{_}4065{_}"John is--she's a good girl, Mr. Buckheath; I beg of you to believe me when I assure you that John is a good, honest, upright girl.
10068-8{_}4066{_}I would not think anything else for a minute; but it seems to me that somebody has to do something, or--or--"  Shade raised his hand to his mouth to conceal the swift, sarcastic smile on his lips.
10068-8{_}4067{_}He spat toward the pathside before agreeing seriously with Miss Lydia.
10068-8{_}4068{_}"Her and me was promised, before she come down here and got all this foolishness into her head," he said finally.
10068-8{_}4069{_}"Her mother never could do anything with Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4070{_}Looks like Johnnie's got more authority--her mother's more like a little girl to her than the other way round.
10068-8{_}4071{_}Her uncle Pros has been crazy in the hospital, and Pap Himes, her stepfather--well, I reckon she's the only human that ever had to mind Pap and didn't do it."
10068-8{_}4072{_}This somewhat ambiguous statement of the case failed to bring any smile to his hearer's lips.
10068-8{_}4073{_}"There's no use talking to John herself," Miss Lydia took up the tale feverishly.
10068-8{_}4074{_}"I've done that, and it had no effect on--.
10068-8{_}4075{_}Well, of course she would say that she didn't encourage him to the things I saw afterward; but I know that a man of his sort does not do things without encouragement, and--Mr. Buckheath don't you think you ought to go right to Mr. Stoddard and tell him that John is your promised wife, and show him the folly and--and the wickedness of his course--or what would be wickedness if he persisted in it?
10068-8{_}4076{_}Don't you think you ought to do that?"
10068-8{_}4077{_}Shade held down his head and appeared to be giving this matter some consideration.
10068-8{_}4078{_}The weak point of such an argument lay in the fact that Johnnie was not his promised wife, and Gray Stoddard was very likely to know it.
10068-8{_}4079{_}Indeed, Lydia Sessions herself only believed the statement because she so wished.
10068-8{_}4080{_}"I reckon I ort," he said finally.
10068-8{_}4081{_}"If I could ever get a chance of private speech with him, mebbe I'd--"  There came a sound of light hoofs down the road, and Stoddard on Roan Sultan, riding bareheaded, came toward them under the trees.
10068-8{_}4082{_}Miss Sessions clutched the gate and stood staring.
10068-8{_}4083{_}Buckheath drew a little closer, set his shoulder against the fence and tried to look unconcerned.
10068-8{_}4084{_}The rising sun behind the mountains threw long slant rays across into the bare tree tops, so that the shimmer of it dappled horse and man.
10068-8{_}4085{_}Gray's face was pale, his brow looked anxious; but he rode head up and alert, and glanced with surprise at the two at the Sessions gate.
10068-8{_}4086{_}He had no hat to raise, but he saluted Lydia Sessions with a sweeping gesture of the hand and passed on.
10068-8{_}4087{_}A blithe, gallant figure cantering along the suburban road, out toward the Gap, and the mountains beyond, Gray Stoddard rode into the dip of the ridge and--so far as Cottonville was concerned--vanished utterly.
10068-8{_}4088{_}Buckheath drew a long breath and straightened up.
10068-8{_}4089{_}"I'm but a poor man," he began truculently, "yit there ain't nobody can marry the gal I set out to wed and me stand by and say nothing."
10068-8{_}4090{_}"Oh, Mr.
10068-8{_}4091{_}Buckheath!"
10068-8{_}4092{_}cried Miss Lydia.
10068-8{_}4093{_}"Mr. Stoddard had no idea of _marrying_ John--a mill girl!
10068-8{_}4094{_}There is no possibility of any such thing as that.
10068-8{_}4095{_}I want you to understand that there isn't--to feel assured, once for all.
10068-8{_}4096{_}I have reason to know, and I urge you to put that out of your mind."
10068-8{_}4097{_}Shade looked at her narrowly.
10068-8{_}4098{_}Up to the time Pap gave him definite information from headquarters, he had never for an instant supposed that there was a possibility of Stoddard desiring to marry Johnnie; but the flurried eagerness of Miss Sessions convinced him that such a possibility was a very present dread with her, and he sent a venomous glance after the disappearing horseman.
10068-8{_}4099{_}"You go and talk to him right now, Mr. Buckheath," insisted Lydia anxiously.
10068-8{_}4100{_}"Tell him, just as you have told me, how long you and John have been engaged, and how devoted she was to you before she came down to the mill.
10068-8{_}4101{_}You appeal to him that way.
10068-8{_}4102{_}You can overtake him--I mean you can intercept him--if you start right on now--cut across the turn, and go through the tunnel."
10068-8{_}4103{_}"If I go after him to talk to him, and we--uh--we have an interruption--are you going to tell everybody you see about it?"
10068-8{_}4104{_}demanded Shade sharply, staring down at the woman.
10068-8{_}4105{_}She crouched a little, still clinging to the pickets of the gate.
10068-8{_}4106{_}The word "interruption" only conveyed to her mind the suggestion that they might be interfered with in their conversation.
10068-8{_}4107{_}She did not recollect the mountain use of it to describe a quarrel, an outbreak, or an affray.
10068-8{_}4108{_}"No," she whispered.
10068-8{_}4109{_}"Oh, certainly not--I'll never tell anything that you don't want me to."
10068-8{_}4110{_}"All right," returned Buckheath hardily.
10068-8{_}4111{_}"If you won't, I won't.
10068-8{_}4112{_}If you name to people that I was the last one saw with Mr. Stoddard, I shall have obliged to tell 'em of what you and me was talkin' about when he passed us.
10068-8{_}4113{_}You see that, don't you?"
10068-8{_}4114{_}She nodded silently, her frightened eyes on his face; and without another word he set off at that long, swinging pace which belongs to his people.
10068-8{_}4115{_}Lydia turned and ran swiftly into the house, and up the stairs to her own room.
10068-8{_}4116{_}CHAPTER XX  MISSING  When Stoddard did not come to his desk that morning the matter remained for a time unnoticed, except by McPherson, who fretted a bit at so unusual a happening.
10068-8{_}4117{_}Truth to tell, the old Scotchman had dreaded having this rich young man for an associate, and had put a rod in pickle for his chastisement.
10068-8{_}4118{_}When Stoddard turned out to be a regular worker, punctual, amenable to discipline, he congratulated himself, and praised his assistant, but warily.
10068-8{_}4119{_}Now came the first delinquency, and in his heart he cared more that Stoddard should absent himself without notice than for the pile of letters lying untouched.
10068-8{_}4120{_}"Dave," he finally said to the yellow office boy, "I wish you'd 'phone to Mr. Stoddard's place and see when he'll be down."
10068-8{_}4121{_}Dave came back with the information that Mr. Stoddard was not at the house; he had left for an early-morning ride, and not returned to his breakfast.
10068-8{_}4122{_}"He'll just about have stopped up at the Country Club for a snack," MacPherson muttered to himself.
10068-8{_}4123{_}"I wonder who or what he found there attractive enough to keep him from his work."
10068-8{_}4124{_}Looking into Gray's office at noon, the closed desk with its pile of mail once more offended MacPherson's eye.
10068-8{_}4125{_}"Mr. Stoddard here?"
10068-8{_}4126{_}inquired Hartley Sessions, glancing in at the same moment.
10068-8{_}4127{_}"No, I think not," returned the Scotchman, unwilling to admit that he did not exactly know.
10068-8{_}4128{_}"I believe he's up at the club.
10068-8{_}4129{_}Perhaps he's got tangled in for a longer game of golf than he reckoned on."
10068-8{_}4130{_}This unintentional and wholly innocent falsehood stopped any inquiry that there might have been.
10068-8{_}4131{_}MacPherson had meant to 'phone the club during the day, but he failed to do so, and it was not until evening that he walked up himself to put more cautious inquiries.
10068-8{_}4132{_}"No, sah--no, sah, Mr. Gray ain't been here," the Negro steward told him promptly.
10068-8{_}4133{_}"I sure would have remembered, sah," in answer to a startled inquiry from MacPherson.
10068-8{_}4134{_}"Dey been havin' a big game on between Mr. Charley Conroy and Mr. Hardwick, and de bofe of 'em spoke of Mr. Gray, and said dey was expectin' him to play."
10068-8{_}4135{_}MacPherson came down the stone steps of the clubhouse, gravely disquieted.
10068-8{_}4136{_}Below him the road wound, a dimly conjectured, wavering gray ribbon; on the other side of it the steep slope took off to a gulf of inky shadow, where the great valley lay, hushed under the solemn stars, silent, black, and shimmering with a myriad pulsating electric lights which glowed like swarms of fireflies caught in an invisible net.
10068-8{_}4137{_}That was Watauga.
10068-8{_}4138{_}The strings of brilliants that led from it were arc lights at switch crossings where the great railway lines rayed out.
10068-8{_}4139{_}Near at hand was Cottonville with its vast bulks of lighted mills whose hum came faintly up to him even at this distance.
10068-8{_}4140{_}MacPherson stood uncertainly in the middle of the road.
10068-8{_}4141{_}Supper and bed were behind him.
10068-8{_}4142{_}But he had not the heart to turn back to either.
10068-8{_}4143{_}Somewhere down in that abyss of night, there was a clue--or there were many clues--to this strange absence of Gray Stoddard.
10068-8{_}4144{_}Perhaps Gray himself was there; and the Scotchman cursed his own dilatoriness in waiting till darkness had covered the earth before setting afoot inquiries.
10068-8{_}4145{_}He found himself hurrying and getting out of breath as he took his way down the ridge and straight to Stoddard's cottage, only to find that the master's horse was not in the stable, and the Negro boy who cared for it had seen nothing of it or its rider since five o'clock that morning.
10068-8{_}4146{_}"I wonder, now, should I give the alarm to Hardwick," MacPherson said to himself.
10068-8{_}4147{_}"The lad may have just ridden on to La Fayette, or some little nearby town, and be staying the night.
10068-8{_}4148{_}Young fellows sometimes have affairs they'd rather not share with everybody--and then, there's Miss Lydia.
10068-8{_}4149{_}If I go up to Hardwick's with the story, she'll be sure to hear it from Hardwick's wife."
10068-8{_}4150{_}"Did Mr. Stoddard ever go away like this before without giving you notice?"
10068-8{_}4151{_}he asked with apparent carelessness.
10068-8{_}4152{_}The boy shook his head in vigorous negative.
10068-8{_}4153{_}"Never since I've been working for him," he asserted.
10068-8{_}4154{_}"Mr. Stoddard wasn't starting anywhere but for his early ride--at least he wasn't intending to.
10068-8{_}4155{_}He hadn't any hat on, and he was in his riding clothes.
10068-8{_}4156{_}He didn't carry anything with him.
10068-8{_}4157{_}I know in reason he wasn't intending to stay."
10068-8{_}4158{_}This information sent MacPherson hurrying to the Hardwick home.
10068-8{_}4159{_}Dinner was over.
10068-8{_}4160{_}The master of the house conferred with him a moment in the vestibule, then opened the door into the little sitting room and asked abruptly:  "When was the last time any of you saw Gray Stoddard?"
10068-8{_}4161{_}His sister-in-law screamed faintly, then cowered in her chair and stared at him mutely.
10068-8{_}4162{_}But Mrs. Hardwick as yet noted nothing unusual.
10068-8{_}4163{_}"Yesterday evening," she returned placidly.
10068-8{_}4164{_}"Don't you remember, Jerome, he was here at the Lyric reception?"
10068-8{_}4165{_}"Oh, I remember well enough," said Hardwick knitting his brows.
10068-8{_}4166{_}"I thought some of you might have seen him since then.
10068-8{_}4167{_}He's missing."
10068-8{_}4168{_}"Missing!"
10068-8{_}4169{_}echoed Lydia Sessions with a note of terror in her tones.
10068-8{_}4170{_}Now Mrs. Hardwick looked startled.
10068-8{_}4171{_}"But, Jerome, I think you're inconsiderate," she began, glancing solicitously at her sister.
10068-8{_}4172{_}"Under the circumstances, it seems to me you might have made your announcement more gently--to Lydia, anyhow.
10068-8{_}4173{_}Never mind, dearie--there's nothing in it to be frightened at."
10068-8{_}4174{_}"I'm not frightened," whispered Lydia Sessions through white lips that belied her assertion.
10068-8{_}4175{_}Hardwick looked impatiently from his sister-in-law to his wife.
10068-8{_}4176{_}"I'm sorry if I startled you, Lydia," he said in a perfunctory tone, "but this is a serious business.
10068-8{_}4177{_}MacPherson tells me Stoddard hasn't been at the factory nor at his boarding-house to-day.
10068-8{_}4178{_}The last person who saw him, so far as we know, is his stable boy.
10068-8{_}4179{_}Black Jim says Stoddard rode out of the gate at five o'clock this morning, bareheaded and in his riding clothes.
10068-8{_}4180{_}Have any of you seen him since--that's what I want to know?"
10068-8{_}4181{_}"Since?"
10068-8{_}4182{_}repeated Miss Sessions, who seemed unable to get beyond the parrot echoing of her questioner's words.
10068-8{_}4183{_}"Why Jerome, what makes you think I've seen him since then?
10068-8{_}4184{_}Did he say--did anybody tell you--"  She broke off huskily and sat staring at her interlaced fingers dropped in her lap.
10068-8{_}4185{_}"No--no.
10068-8{_}4186{_}Of course not, Lydia," her sister hastened to reassure her, crossing the room and putting a protecting arm about the girl's shoulders.
10068-8{_}4187{_}"He shouldn't have spoken as he did, knowing that you and Gray--knowing how affairs stand."
10068-8{_}4188{_}"Well, I only thought since you and Stoddard are such great friends," Hardwick persisted, "he might have mentioned to you some excursion, or made opportunity to talk with you alone, sometime last night--to--to say something.
10068-8{_}4189{_}Did he tell you where he was going, Lydia?
10068-8{_}4190{_}Are you keeping something from us that we ought to know?
10068-8{_}4191{_}Remember this is no child's play.
10068-8{_}4192{_}It begins to look as though it might be a question of the man's life."
10068-8{_}4193{_}Lydia Sessions started galvanically.
10068-8{_}4194{_}She pushed off her sister's caressing hand with a fierce gesture.
10068-8{_}4195{_}"There's nothing--no such relation as you're hinting at, Elizabeth, between Gray Stoddard and me," she said sharply.
10068-8{_}4196{_}Memory of what Gray had (as she supposed) followed her into the library to say to her wrung a sort of groan from the girl.
10068-8{_}4197{_}"I suppose Matilda's told you that we had--had some conversation in the library," she managed to say.
10068-8{_}4198{_}Her brother-in-law shook his head.
10068-8{_}4199{_}"We haven't questioned the servants yet," he said briefly.
10068-8{_}4200{_}"We haven't questioned anybody nor hunted up any evidence.
10068-8{_}4201{_}MacPherson came direct to me from Stoddard's stable boy.
10068-8{_}4202{_}Gray did stop and talk to you last night?
10068-8{_}4203{_}What did he say?"
10068-8{_}4204{_}"I--why nothing in--I really don't remember," faltered Lydia, with so strange a look that both her sister and Hardwick looked at her in surprise.
10068-8{_}4205{_}"That is--oh, nothing of any importance, you know.
10068-8{_}4206{_}I--I believe we were talking about socialism, and--and different classes of people.... That sort of thing."
10068-8{_}4207{_}MacPherson, who had pushed unceremoniously into the room behind his employer, nodded his gray head.
10068-8{_}4208{_}"That would always be what he was speaking of."
10068-8{_}4209{_}He smiled a little as he said it.
10068-8{_}4210{_}"All right," returned Hardwick, struggling into his overcoat at the hat-tree, and seeking his hat and stick, "I'll go right back with you, Mac.
10068-8{_}4211{_}This thing somehow has a sinister look to me."
10068-8{_}4212{_}As the two men were leaving the house, Hardwick felt a light, trembling touch on his arm, and turned to face his sister-in-law.
10068-8{_}4213{_}"Why--Jerome, why did you say that last?"
10068-8{_}4214{_}Lydia quavered.
10068-8{_}4215{_}"What do you think has happened to him?
10068-8{_}4216{_}Do you think anybody--that is--?
10068-8{_}4217{_}Oh, you looked at me as though you thought I had something to do with it!"
10068-8{_}4218{_}"Come, come, Lyd.
10068-8{_}4219{_}Pull yourself together.
10068-8{_}4220{_}You're getting hysterical," urged Hardwick kindly.
10068-8{_}4221{_}Then he turned to MacPherson.
10068-8{_}4222{_}As the two men went companionably down the walk and out into the street, the Scotchman said apologetically:  "Of course, I knew Miss Lydia would be alarmed.
10068-8{_}4223{_}I understand about her and Stoddard.
10068-8{_}4224{_}It made me hesitate a while before coming up to you folks with the thing."
10068-8{_}4225{_}"Well, by the Lord, you did well not to hesitate too long, Mac!"
10068-8{_}4226{_}ejaculated Hardwick.
10068-8{_}4227{_}"I shouldn't feel the anxiety I do if we hadn't been having trouble with those mountain people up toward Flat Rock over that girl that died at the hospital."
10068-8{_}4228{_}He laughed a little ruefully.
10068-8{_}4229{_}"Trying to do things for folks is ticklish business.
10068-8{_}4230{_}There wasn't a man in the crowd that interviewed me whom I could convince that our hospital wasn't a factory for the making of stiffs which we sold to the Northern Medical College.
10068-8{_}4231{_}Oh, it was gruesome!
10068-8{_}4232{_}"I told them the girl had had every attention, and that she died of pernicious anaemia.
10068-8{_}4233{_}They called it 'a big dic word' and asked me point blank if the girl hadn't been killed in the mill.
10068-8{_}4234{_}I told them that we couldn't keep the body indefinitely, and they said they 'aimed to come and haul it away as soon as they could get a horse and wagon.'
10068-8{_}4235{_}I called their attention to the fact that I couldn't know this unless they wrote and told me so in answer to my letter.
10068-8{_}4236{_}But between you and me, Mac, I don't believe there was a man in the crowd who could read or write."
10068-8{_}4237{_}"For God's sake!"
10068-8{_}4238{_}exclaimed the Scotchman.
10068-8{_}4239{_}"You don't think _those_ people were up to doing a mischief to Stoddard, do you?"
10068-8{_}4240{_}"I don't know what to think," protested Hardwick.
10068-8{_}4241{_}"Yes; they are mediaeval--half savage.
10068-8{_}4242{_}The fact is, I have no idea what they would or what they wouldn't do."
10068-8{_}4243{_}MacPherson gave a whistle of dismay.
10068-8{_}4244{_}"Gad, it sounds like the manoeuvres of one of our Highland clans three hundred years ago!"
10068-8{_}4245{_}he said.
10068-8{_}4246{_}"Wouldn't it be the irony of fate that Stoddard--poor fellow!--a friend of the people, a socialist, ready to call every man his brother--should be sacrificed in such a way?"
10068-8{_}4247{_}The words brought them to Stoddard's little home, silent and deserted now.
10068-8{_}4248{_}Down the street, the lamps flared gustily.
10068-8{_}4249{_}It was after eleven o'clock.
10068-8{_}4250{_}"Where does that boy live that takes care of the horses--black Jim?"
10068-8{_}4251{_}Hardwick inquired, after they had rung the bell, thumped on the door, and called, to make sure the master had not returned during MacPherson's absence.
10068-8{_}4252{_}"I don't know--really, I don't know.
10068-8{_}4253{_}He might have a room over the stable," MacPherson suggested.
10068-8{_}4254{_}But the stable proved to be a one-story affair, and they were just turning to leave when a stamping sound within arrested their notice.
10068-8{_}4255{_}"Good God!--what's that?"
10068-8{_}4256{_}ejaculated MacPherson, whose nerves were quivering.
10068-8{_}4257{_}"It's the horse," answered Hardwick in a relieved tone.
10068-8{_}4258{_}"Stoddard's got back--"  "Of course," broke in old MacPherson, quickly, "and gone over to Mrs. Gandish's for some supper.
10068-8{_}4259{_}That is why he wasn't in the house."
10068-8{_}4260{_}To make assurance doubly sure, they opened the unlocked stable door, and MacPherson struck a match.
10068-8{_}4261{_}The roan turned and whinnied hungrily at sight of them.
10068-8{_}4262{_}"That's funny," said Hardwick, scarcely above his breath.
10068-8{_}4263{_}"It looks to me as though that animal hadn't been fed."
10068-8{_}4264{_}In the flare of the match MacPherson had descried the stable lantern hanging on the wall.
10068-8{_}4265{_}They lit this and examined the stall.
10068-8{_}4266{_}There was no feed in the box, no hay in the manger.
10068-8{_}4267{_}The saddle was on Gray Stoddard's horse; the bit in his mouth; he was tied by the reins to his stall ring.
10068-8{_}4268{_}The two men looked at each other with lengthening faces.
10068-8{_}4269{_}"Stoddard's too good a horseman to have done that," spoke Hardwick slowly.
10068-8{_}4270{_}"And too kind a man," supplied MacPherson loyally.
10068-8{_}4271{_}"He'd have seen to the beast's hunger before he satisfied his own."
10068-8{_}4272{_}As the Scotchman spoke he was picking up the horse's hoofs, and digging at them with a bit of stick.
10068-8{_}4273{_}"They're as clean as if they'd just been washed," he said, as he straightened up.
10068-8{_}4274{_}"By Heaven!
10068-8{_}4275{_}I have it, Hardwick--that fellow came into town with his hoofs muffled."
10068-8{_}4276{_}The younger man looked also, and assented mutely, then suggested:  "He hasn't come far; there's not a hair turned on him."
10068-8{_}4277{_}The Scotchman shook his head.
10068-8{_}4278{_}"I'm not sure of that," he debated.
10068-8{_}4279{_}"Likely he's been led, and that slowly.
10068-8{_}4280{_}God--this is horrible!"
10068-8{_}4281{_}Mechanically Hardwick got some hay down for the horse, while MacPherson pulled off the saddle and bridle, examining both in the process.
10068-8{_}4282{_}Grain was poured into the box, and then water offered.
10068-8{_}4283{_}"He won't drink," murmured the Scotchman.
10068-8{_}4284{_}"D'ye see, Hardwick?
10068-8{_}4285{_}He won't drink.
10068-8{_}4286{_}You can't come into Cottonville without crossing a stream.
10068-8{_}4287{_}This fellow's hoofs have been wet within an hour--yes, within the half-hour."
10068-8{_}4288{_}As their eyes encountered, Hardwick caught his breath sharply; both felt that chill of the cuticle, that stirring at the roots of the hair, that marks the passing close to us of some sinister thing--stark murder, or man's naked hatred walking in the dark beside our cheerful, commonplace path.
10068-8{_}4289{_}By one consent they turned back from the stable and went together to Mrs. Gandish's.
10068-8{_}4290{_}The house was dark.
10068-8{_}4291{_}"Of course, you know I don't expect to find him here," said Hardwick.
10068-8{_}4292{_}"I don't suppose they know anything about the matter.
10068-8{_}4293{_}But we've got to wake them and ask."
10068-8{_}4294{_}They did so, and set trembling the first wave of that widening ring of horror which finally informed the remotest boundaries of the little village that a man from their midst was mysteriously missing.
10068-8{_}4295{_}The morning found the telegraph in active requisition, flashing up and down all lines by which a man might have left Cottonville or Watauga.
10068-8{_}4296{_}The police of the latter place were notified, furnished with information, and set to find out if possible whether anybody in the city had seen Stoddard since he rode away on Friday morning.
10068-8{_}4297{_}The inquiries were fruitless.
10068-8{_}4298{_}A young lady visiting in the city had promised him a dance at the Valentine masque to be held at the Country Club-house Friday night.
10068-8{_}4299{_}Some clothing put out a few days before to be cleaned and pressed was ready for delivery.
10068-8{_}4300{_}His laundry came home.
10068-8{_}4301{_}His mail arrived punctually.
10068-8{_}4302{_}The postmaster stated that he had no instructions for a change of address; all the little accessories of Gray Stoddard's life offered themselves, mute, impressive witnesses that he had intended to go on with it in Cottonville.
10068-8{_}4303{_}But Stoddard himself had dropped as completely out of the knowledge of man as though he had been whisked off the planet.
10068-8{_}4304{_}CHAPTER XXI  THE SEARCH  The fruitless search was vigorously prosecuted.
10068-8{_}4305{_}On Saturday the Hardwick mill ran short-handed while nearly half its male employees made some effort to solve the mystery.
10068-8{_}4306{_}Parties combed again and again the nearer mountains.
10068-8{_}4307{_}Sunday all the mill operatives were free; and then groups of women and children added themselves to the men; dinners were taken along, lending a grotesque suggestion of picnicking to the work, a suggestion contradicted by the anxious faces, the strained timbre of the voices that called from group to group.
10068-8{_}4308{_}But night brought the amateur searchers straggling home with nothing to tell.
10068-8{_}4309{_}It should have been significant to any one who knew the mountain people, that information concerning Gray Stoddard within a week of his disappearance, was noticeably lacking.
10068-8{_}4310{_}Nobody would admit that his had been a familiar figure on those roads.
10068-8{_}4311{_}At the utmost they had "seed him a good deal a while ago, but he'd sorter quit riding up this-a-way of late."
10068-8{_}4312{_}But on no road could there be found man, woman, or child who had seen Gray Stoddard riding Friday morning on his roan horse.
10068-8{_}4313{_}The whole outlying district seemed to be in a conspiracy of silence.
10068-8{_}4314{_}In Watauga and in Cottonville itself, clues were found by the police, followed up and proved worthless.
10068-8{_}4315{_}All Gray's Eastern connections were immediately communicated with by telegraph, in the forlorn hope of finding some internal clue.
10068-8{_}4316{_}The business men in charge of his large Eastern interests answered promptly that nothing from recent correspondence with him pointed to any intention on his part of making a journey or otherwise changing his ordinary way of living.
10068-8{_}4317{_}They added urgent admonitions to Mr. MacPherson to have locked up in the Company's safe various important papers which they had sent, at Stoddard's request, for signature, and which they supposed from the date, must be lying with his other mail.
10068-8{_}4318{_}A boyhood friend telegraphed his intention of coming down from Massachusetts and joining the searchers.
10068-8{_}4319{_}Stoddard had no near relatives.
10068-8{_}4320{_}A grand-aunt, living in Boston, telegraphed to Mr. Hardwick to see that money be spent freely.
10068-8{_}4321{_}Meantime there was reason for Johnnie Consadine, shut in the little sister's sick room day and night, to hear nothing of these matters.
10068-8{_}4322{_}Lissy had been allowed to help wait upon the injured child only on promise that nothing exciting should be mentioned.
10068-8{_}4323{_}Both boys had instantly begged to join a searching party, Milo insisting that he could work all night and search all day, and that nobody should complain that he neglected his job.
10068-8{_}4324{_}Pony, being refused, had run away; Milo the rulable followed to get him to return; and by Sunday night Mavity was feeding both boys from the back door and keeping them out of sight of Pap's vengeance.
10068-8{_}4325{_}Considering that Johnnie had trouble enough, she cautioned everybody on the place to say nothing of these matters to the girl.
10068-8{_}4326{_}Mandy, a feeble, unsound creature at best, was more severely injured than had been thought.
10068-8{_}4327{_}She was confined to her bed for days.
10068-8{_}4328{_}Pap went about somewhat like a whipped dog, spoke little on any subject, and tolerated no mention of the topic of the day in Cottonville; his face kept the boarders quiet at table and in the house, anyhow.
10068-8{_}4329{_}Shade Buckheath never entered the place after Deanie was carried in from the hastily summoned carriage Thursday night.
10068-8{_}4330{_}The doctors told them that if Deanie survived the shock and its violent reaction, she had a fair chance of recovery.
10068-8{_}4331{_}They found at once that she was not internally injured; the blood that had been seen came only from a cut lip.
10068-8{_}4332{_}But the child's left arm was broken, the small body was dreadfully bruised, and the terror had left a profound mental disturbance.
10068-8{_}4333{_}Nothing but quiet and careful nursing offered any good hope; while there was the menace that she would never be strong again, and might not live to womanhood.
10068-8{_}4334{_}At first she lay with half-closed, glazed eyes, barely breathing, a ghastly sight.
10068-8{_}4335{_}Then, when she roused a bit, she wanted, not Lissy, not even Johnnie; she called for her mother.
10068-8{_}4336{_}When her child was brought home to her, dying as they all thought, Laurella had rallied her forces and got up from the pallet on which she lay to tend on the little thing; but she broke down in the course of a few hours, and seemed about to add another patient to Johnnie's cares.
10068-8{_}4337{_}Yet when the paroxysms of terror shook the emaciated frame, and the others attempted to reassure Deanie by words, it was her mother who called for a bit of gay calico, for scissors and needle and thread, and began dressing a doll in the little sufferer's sight.
10068-8{_}4338{_}Laurella had carried unspoiled the faculty for play, up with her through the years.
10068-8{_}4339{_}"Let her be," the doctor counselled Johnnie, in reply to anxious inquiries.
10068-8{_}4340{_}"Don't you see she's getting the child's attention?
10068-8{_}4341{_}The baby notices.
10068-8{_}4342{_}An ounce of happiness is worth a pound of any medicine I could bring."
10068-8{_}4343{_}And so, when Laurella could no longer sit up, they brought another cot for her, and she lay all day babbling childish nonsense, and playing dolls within hand-reach of the sick-bed; while Johnnie with Lissy's help, tended on them both.
10068-8{_}4344{_}"You've got two babies now, you big, old, solemn Johnnie," Laurella said, with a ghost of her sparkling smile.
10068-8{_}4345{_}"Deanie and me is just of one age, and that's a fact."
10068-8{_}4346{_}If Pap wanted to see his young wife--and thirst for a sight of her was a continual craving with him; she was the light of the old sinner's eyes--he had to go in and look on the child he had injured.
10068-8{_}4347{_}This kept him away pretty effectually after that first fiery scene, when Laurella had flown at him like a fierce little vixen and told him that she never wanted to see his face again, that she rued the day she married him, and intended to leave him as soon as she could put foot to the ground.
10068-8{_}4348{_}In the gray dawn of Monday morning, when Johnnie was downstairs eating her bit of early breakfast, Pap shambled in to make Laurella's fire.
10068-8{_}4349{_}Having got the hickory wood to blazing, he sat humped and shame-faced by the bedside a while, whispering to his wife and holding her hand, a sight for the student of man to marvel at.
10068-8{_}4350{_}He had brought a paper of coarse, cheap candy for Deanie, but the child was asleep.
10068-8{_}4351{_}The offering was quite as acceptable to Laurella, and she nibbled a stick as she listened to him.
10068-8{_}4352{_}The bald head with its little fringe of grizzled curls, bent close to the dark, slant-browed, lustrous-eyed, mutinous countenance; Pap whispered hoarsely for some time, Laurella replying at first in a sort of languid tolerance, but presently with little ejaculations of wonder and dismay.
10068-8{_}4353{_}A step on the stair which he took to be Johnnie's put Himes to instant flight.
10068-8{_}4354{_}"I've got to go honey," he breathed huskily.
10068-8{_}4355{_}"Cain't you say you forgive me before I leave?
10068-8{_}4356{_}I know I ain't fitten fer the likes of you; but when I come back from this here raid I'm a-goin' to take some money out of the bank and git you whatever you want.
10068-8{_}4357{_}Look-a-here; see what I've done," and he showed a little book in his hand, and what he had written in it.
10068-8{_}4358{_}"Oh--I forgive you, if that's any account to you," returned Laurella with kindly contempt.
10068-8{_}4359{_}"I never noticed that forgiving things undid the harm any; but--yes--oh, of course I forgive you.
10068-8{_}4360{_}Go along; I'm tired now.
10068-8{_}4361{_}Don't bother me any more, Gid; I want to sleep."
10068-8{_}4362{_}The old man thrust the treasured bankbook under Laurella's pillow, and hurried away.
10068-8{_}4363{_}Downstairs in the dining room Johnnie was eating her breakfast.
10068-8{_}4364{_}"Johnnie," said Mavity Bence, keeping behind the girl's chair as she served the meal to her at the end of the long table, "I ain't never done you a meanness yet, have I?
10068-8{_}4365{_}And you know I've got all the good will in the world toward you--now don't you?"
10068-8{_}4366{_}"Why, of course, Aunt Mavity," returned Johnnie wonderingly, trying to get sight of the older woman's face.
10068-8{_}4367{_}Mrs. Bence took a plate and hurried out for more biscuits.
10068-8{_}4368{_}She came back with some resolution plainly renewed in her mind.
10068-8{_}4369{_}"Johnnie," she began once more, "there's something I've got to tell you.
10068-8{_}4370{_}Your Uncle Pros has got away from 'em up at the hospital, and to the hills, and--and--I have obliged to tell you."
10068-8{_}4371{_}"Yes, I know," returned Johnnie passively.
10068-8{_}4372{_}"They sent me word last night.
10068-8{_}4373{_}I'm sorry, but I can't do anything about it.
10068-8{_}4374{_}Maybe he won't come to any harm out that way.
10068-8{_}4375{_}I can't imagine Uncle Pros hurting anybody.
10068-8{_}4376{_}Perhaps it will do him good."
10068-8{_}4377{_}"Hit wasn't about your Uncle Pros that I was meaning.
10068-8{_}4378{_}At least not about his gettin' away from the hospital," amended Mavity.
10068-8{_}4379{_}"It was about the day he got hurt here.
10068-8{_}4380{_}I--I always aimed to tell you.
10068-8{_}4381{_}I know I ort to have done it.
10068-8{_}4382{_}I was always a-goin' to, and then--Pap--he--"  She broke off and stood silent so long that Johnnie turned and looked at her.
10068-8{_}4383{_}"Surely you aren't afraid of me, Aunt Mavity," she said finally.
10068-8{_}4384{_}"No," said Mavity Bence in a low voice, "but I'm scared of--the others."
10068-8{_}4385{_}The girl stared at her curiously.
10068-8{_}4386{_}"Johnnie," burst out the woman for the third time, "yo' Uncle Pros found his silver mine!
10068-8{_}4387{_}Oh, yes, he did; and Pap's got his pieces of ore upstairs in a bandanner; and him and Shade Buckheath aims to git it away from you-all and--oh, I don't know what!"
10068-8{_}4388{_}There fell a long silence.
10068-8{_}4389{_}At last Johnnie's voice broke it, asking very low:  "Did they--how was Uncle Pros hurt?"
10068-8{_}4390{_}"Neither of 'em touched him," Mavity hastened to assure her.
10068-8{_}4391{_}"He heard 'em name it how they'd get the mine from him--or thought he did--and he come out and talked loud, and grabbed for the bandanner, and he missed it and fell down the steps.
10068-8{_}4392{_}He wasn't crazy when he come to the house.
10068-8{_}4393{_}He was jest plumb wore out, and his head was hurt.
10068-8{_}4394{_}He called it yo' silver mine.
10068-8{_}4395{_}He said he had to put the bandanner in yo' lap and tell you hit was for you."
10068-8{_}4396{_}Johnny got suddenly to her feet.
10068-8{_}4397{_}"Thank you, Aunt Mavity," she said kindly.
10068-8{_}4398{_}"This is what's been troubling you, is it?
10068-8{_}4399{_}Don't worry any more, I'll see about this, somehow.
10068-8{_}4400{_}I must go back to Mother now."
10068-8{_}4401{_}Laurella had said to Pap Himes that she wanted to sleep, and indeed her eyes, were closed when Johnnie entered the room; but beneath the shadow of the sweeping lashes burned such spots of crimson that her nurse was alarmed.
10068-8{_}4402{_}"What was Pap Himes saying to you to get you so excited?"
10068-8{_}4403{_}she asked anxiously.
10068-8{_}4404{_}"Johnnie, come here.
10068-8{_}4405{_}Sit down on the edge of the bed and listen to me," demanded Laurella feverishly.
10068-8{_}4406{_}She laid hold of her daughter's arm, and half pulled herself up by it, staring into Johnnie's face as she talked; and out tumbled the whole story of Gray Stoddard's disappearance.
10068-8{_}4407{_}As full understanding of what her mother said came home to Johnnie, her eyes dilated in her pale face.
10068-8{_}4408{_}She sank to her knees beside the bed.
10068-8{_}4409{_}"Lost!"
10068-8{_}4410{_}she echoed.
10068-8{_}4411{_}"Lost--gone!
10068-8{_}4412{_}Hasn't been seen since Friday morning--Friday morning before sunup!
10068-8{_}4413{_}Friday, Saturday, Sunday.
10068-8{_}4414{_}My God, Mother--it's three days and three nights!"
10068-8{_}4415{_}"Yes, honey, it's three days and three nights," assented Laurella fearfully.
10068-8{_}4416{_}"Gid says he's going up in the mountains with a lot of others to search.
10068-8{_}4417{_}He says some thinks the moonshiners have taken him in mistake for a revenuer; and some believe it was robbery--for his watch and money; and Mr. Hardwick is blaming it on the Groner crowd that raised up such a fuss when Lura Dawson died in the hospital here.
10068-8{_}4418{_}Gid says they've searched every ridge and valley this side of Big Unaka.
10068-8{_}4419{_}He--Johnnie, he says _he_ believes Mr. Stoddard suicided."
10068-8{_}4420{_}[Illustration: "LOST--GONE!
10068-8{_}4421{_}MY GOD, MOTHER--IT'S THREE DAYS AND THREE NIGHTS!"]
10068-8{_}4422{_}"Where is Shade Buckheath?"
10068-8{_}4423{_}whispered Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4424{_}"Shade's been out with mighty nigh every crowd that went," Laurella told her.
10068-8{_}4425{_}"Mr. Hardwick pays them wages, just the same as if they were in the mill.
10068-8{_}4426{_}Shade's going with Gid this morning, in Mr. Stoddard's automobile."
10068-8{_}4427{_}"Are they gone--oh, are they gone?"
10068-8{_}4428{_}Johnnie sprang to her feet in dismay, and stood staring a moment.
10068-8{_}4429{_}Then swiftly she bent once more over the little woman in the bed.
10068-8{_}4430{_}"Mother," she said before Laurella could speak or answer her, "Aunt Mavity can wait on you and Deanie for a little while--with what help Lissy will give you--can't she, honey?
10068-8{_}4431{_}And Mandy was coming downstairs to her breakfast this morning--she's able to be afoot now--and I know she'll be wanting to help tend on Deanie.
10068-8{_}4432{_}You could get along for a spell without me--don't you think you could?
10068-8{_}4433{_}Honey," she spoke desperately.
10068-8{_}4434{_}"I've just got to find Shade Buckheath--I must see him."
10068-8{_}4435{_}"Sure, we'll get along all right, Johnnie," Laurella put in eagerly.
10068-8{_}4436{_}She tugged at a corner of the pillow, fumbled thereunder with her little brown hand, and dragging out Pap Himes's bankbook, showed it to her daughter, opening at that front page where Pap's clumsy characters made Laurella Himes free of all his savings.
10068-8{_}4437{_}"You go right along, Johnnie, and see cain't you help about Mr. Stoddard.
10068-8{_}4438{_}Looks like I cain't bear to think ... the pore boy ... you go on--me and Deanie'll be all right till you get back."
10068-8{_}4439{_}Johnnie stooped and kissed the cheek with its feverish flush.
10068-8{_}4440{_}"Good-bye, Mommie," she whispered hurriedly.
10068-8{_}4441{_}"Don't worry about me.
10068-8{_}4442{_}I'll be back--.
10068-8{_}4443{_}Well, don't worry.
10068-8{_}4444{_}Good-bye."
10068-8{_}4445{_}She snatched a coat and hat, and, going out, closed the door quietly behind her.
10068-8{_}4446{_}She stepped out into the dancing sunlight of an early spring morning.
10068-8{_}4447{_}The leafless vine on Mavity Bence's porch rattled dry stems against the lattice work in a gay March wind.
10068-8{_}4448{_}Taking counsel with herself for a moment, she started swiftly down the street in the direction of the mills.
10068-8{_}4449{_}In the office they told her that Mr. Hardwick had gone to Nashville to see about getting bloodhounds; MacPherson was following his own plan of search in Watauga.
10068-8{_}4450{_}She was permitted to go down into the mechanical department and ask the head of it about Shade Buckheath.
10068-8{_}4451{_}"No, he ain't here," Mr. Ramsey told her promptly.
10068-8{_}4452{_}"We're running so short-handed that I don't know how to get along; and if I try to get an extra man, I find he's out with the searchers.
10068-8{_}4453{_}I sent up for Himes yesterday, but him and Buckheath was to go together to-day, taking Mr. Stoddard's car, so as to get further up into the Unakas."
10068-8{_}4454{_}Johnnie felt as though the blood receded from her face and gathered all about a heart which beat to suffocation.
10068-8{_}4455{_}For a wild moment she had an impulse to denounce Buckheath and her stepfather.
10068-8{_}4456{_}But almost instantly she realized that she would weaken her cause and lose all chance of assistance by doing so.
10068-8{_}4457{_}Her standing in the mill was excellent, and as she ran up the stairs she was going over in her mind the persons to whom she might take her story.
10068-8{_}4458{_}She found no one from whom she dared expect credence and help.
10068-8{_}4459{_}Out in the street again she caught sight of Charlie Conroy, and her thoughts were turned by a natural association of ideas to Lydia Sessions.
10068-8{_}4460{_}That was it!
10068-8{_}4461{_}Why had it not occurred to her before?
10068-8{_}4462{_}She hurried up the long hill to the Hardwick home and, trying first the bell at the front, where she got no reply, skirted the house and rapped long and loudly at the side door.
10068-8{_}4463{_}Harriet Hardwick, when things began to wear a tragic complexion, had promptly packed her wardrobe and her children and flitted to Watauga.
10068-8{_}4464{_}This hegira was undertaken mainly to get her sister away from the scene of Gray Stoddard's disappearance; yet when the move came to be made, Miss Sessions refused to accompany her sister.
10068-8{_}4465{_}"I can't go," she repeated fiercely.
10068-8{_}4466{_}"I'll stay here and keep house for Jerome.
10068-8{_}4467{_}Then if there comes any news, I'll be where--oh, don't look at me that way.
10068-8{_}4468{_}I wish you'd go on and let me alone.
10068-8{_}4469{_}Yes--yes--yes--it is better for you to go to Watauga and leave me here."
10068-8{_}4470{_}Ever since her brother-in-law opened the door of the sitting room and announced to the family Gray Stoddard's disappearance, Lydia Sessions had been, as it were, a woman at war with herself.
10068-8{_}4471{_}Her first impulse was of decorum--to jerk her skirts about her in seemly fashion and be certain that no smirch adhered to them.
10068-8{_}4472{_}Then she began to wonder if she could find Shade Buckheath, and discover from him the truth of the matter.
10068-8{_}4473{_}Whenever she would have made a movement toward this, she winced away from what she knew he would say to her.
10068-8{_}4474{_}She flinched even from finding out that her fears were well grounded.
10068-8{_}4475{_}As matters began to wear a more serious face, she debated now and again telling her brother-in-law of her suspicions that Buckheath had a grudge against Stoddard.
10068-8{_}4476{_}But if she said this, how account for the knowledge?
10068-8{_}4477{_}How explain to Jerome why she had denied seeing Stoddard Friday morning?
10068-8{_}4478{_}Jerome was so terribly practical--he would ask such searching questions.
10068-8{_}4479{_}Back of it all there was truly much remorse, and terrible anxiety for Stoddard himself; but this was continually swallowed up in her concern for her own welfare, her own good name.
10068-8{_}4480{_}Always, after she had agonized so much, there would come with a revulsion--a gust of anger.
10068-8{_}4481{_}Stoddard had never cared for her, he had been cruel in his attitude of kindness.
10068-8{_}4482{_}Let him take what followed.
10068-8{_}4483{_}Cottonville was a town distraught, and the Hardwick servants had seized the occasion to run out for a bit of delectable gossip in which the least of the horrors included Gray Stoddard's murdered and mutilated body washed down in some mountain stream to the sight of his friends.
10068-8{_}4484{_}Johnnie was too urgent to long delay.
10068-8{_}4485{_}Getting no answer at the side door, she pushed it open and ventured through silent room after room until she came to the stairway, and so on up to Miss Sessions's bedroom door.
10068-8{_}4486{_}She had been there before, and fearing to alarm by knocking, she finally called out in what she tried to make a normal, reassuring tone.
10068-8{_}4487{_}"It's only me--Johnnie Consadine--Miss Lydia."
10068-8{_}4488{_}The answer was a hasty, muffled outcry.
10068-8{_}4489{_}Somebody who had been kneeling by the bed on the further side of the room sprang up and came forward, showing a face so disfigured by tears and anxiety, by loss of sleep and lack of food, as to be scarcely recognizable.
10068-8{_}4490{_}That ravaged visage told plainly the battle-ground that Lydia Sessions's narrow soul had become in these dreadful days.
10068-8{_}4491{_}She knew now that she had set Shade Buckheath to quarrel with Gray Stoddard--and Gray had never been seen since the hour she sent the dangerous, unscrupulous man after him to that quarrel.
10068-8{_}4492{_}With this knowledge wrestled and fought the instinct we strive to develop in our girl children, the fear we brand shamefully into their natures--her name must not be connected with such an affair--she must not be "talked about."
10068-8{_}4493{_}"Have they found him?"
10068-8{_}4494{_}Lydia gasped.
10068-8{_}4495{_}"Is he alive?"
10068-8{_}4496{_}Johnnie, generous soul, even in the intense preoccupation of her own pain, could pity the woman who looked and spoke thus.
10068-8{_}4497{_}"No," she answered, "they haven't found him--and some that are looking for him never will find him.
10068-8{_}4498{_}"Oh, Miss Lydia, I want you to help me make them send somebody that we can trust up the Gap road, and on to the Unakas."
10068-8{_}4499{_}Miss Sessions flinched plainly.
10068-8{_}4500{_}"What do you know about it?"
10068-8{_}4501{_}she inquired in a voice which shook.
10068-8{_}4502{_}Still staring at Johnnie, she moved back toward her bedroom door.
10068-8{_}4503{_}"Why should you mention the Gap road?
10068-8{_}4504{_}What makes you think he went up in the Unakas?"
10068-8{_}4505{_}"I--don't know that he went there," hesitated Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4506{_}"But I do know who you've got to find before you can find him.
10068-8{_}4507{_}Oh, get somebody to go with me and help me, before it's too late.
10068-8{_}4508{_}I--" she hesitated--"I thought maybe we could get your brother Hartley's car.
10068-8{_}4509{_}I could run it--I could run a car."
10068-8{_}4510{_}The bitterness that had racked Lydia Sessions's heart for more than forty-eight hours culminated.
10068-8{_}4511{_}She had been instrumental in putting Gray Stoddard in mortal danger--and now if he was to be helped, assistance would come through Johnnie Consadine!
10068-8{_}4512{_}It was more than she could bear.
10068-8{_}4513{_}"I don't believe it!"
10068-8{_}4514{_}she gasped.
10068-8{_}4515{_}"You know who to find!
10068-8{_}4516{_}You're just getting up this story to be noticed.
10068-8{_}4517{_}You're always doing things to attract attention to yourself.
10068-8{_}4518{_}You want to go riding around in an automobile and--and--Mr. Stoddard has probably gone in to Watauga and taken the midnight train for Boston.
10068-8{_}4519{_}This looking around in the mountains is folly.
10068-8{_}4520{_}Who would want to harm him in the mountains?"
10068-8{_}4521{_}For a moment Johnnie stood, thwarted and non-plussed.
10068-8{_}4522{_}The insults directed toward herself made almost no impression on her, strangely as they came from Lydia Sessions's lips.
10068-8{_}4523{_}She was too intent on her own purpose to care greatly.
10068-8{_}4524{_}"Shade Buckheath--" she began cautiously, intending only to state that Shade had taken Stoddard's car; but Lydia Sessions drew back with a scream.
10068-8{_}4525{_}"It's a lie!"
10068-8{_}4526{_}she cried.
10068-8{_}4527{_}"There isn't a word of truth in what you say, John Consadine.
10068-8{_}4528{_}Oh, you're the plague of my life--you have been from the first!
10068-8{_}4529{_}You follow me about and torment me.
10068-8{_}4530{_}Shade Buckheath had nothing to do with Gray Stoddard's disappearance, I tell you.
10068-8{_}4531{_}Nothing--nothing --nothing!"
10068-8{_}4532{_}She thrust forward her face and sent forth the words with incredible vehemence.
10068-8{_}4533{_}But her tirade kindled in Johnnie no heat of personal anger.
10068-8{_}4534{_}She stood looking intently at the frantic woman before her.
10068-8{_}4535{_}Slowly a light of comprehension dawned in her eyes.
10068-8{_}4536{_}"Shade Buckheath had everything to do with Gray Stoddard's disappearance.
10068-8{_}4537{_}You know it--that's what ails you now.
10068-8{_}4538{_}You--you must have been there when they quarrelled!"
10068-8{_}4539{_}"They didn't quarrel--they didn't!"
10068-8{_}4540{_}protested Miss Lydia, with a yet more hysteric emphasis.
10068-8{_}4541{_}"They didn't even speak to each other.
10068-8{_}4542{_}Mr. Stoddard said 'Good morning' to me, and rode right past."
10068-8{_}4543{_}Johnnie leant forward and, with a sudden sweeping movement, caught the other woman by the wrist, looking deep into her eyes.
10068-8{_}4544{_}"Lydia," she said accusingly, and neither of them noticed the freedom of the address, "you didn't tell the truth when you said you hadn't seen Gray since Friday night.
10068-8{_}4545{_}You saw him Friday morning--_you_--_and_-- _Shade_--_Buckheath_!
10068-8{_}4546{_}You have both lied about it--God knows why.
10068-8{_}4547{_}Now, Shade and my stepfather have taken poor Gray's car and gone up into the mountains.
10068-8{_}4548{_}_What do you think they went for?_"  The blazing young eyes were on Miss Sessions's tortured countenance.
10068-8{_}4549{_}"Oh, don't let those men get at Gray.
10068-8{_}4550{_}They'll murder him!"
10068-8{_}4551{_}sobbed the older woman, sinking once more to her knees.
10068-8{_}4552{_}"Johnnie--I've always been good to you, haven't I?
10068-8{_}4553{_}You go and tell them that--say that Shade Buckheath--that somebody ought to--"  She broke off abruptly, and sprang up like a suddenly goaded creature.
10068-8{_}4554{_}"No, I won't!"
10068-8{_}4555{_}she cried out.
10068-8{_}4556{_}"You needn't ask it of me.
10068-8{_}4557{_}I will not tell about seeing Mr. Stoddard Friday morning.
10068-8{_}4558{_}I promised not to, and it can't do any good, anyhow.
10068-8{_}4559{_}If you set them at me, I'll deny it and tell them you made up the story.
10068-8{_}4560{_}I will--I will--I will!"
10068-8{_}4561{_}And she ran into her room once more, and threw herself down beside the bed.
10068-8{_}4562{_}Johnnie turned contemptuously and left the woman babbling incoherencies on her knees, evidently preparing to pray to a God whose laws she was determined to break.
10068-8{_}4563{_}CHAPTER XXII  THE ATLAS VERTEBRA  Johnnie hurried downstairs, in a mental turmoil out of which there swiftly formed itself the resolution to go herself and if possible overtake or find Shade and her stepfather.
10068-8{_}4564{_}Word must first be sent to her mother.
10068-8{_}4565{_}She was glad to remember that little bankbook under Laurella's pillow.
10068-8{_}4566{_}Mavity and Mandy would tend the invalids well, helped by little Lissy; and with money available, she was sure they would be allowed to lack for nothing.
10068-8{_}4567{_}She crossed the hall swiftly, meaning to go past the little grocery where they bought their supplies and telephone Mavity that she might be away for several days.
10068-8{_}4568{_}But near the side door she noted the Hardwick telephone, and hesitated a moment.
10068-8{_}4569{_}People would hear her down at Mayfield's.
10068-8{_}4570{_}Already she began to have a terror of being watched or followed.
10068-8{_}4571{_}Hesitatingly she took down the receiver and asked for connection.
10068-8{_}4572{_}At the little tinkle of the bell, there was a swift, light rush above stairs.
10068-8{_}4573{_}"Mahala!"
10068-8{_}4574{_}screamed Miss Sessions's voice over the banisters, thinking the maid was below stairs; "answer that telephone."
10068-8{_}4575{_}She heard Johnnie move, and added, "Tell everybody that I can't be seen.
10068-8{_}4576{_}If it's anything about Mr. Stoddard, say that I'm sick--utterly prostrated--and can't be talked to."
10068-8{_}4577{_}She turned from the stairway, ran back into her own room and shut and locked the door.
10068-8{_}4578{_}And at that moment Johnnie heard Mavity Bence's voice replying to her.
10068-8{_}4579{_}"Aunt Mavity," she began, "this is Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4580{_}I'm up at Mr. Hardwick's now.
10068-8{_}4581{_}Uncle Pros is out in the mountains, and I'm going to look for him.
10068-8{_}4582{_}I'd rather not have anybody know I'm gone; do you understand that?
10068-8{_}4583{_}Try to keep it from the boarders and the children.
10068-8{_}4584{_}You and Mandy are the only ones that would have to know."
10068-8{_}4585{_}"Yes, honey, yes, Johnnie," came the eager, humble reply.
10068-8{_}4586{_}"I'll do just like you say.
10068-8{_}4587{_}Shan't nobody find out from me.
10068-8{_}4588{_}Johnnie--" there was a pause--"Johnnie, Pap and Shade didn't get off as soon as they expected.
10068-8{_}4589{_}Something was the matter with the machine, I believe.
10068-8{_}4590{_}They ain't been gone to exceed a quarter of an hour.
10068-8{_}4591{_}I--I thought maybe you'd like to know."
10068-8{_}4592{_}"Thank you, Aunt Mavity," said Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4593{_}"Yes, I'm glad you told me."
10068-8{_}4594{_}She understood what a struggle the kind soul had had with her weakness and timidity ere, for loyalty's sake, she was able to make the disclosure.
10068-8{_}4595{_}"I may not be back for two or three days.
10068-8{_}4596{_}Don't worry about me.
10068-8{_}4597{_}I'll be all right.
10068-8{_}4598{_}Mother's got money.
10068-8{_}4599{_}You buy what she and Deanie need, and don't work too hard.
10068-8{_}4600{_}Good-bye."
10068-8{_}4601{_}She hung up the receiver, went out the side door and, reaching the main street, struck straight for the Gap, holding the big road for the Unakas.
10068-8{_}4602{_}To her left was the white highway that ran along above the valley, and that Palace of Pleasure which had seemed a wonder and a mystery to her one year gone.
10068-8{_}4603{_}To-day she gave no thought to the sight of river and valley and town, except to look back once at the roofs and reflect that, among all the people housed there in sight of her, there were surely those who knew the secret of Gray Stoddard's disappearance--who could tell her if they would where to search for him.
10068-8{_}4604{_}Somehow, the thought made her feel very small and alone and unfriended.
10068-8{_}4605{_}With its discouragement came that dogged persistence that was characteristic of the girl.
10068-8{_}4606{_}She set her trembling lip and went over her plans resolutely, methodically.
10068-8{_}4607{_}Deanie and Laurella were safe to be well looked after in her absence.
10068-8{_}4608{_}Mavity Bence and Mandy would care for them tenderly.
10068-8{_}4609{_}And there was the bankbook.
10068-8{_}4610{_}If Johnnie knew her mother, the household back there would not lack, either for assistance or material matters.
10068-8{_}4611{_}And now the present enterprise began to shape itself in her mind.
10068-8{_}4612{_}A practical creature, she depended from the first on getting a lift from time to time.
10068-8{_}4613{_}Yet Johnnie knew better than another the vast, silent, secret network of hate that draws about the victim in a mountain vendetta.
10068-8{_}4614{_}If the spirit of feud was aroused against the mill owners, if the Groners and Dawsons had been able to enlist their kin and clan, she was well aware that the man or woman who gave her smiling information as to ways and means, might, the hour before, have looked on Gray Stoddard lying dead, or sat in the council which planned to kill him.
10068-8{_}4615{_}Thus she walked warily, and dared ask from none directions or help.
10068-8{_}4616{_}She was not yet in her own region, these lower ridges lying between two lines of railway, which, from the mountaineer's point of view, contaminated them and gave them a tincture of the valley and the Settlement.
10068-8{_}4617{_}Noon came and passed.
10068-8{_}4618{_}She was very weary.
10068-8{_}4619{_}Factory life had told on her physically, and the recent distress of mind added its devitalizing influence.
10068-8{_}4620{_}There was a desperate flagging of the muscles weakened by disuse and an unhealthy indoor life.
10068-8{_}4621{_}"I wonder can I ever make it?"
10068-8{_}4622{_}she questioned herself.
10068-8{_}4623{_}Then swiftly, "I've got to--I've got to."
10068-8{_}4624{_}Her eye roved toward a cabin on the slope above.
10068-8{_}4625{_}There lived a man by the name of Straley, but he was a cousin to Lura Dawson, the girl who had died in the hospital.
10068-8{_}4626{_}Johnnie knew him to be one of the bitterest enemies of the Cottonville mill owners, and realized that he would be the last one to whom she should apply.
10068-8{_}4627{_}Mutely, doggedly, she pressed on, and rounding a bend in a long, lonely stretch of road, saw before her the tall, lithe form of a man, trousers tucked into boots, a tall staff in hand, making swift progress up the road.
10068-8{_}4628{_}The sound of feet evidently arrested the attention of the wayfarer.
10068-8{_}4629{_}He turned and waited for her to come up.
10068-8{_}4630{_}The figure was so congruous with its surroundings that she saw with surprise a face totally strange to her.
10068-8{_}4631{_}The turned-down collar of the rumpled shirt was unbuttoned at a brown throat; the face above seemed to her eyes neither old nor young, though the light, springing gait when he walked, the supple, easeful attitude now that he rested, one hand flung high on the curious tall staff, were those of a youth; the eyes of a warm, laughing hazel had the direct fearlessness of a child, and a slouch hat carried in the hand showed a fair crop of slightly grizzled, curling hair.
10068-8{_}4632{_}A stranger--at first the thought frightened, and then attracted her.
10068-8{_}4633{_}This man looked not unlike Johnnie's own people, and there was something in his face that led her to entertain the idea of appealing to him for help.
10068-8{_}4634{_}He settled the question of whether or no she should enter into conversation, by accosting her at once brusquely and genially.
10068-8{_}4635{_}"Mornin', sis'.
10068-8{_}4636{_}You look tired," he said.
10068-8{_}4637{_}"You ought to have a stick, like me.
10068-8{_}4638{_}Hold on--I'll cut you one."
10068-8{_}4639{_}Before the girl could respond beyond an answering smile and "good morning," the new friend had put his own alpenstock into her hands and gone to the roadside, where, with unerring judgment, he selected a long, straight, tapering shoot of ash, and hewed it deftly with a monster jack-knife drawn from his trousers pocket.
10068-8{_}4640{_}"There--try that," he said as he returned, trimming off the last of the leaves and branches.
10068-8{_}4641{_}Johnnie took the staff with her sweet smile of thanks.
10068-8{_}4642{_}For a few moments the two walked on silently side by side, she desperately absorbed in her anxieties, her companion apparently returning to some world apart in his own mind.
10068-8{_}4643{_}Suddenly:  "Can I get to the railroad down this side?"
10068-8{_}4644{_}the man asked her in that odd, incidental voice of his which suggested that what he said was merely a small portion of what he thought.
10068-8{_}4645{_}"Why--yes, I reckon so," hesitated Johnnie.
10068-8{_}4646{_}"It's a pretty far way, and there don't many folks travel on it.
10068-8{_}4647{_}It's an old Indian trail; a heap of our roads here are that; but it'll take you right to the railroad--the W. and A."
10068-8{_}4648{_}Her companion chuckled, seemingly with some inner satisfaction.
10068-8{_}4649{_}"Yes, that's just what I supposed.
10068-8{_}4650{_}I soldiered all over this country, and I thought it was about as pretty scenery as God ever made.
10068-8{_}4651{_}I promised myself then that if I ever came back into this part of the world, I'd do some tramping through here.
10068-8{_}4652{_}They're going to have a great big banquet at Atlanta, and they had me caged up taking me down there to make a speech.
10068-8{_}4653{_}I gave them the slip at Watauga.
10068-8{_}4654{_}I knew I'd strike the railroad if I footed it through the mountains here."
10068-8{_}4655{_}Johnnie examined her companion with attention.
10068-8{_}4656{_}Would it do to ask him if he had seen an automobile on the road--a dark green car?
10068-8{_}4657{_}Dare she make inquiry as to whether he had heard of Gray Stoddard's disappearance, or met any of the searchers?
10068-8{_}4658{_}She decided on a conservative course.
10068-8{_}4659{_}"I wish I had time to set you in the right road," she hesitated; "but my poor old uncle is out here somewhere among these ridges and ravines; he's not in his right mind, and I've got to find him if I can."
10068-8{_}4660{_}"Crazy, do you mean?"
10068-8{_}4661{_}asked her companion, with a quick yet easy, smiling attention.
10068-8{_}4662{_}"I'd like to see him, if he's crazy.
10068-8{_}4663{_}I take a great interest in crazy folks.
10068-8{_}4664{_}Some of 'em have a lot of sense left."
10068-8{_}4665{_}Johnnie nodded.
10068-8{_}4666{_}"He doesn't know any of us," she said pitifully.
10068-8{_}4667{_}"They've had him in the hospital three months, trying to do something for him; but the doctors say he'll never be well."
10068-8{_}4668{_}"That's right hopeful," observed the man, with a plainly intentional, dry ludicrousness.
10068-8{_}4669{_}"I always think there's some chance when the doctors give 'em up--and begin to let 'em alone.
10068-8{_}4670{_}How was he hurt, sis'?"
10068-8{_}4671{_}Johnnie did not pause to reflect that she had not said Uncle Pros was hurt at all.
10068-8{_}4672{_}For some reason which she would herself have been at a loss to explain, she hastened to detail to this chance-met stranger the exact appearance and nature of Pros Passmore's injuries, her listener nodding his head at this or that point; making some comment or inquiry at another.
10068-8{_}4673{_}"The doctors say that they would suppose it was a fractured skull, or concussion of the brain, or something like that; but they've examined him and there is nothing to see on the outside; and they trephined and it didn't do any good; so they just let him stay about the hospital."
10068-8{_}4674{_}"No," said her new friend softly, almost absently, "it didn't do any good to trephine--but it might have done a lot of harm.
10068-8{_}4675{_}I'd like to see the back of your uncle's neck.
10068-8{_}4676{_}I ain't in any hurry to get to that banquet at Atlanta--a man can always overeat and make himself sick, without going so far to do it."
10068-8{_}4677{_}So, like an idle schoolboy, the unknown forsook his own course, turning from the road when Johnnie turned, and went with her up the steep, rocky gulch where the door of a deserted cabin flung to and fro on its hinges.
10068-8{_}4678{_}At sight of the smokeless chimney, the gaping doorway and empty, inhospitable interior, Johnnie looked blank.
10068-8{_}4679{_}"Have you got anything to eat?"
10068-8{_}4680{_}she asked her companion, hesitatingly.
10068-8{_}4681{_}"I came off in such a hurry that I forgot all about it.
10068-8{_}4682{_}Some people that I know used to live in that cabin, and I hoped to get my dinner there and ask after my uncle; but I see they have moved."
10068-8{_}4683{_}"Sit right down here," said the stranger, indicating the broad door-stone, around which the grass grew tall.
10068-8{_}4684{_}"We'll soon make that all right."
10068-8{_}4685{_}He sought in the pockets of the coat he carried slung across his shoulder and brought out a packet of food.
10068-8{_}4686{_}"I laid in some fuel when I thought I might get the chance to run my own engine across the mountains," he told the girl, opening his bundle and dividing evenly.
10068-8{_}4687{_}He uttered a few musical words in an unknown tongue.
10068-8{_}4688{_}"That's Indian," he commented carelessly, without looking at her.
10068-8{_}4689{_}"It means you're to eat your dinner.
10068-8{_}4690{_}I was with the Shawnees when I was a boy.
10068-8{_}4691{_}I learned a lot of their language, and I'll never forget it.
10068-8{_}4692{_}They taught me more things than talk."
10068-8{_}4693{_}Johnnie studied the man beside her as they ate their bit of lunch.
10068-8{_}4694{_}"My name is Johnnie Consadine, sir," she told him.
10068-8{_}4695{_}"What shall I call you?"
10068-8{_}4696{_}Thus directly questioned, the unknown smiled quizzically, his hazel eyes crinkling at the corners and overflowing with good humour.
10068-8{_}4697{_}"Well, you might say 'Pap,'" he observed consideringly, "Lots of boys and girls do call me Pap--more than a thousand of 'em, now, I guess.
10068-8{_}4698{_}And I'm eighty--mighty near old enough to have a girl of nineteen."
10068-8{_}4699{_}She looked at him in astonishment.
10068-8{_}4700{_}Eighty years old, as lithe as a lad, and with a lad's clear, laughing eye!
10068-8{_}4701{_}Yet there was a look of power, of that knowledge which is power, in his face that made her say to him:  "Do you think that Uncle Pros can ever be cured--have his right mind back again, I mean?
10068-8{_}4702{_}Of course, the cut on his head is healed up long ago."
10068-8{_}4703{_}"The cut on his head didn't make him crazy," said her companion, murmuringly.
