10068-8{_}4706{_}"Yes, there did," Johnnie assented wonderingly--falteringly.
10068-8{_}4707{_}"I don't know how you came to guess it, but the woman who told me that she was hiding in the front room when they were quarrelling and saw Uncle Pros fall down the steps, says he landed almost square on his head.
10068-8{_}4708{_}She thought at first his neck was broken--that he was killed."
10068-8{_}4709{_}"Uh-huh," nodded the newcomer.
10068-8{_}4710{_}"You see I'm a good guesser.
10068-8{_}4711{_}I make my living guessing things."
10068-8{_}4712{_}He flung her a whimsical, sidelong glance, as, having finished their lunch, they rose and moved on.
10068-8{_}4713{_}"I wish I had my hands on the processes of that atlas vertebra," he said.

10068-8{_}4715{_}inquired Johnnie in a slightly startled tone.
10068-8{_}4716{_}"Never mind, sis'.
10068-8{_}4717{_}If we find him, and I can handle him, I'll know where to look."
10068-8{_}4718{_}"Nobody can touch him but me when he gets out this way," Johnnie said.
10068-8{_}4719{_}"He acts sort of scared and sort of fierce, and just runs and hides from people.

10068-8{_}4721{_}"Maybe you could--and then again maybe you couldn't," returned the other, with a great show of giving her proposition serious consideration.
10068-8{_}4722{_}"A good many folks think they can do just what I can--if I'd only tell 'em how--and sometimes they find out they can't."

10068-8{_}4724{_}At the roadside, in a little open, grassy space where once evidently a cabin had stood, knelt the figure of a gaunt old man.
10068-8{_}4725{_}At first he seemed to the approaching pair to be gesticulating and pointing, but a moment's observation gave them the gleam of a knife in his hand--he was playing mumblety-peg.

10068-8{_}4727{_}"Hi!
10068-8{_}4728{_}Hi!
10068-8{_}4729{_}Hi!
10068-8{_}4730{_}I th'owed it.
10068-8{_}4731{_}That counts two for me," the cracked old falsetto shrilled out.
10068-8{_}4732{_}There on that grassy plot that might have been a familiar dooryard of his early days, he was playing alone, gone back to childhood.

10068-8{_}5057{_}Nary one o' them families lost a man; but Burkhalter's boy got hisself killed up.
10068-8{_}5058{_}Yes, that's what happened to him.
10068-8{_}5059{_}Dead.
10068-8{_}5060{_}I went to the funeral."
10068-8{_}5061{_}"True as Scriptur'," confirmed Zack--"reach an' take off, Pros.
10068-8{_}5062{_}Johnnie, eat hearty--true as you-all set here.
10068-8{_}5063{_}I he'ped make the coffin an' dig the grave."
10068-8{_}5064{_}After a time there came a sort of ruth to Johnnie for the poor creatures, furtive, stealing glances at each other, and answering her inquiries or Uncle Pros's with dry, evasive platitudes.
10068-8{_}5065{_}She knew there was no malice in either of them; and that only the abject terror of the weak kept them from giving whatever bit of information it was they had and were consciously withholding.
10068-8{_}5066{_}Soon she ceased plying them with questions, and signalled Uncle Pros that he should do the same.
10068-8{_}5067{_}After the children were asleep in their trundle-bed, the four elders sat by the dying fire on the hearth and talked a little.
10068-8{_}5068{_}Johnnie told Zack and Roxy of the mill work at Cottonville, how well she had got on, and how good Mr. Stoddard had been to her, choking over the treasured remembrances.
10068-8{_}5069{_}She related the many kindnesses that had been shown Pros and his kinfolk at the Hospital, how the old man had been there for three months, treated as a guest during the latter part of his stay rather than a patient, and how Mr. Stoddard would leave his work in the office to come and cheer the sick man, or quiet him if he got violent.
10068-8{_}5070{_}"He looked perfectly dreadful when I first saw him," she said to them, "but the doctors took care of him as if he'd been a little baby.
10068-8{_}5071{_}The nurses fed him by spoonfuls and coaxed him just like you would little Honey; and Mr. Stoddard--he never was too busy to--" the tears brimmed her eyes in the dusky cabin interior--"to come when Uncle Pros begged for him."
10068-8{_}5072{_}The woman sighed and stirred uneasily, her eye stealthily seeking her husband's.
10068-8{_}5073{_}In that little one-room hut there was no place for guests.
10068-8{_}5074{_}Presently the men drifted out to the chip pile, where they lingered a while in desultory talk.
10068-8{_}5075{_}Roxy and Johnnie, partly undressed, occupied the one bed; and later the host and his guest came in and lay down, clothed just as they were, with their feet to the fire, and slept.
10068-8{_}5076{_}In the darkness just before dawn, Johnnie wakened from heavy sleep and raised her head to find that a clear fire was burning on the hearth and the two men were gone.
10068-8{_}5077{_}Noiselessly she arose, and replaced her outer wear, thinking to slip away without disturbing Roxy.
10068-8{_}5078{_}But when she returned softly to the interior, after laving face and hands out at the wash-basin, and ordering her abundant hair, she found the little woman up and clad, slicing bacon and making coffee of generous strength from their scanty store.
10068-8{_}5079{_}"No--why, the idea!"
10068-8{_}5080{_}cried Roxy.
10068-8{_}5081{_}"Of course, you wasn't a-goin' on from no house o' mine 'thout no breakfast.
10068-8{_}5082{_}Why, I say!"
10068-8{_}5083{_}Johnnie's throat swelled at the humble kindness.
10068-8{_}5084{_}They ate, thanked Roxy and her man Zack in the simple uneffusive mountain fashion, and started away in the twilight of dawn.
10068-8{_}5085{_}The big road was barely reached, when they heard steps coming after them in the dusk, and a breathless voice calling in a whisper, "Johnnie!
10068-8{_}5086{_}Johnnie!"
10068-8{_}5087{_}The two turned and waited till Roxy came up.
10068-8{_}5088{_}"I--ye dropped this on the floor," the woman said, fumbling in her pocket and bringing out a bit of paper.
10068-8{_}5089{_}"I didn't know as it was of any value--and then again I didn't know but what it might be.
10068-8{_}5090{_}Johnnie--" she broke off and stood peering hesitatingly into the gloom toward the girl's shining face.
10068-8{_}5091{_}With a quick touch of the arm Johnnie signed to Pros to move on.
10068-8{_}5092{_}As he swung out of earshot, the bulging light eyes, so like Mandy's, were suddenly dimmed by a rush of tears.
10068-8{_}5093{_}"I reckon he'd beat me ef he knowed I told," Roxy gasped.
10068-8{_}5094{_}"He ain't never struck me yit, and us married five year--but I reckon he'd beat me for that."
10068-8{_}5095{_}Johnnie wisely forbore reply or interference of any sort.
10068-8{_}5096{_}The woman gulped, drew her breath hard, and looked about her.
10068-8{_}5097{_}"Johnnie," she whispered again, "the--that there thing they ride in--the otty-mobile--hit broke down, and Zack was over to Pres Blevin's blacksmith shop a-he'pin' 'em work on it all day yesterday.
10068-8{_}5098{_}You know Pres--he married Lura Dawson's aunt.
10068-8{_}5099{_}Neither Himes nor Buckheath could git it to move, but by night they had it a-runnin'--or so hit _would_ run.
10068-8{_}5100{_}That's why you never saw tracks of it on the road--hit hadn't been along thar yit.
10068-8{_}5101{_}But hit's went on this morning.
10068-8{_}5102{_}No--no--no!
10068-8{_}5103{_}I don't know whar it went.
10068-8{_}5104{_}I don't know what they was aimin' to do.
10068-8{_}5105{_}I don't know nothin'!
10068-8{_}5106{_}Don't ask me, Johnnie Consadine, I reckon I've said right now what's put my man's neck in danger.
10068-8{_}5107{_}Oh, my God--I wish the men-folks would quit their fussin' an' feudin'!"
10068-8{_}5108{_}And she turned and ran distractedly back into the cabin while Johnnie hurried on to join her uncle.
10068-8{_}5109{_}CHAPTER XXIV  THE RESCUE  Johnnie caught her uncle's hand and ran with him through the little thicket of saplings toward the main road.
10068-8{_}5110{_}"We'll get the track of the wheels, and when we find that car--and Shade Buckheath--and Pap Himes....I ..." Johnnie panted, and did not finish her sentence.
10068-8{_}5111{_}Her heart leaped when they came upon the broad mark of the pneumatic tires still fresh in the lonely mountain road.
10068-8{_}5112{_}"Looks like they might have passed here while we was standin' back there talkin' to Roxy," Uncle Pros said.
10068-8{_}5113{_}"They could have--we'd not have heard a thing that distance, through this thick woods.
10068-8{_}5114{_}Wonder could we catch up with them?"
10068-8{_}5115{_}Johnnie shook her head.
10068-8{_}5116{_}She remembered the car flying up the ascents, swooping down long slopes and skimming like a bird across the levels, that morning when she had driven it.
10068-8{_}5117{_}"They'll go almost as fast as a railroad train, Uncle Pros," she told him, "but we must get there as soon as we can."
10068-8{_}5118{_}After that scarcely a word was spoken, while the two, still hand in hand, made what speed they could.
10068-8{_}5119{_}The morning waxed.
10068-8{_}5120{_}The March sunshine was warm and pleasant.
10068-8{_}5121{_}It was even hot, toiling endlessly up that mountain road.
10068-8{_}5122{_}Now and again they met people who knew and saluted them, and who looked back at them curiously, furtively; at least it seemed so to the old man and the girl.
10068-8{_}5123{_}Once a lean, hawk-nosed fellow ploughing a hillside field shouted across it:  "Hey-oh, Pros Passmore!
10068-8{_}5124{_}How yuh come on?
10068-8{_}5125{_}I 'lowed the student doctors would 'a' had you, long ago."
10068-8{_}5126{_}Pros ventured no reply, save a wagging of the head.
10068-8{_}5127{_}"That's Blaylock's cousin," he muttered to Johnnie.
10068-8{_}5128{_}"Mighty glad we never went near 'em last night."
10068-8{_}5129{_}Once or twice they were delayed to talk.
10068-8{_}5130{_}Johnnie would have hurried on, but her uncle warned her with a look to do nothing unusual.
10068-8{_}5131{_}Everybody spoke to them of Gray Stoddard.
10068-8{_}5132{_}Nobody had seen anything of him within a month of his disappearance, but several of them had "hearn say."
10068-8{_}5133{_}"They tell me," vouchsafed a lanky boy dawdling with his axe at a chip pile, "that the word goes in Cottonville now, that he's took money and lit out for Canada.
10068-8{_}5134{_}Town folks is always a-doin' such."
10068-8{_}5135{_}"Like as not, bud," Pros assented gravely.
10068-8{_}5136{_}"Me and Johnnie is goin' up to look after the old house, but we allowed to sleep to-night at Bushares's.
10068-8{_}5137{_}Time enough to git to our place to-morrow."
10068-8{_}5138{_}Johnnie, who knew that her uncle hoped to reach the Consadine cabin by noon, instantly understood that he considered the possibility of this boy being a sort of picket posted to interview passers-by; and that the intention was to misinform him, so that he should not carry news of their approach.
10068-8{_}5139{_}After this, they met no one, but swung on at their best pace, and for the most part in silence, husbanding strength and breath.
10068-8{_}5140{_}Twelve o'clock saw them entering that gash of the hills where the little cabin crouched against the great mountain wall.
10068-8{_}5141{_}The ground became so rocky, that the track of the automobile was lost.
10068-8{_}5142{_}At first it would be visible now and again on a bit of sandy loam, chain marks showing, where the tire left no impression; but, within a mile or so of the Consadine home, it seemed to have left the trail.
10068-8{_}5143{_}When this point arrived, Johnnie differed from her uncle in choosing to hold to the road.
10068-8{_}5144{_}"Honey, this ends the cyar-tracks.
10068-8{_}5145{_}Looks like they'd turned out.
10068-8{_}5146{_}I think they took off into the bushes here, and where that cyar goes we ought to go," Pros argued.
10068-8{_}5147{_}But Johnnie hurried on ahead, looking about her eagerly.
10068-8{_}5148{_}Suddenly she stooped with a cry and picked up from the path a small object.
10068-8{_}5149{_}"They've carried him past this way," she panted.
10068-8{_}5150{_}"Oh, Uncle Pros, he was right here not so very long ago."
10068-8{_}5151{_}She scrutinized the sparse growth, the leafless bushes about the spot, looking for signs of a struggle, and the question in her heart was, "My God, was he alive or dead?"
10068-8{_}5152{_}The thing she held in her hand was a blossom of the pink moccasin flower, carefully pressed, as though for the pages of a herbarium; The bit of paper to which it was attached was crumpled and discoloured.
10068-8{_}5153{_}"Looks like it had laid out in the dew last night," breathed Johnnie.
10068-8{_}5154{_}"Or for a week," supplied Pros.
10068-8{_}5155{_}He scanned the little brown thing, then her face.
10068-8{_}5156{_}"All right," he said dubiously; "if that there tells you that he come a-past here, we'll foller this road--though it 'pears to me like we ought to stick to the cyar."
10068-8{_}5157{_}"It isn't far to our house," urged Johnnie.
10068-8{_}5158{_}"Let's go there first, anyhow."
10068-8{_}5159{_}For a few minutes they pressed ahead in silence; then some subtle excitement made them break into a run.
10068-8{_}5160{_}Thus they rounded the turn.
10068-8{_}5161{_}The cabin came in sight.
10068-8{_}5162{_}Its door swung wide on complaining hinges.
10068-8{_}5163{_}The last of the rickety fence had fallen.
10068-8{_}5164{_}The desolation and decay of a deserted house was over all.
10068-8{_}5165{_}"There's been folks here--lately," panted Pros.
10068-8{_}5166{_}"Look thar!"
10068-8{_}5167{_}and he pointed to a huddle of baskets and garments on the porch.
10068-8{_}5168{_}"Mind out!
10068-8{_}5169{_}Go careful.
10068-8{_}5170{_}They may be thar now."
10068-8{_}5171{_}They "went careful," stealing up the steps and entering with caution; but they found nothing more alarming than the four bare walls, the ash-strewn, fireless hearth, the musty smell of a long-unoccupied house.
10068-8{_}5172{_}Near the back door, at a spot where the dust was thick, Uncle Pros bent to examine a foot-print, when an exclamation from Johnnie called him through to the rear of the cabin.
10068-8{_}5173{_}"See the door!"
10068-8{_}5174{_}she cried, running up the steep way toward the cave spring-house.
10068-8{_}5175{_}"Hold on, honey.
10068-8{_}5176{_}Go easy," cautioned her uncle, following as fast as he could.
10068-8{_}5177{_}He noted the whittling where the sapling bar that held the stout oaken door in place had been recently shaped to its present purpose.
10068-8{_}5178{_}Then a soft, rhythmic sound like a giant breathing in his sleep caught the old hunter's keen ear.
10068-8{_}5179{_}"Watch out, Johnnie," he called, catching her arm, "What's that?
10068-8{_}5180{_}Listen!"
10068-8{_}5181{_}Her fingers were almost on the bar.
10068-8{_}5182{_}They could hear the soft lip-lip of the water as it welled out beneath the threshold, mingled with the tinkle and fall of the spring branch below.
10068-8{_}5183{_}Johnnie turned in her uncle's grasp and clutched him, staring down.
10068-8{_}5184{_}Something shining and dark, brave with brass and flashing lamps, stood on the rocky way beneath, and purred like a great cat in the broad sunlight of noon--Gray Stoddard's motor car!
10068-8{_}5185{_}The two, clinging to each other on the steep above it, gazed half incredulous, now that they had found the thing they sought.
10068-8{_}5186{_}It looked so unbelievably adequate and modern and alive standing there, drawing its perfectly measured breath; it was so eloquent of power and the work of men's hands that there seemed to yawn a gap of half a thousand years between it and the raid in which it was being made a factor.
10068-8{_}5187{_}That this pet toy of the modern millionaire should be set to work out the crude vengeance of wild men in these primitive surroundings, crowded up on a little rocky path of these savage mountains, at the door of a cave spring-house--such a food-cache as a nomad Indian might have utilized, in the gray bluff against the sky-line--it took the breath with its sinister strangeness.
10068-8{_}5188{_}They turned to the barred door.
10068-8{_}5189{_}The cave was a sizable opening running far back into the mountain; indeed, the end of it had never been explored, but the vestibule containing the spring was fitted with rude benches and shelves for holding pans of milk and jars of buttermilk.
10068-8{_}5190{_}As Johnnie's hand went out to the newly cut bar, her uncle once more laid a restraining grasp upon it.
10068-8{_}5191{_}A dozen men might be on the other side of the oaken door, and there might be nobody.
10068-8{_}5192{_}"Hello!"
10068-8{_}5193{_}he called, guardedly.
10068-8{_}5194{_}No answer came; but within there was a sound of clinking, and then a shuffling movement.
10068-8{_}5195{_}The panting motor spoke loud of those who had brought it there, who must be expecting to return to it very shortly.
10068-8{_}5196{_}Johnnie's nerves gave way.
10068-8{_}5197{_}"Hello!
10068-8{_}5198{_}Is there anybody inside?"
10068-8{_}5199{_}she demanded fearfully.
10068-8{_}5200{_}"Who's there?
10068-8{_}5201{_}Who is it?"
10068-8{_}5202{_}came a muffled hail from the cave, in a voice that sent the blood to Johnnie's heart with a sudden shock.
10068-8{_}5203{_}"Uncle Pros, we've found him!"
10068-8{_}5204{_}she screamed, pushing the old man aside, and tugging at the bar which held the door in place.
10068-8{_}5205{_}As she worked, there came a curious clinking sound, and then the dull impact of a heavy fall; and when she dragged the bar loose, swung the door wide and peered into the gloom, there was nothing but the silvery reach of the great spring, and beyond it a prone figure in russet riding-clothes.
10068-8{_}5206{_}"Uncle Pros--he's hurt!
10068-8{_}5207{_}Oh, help me!"
10068-8{_}5208{_}she cried.
10068-8{_}5209{_}The prostrate man struggled to turn his face to them.
10068-8{_}5210{_}"Is that you, Johnnie?"
10068-8{_}5211{_}Gray Stoddard's voice asked.
10068-8{_}5212{_}"No, I'm not hurt.
10068-8{_}5213{_}These things tripped me up."
10068-8{_}5214{_}The two got to him simultaneously.
10068-8{_}5215{_}They found him in heavy shackles.
10068-8{_}5216{_}They noted how ankle and wrist chains had been rivetted in place.
10068-8{_}5217{_}Together they helped him up.
10068-8{_}5218{_}As they did so tears ran down Johnnie's cheeks unregarded.
10068-8{_}5219{_}Passmore deeply moved, yet quiet, studied him covertly.
10068-8{_}5220{_}This, then, was the man of whom Johnnie thought so much, the rich young fellow who had left his work or amusements to come and cheer a sick old man in the hospital; this was the face that was a stranger's to him, but which had leaned over his cot or sat across the checker-board from him for long hours, while they talked or played together.
10068-8{_}5221{_}That face was pale now, the brown hair, "a little longer than other people wore it," tossed helplessly in Stoddard's eyes, because he scarcely could raise his shackled hands to put it right; his russet-brown clothing was torn and grimed, as though with more than one struggle, though it may have been nothing worse than such mishap as his recent fall.
10068-8{_}5222{_}Yet the man's soul looked out of his eyes with the same composure, the same kindness that always were his.
10068-8{_}5223{_}He was eaten by neither terror nor rage, though he was alert for every possibility of help, or of advantage.
10068-8{_}5224{_}"You, Johnnie--you!"
10068-8{_}5225{_}whispered Gray, struggling to his knees with their assistance, and catching a fold of her dress in those manacled hands.
10068-8{_}5226{_}"I have dreamed about you here in the dark.
10068-8{_}5227{_}It is you--it is really Johnnie."
10068-8{_}5228{_}He was pale, dishevelled, with a long mark of black leaf-mould across his cheek from his recent fall; and Johnnie bent speechlessly to wipe the stain away and put back the troublesome lock.
10068-8{_}5229{_}He looked up into the brave beauty of her young, tear-wet face.
10068-8{_}5230{_}"Thank God for you, Johnnie," he murmured.
10068-8{_}5231{_}"I might have known I wouldn't be let to die here in the dark like a rat in a hole while Johnnie lived."
10068-8{_}5232{_}"Whar's them that brought you here?
10068-8{_}5233{_}The keepers?"
10068-8{_}5234{_}questioned the old man anxiously, in a hoarse, hurried whisper.
10068-8{_}5235{_}"Dawson's gone to his dinner," returned Gray.
10068-8{_}5236{_}"There were others here--came in an auto--I heard that.
10068-8{_}5237{_}They've been quarrelling for more than an hour."
10068-8{_}5238{_}--"About what they'd do with you," broke in Pros.
10068-8{_}5239{_}"Yes, part of 'em wants to put you out of the way, of course."
10068-8{_}5240{_}He stooped, eagerly examining the shackles on Gray's ankles.
10068-8{_}5241{_}"No way to git them things off without time and a file," he muttered, shaking his head.
10068-8{_}5242{_}"No," agreed Stoddard.
10068-8{_}5243{_}"And I can't run much with them on.
10068-8{_}5244{_}But we must get away from here as quick as we can.
10068-8{_}5245{_}Dawson came in and told me after the other had gone that they had a big row, and he was standing out for me.
10068-8{_}5246{_}Said he'd never give in to have me taken down and tied on the railroad track in Stryver's Gulch."
10068-8{_}5247{_}Johnnie's fair face whitened at the sinister words.
10068-8{_}5248{_}"The car!"
10068-8{_}5249{_}she cried.
10068-8{_}5250{_}"It's your own, Mr. Stoddard, and it's right down here.
10068-8{_}5251{_}Uncle Pros, we can get him to it--I can run it--I know how."
10068-8{_}5252{_}She put her shoulder under Stoddard's, catching the manacled hand in hers.
10068-8{_}5253{_}Pros laid hold on the other side, and between them they half carried the shackled captive around the spring and to the door.
10068-8{_}5254{_}"Leggo, Johnnie!"
10068-8{_}5255{_}cried her uncle.
10068-8{_}5256{_}"You run on down and see if that contraption will go.
10068-8{_}5257{_}I can git him thar now."
10068-8{_}5258{_}Johnnie instantly loosed the arm she held, sprang through the doorway, and headlong down the bluffy steep, stones rattling about her.
10068-8{_}5259{_}She leaped into the car.
10068-8{_}5260{_}Would her memory serve her?
10068-8{_}5261{_}Would she forget some detail that she must know?
10068-8{_}5262{_}There were two levers under the steering-wheel.
10068-8{_}5263{_}She advanced her spark and partly opened the throttle.
10068-8{_}5264{_}From the steady, comfortable purr which had undertoned all sounds in the tiny glen, the machine burst at once into a deep-toned roar.
10068-8{_}5265{_}The narrow depression vibrated with its joyous clamour.
10068-8{_}5266{_}Suddenly, above the sound, Johnnie was aware of a distant hail, which finally resolved itself into words.
10068-8{_}5267{_}"Hi!
10068-8{_}5268{_}Hoo--ee!
10068-8{_}5269{_}You let that car alone, whoever you are."
10068-8{_}5270{_}She glanced over her shoulder; Passmore had got Gray to the top of the declivity, and was attempting to help him down.
10068-8{_}5271{_}Both men evidently heard the challenge, but she screamed to them again and again.
10068-8{_}5272{_}"Hurry, oh hurry!
10068-8{_}5273{_}They're coming--they're coming."
10068-8{_}5274{_}Stoddard had been stepping as best he could, hobbling along in the hampering leg chains, that were attached to the wrists also, and twitched on his hands with every step.
10068-8{_}5275{_}His muscles responded to Johnnie's cry almost automatically, stiffening to an effort at extra speed, and he fell headlong, dragging Pros down with him.
10068-8{_}5276{_}Despairingly Johnnie started to climb down from the car and go to their aid, but her uncle leaped to his feet clawing and grabbing to find a hold around Gray's waist, panting out, "Stay thar--Johnnie--I can fetch him."
10068-8{_}5277{_}With a straining heave he hoisted Gray's helpless body into his arms.
10068-8{_}5278{_}The car trembled like a great, eager monster, growling in leash.
10068-8{_}5279{_}Johnnie's agonized eyes searched first its mechanism, and then went to the descending figures, where her uncle plunged desperately down the slope, fell, struggled, rolled, but rose and came gallantly on, half dragging, half carrying Gray in his arms.
10068-8{_}5280{_}"Let that car alone!"
10068-8{_}5281{_}a new voice took up the hail, a little nearer this time; and after it came the sound of a shot.
10068-8{_}5282{_}High up on the mountain's brow, against the sky, Johnnie caught a glimpse of the heads and shoulders of men, with the slanting bar of a gun barrel over one.
10068-8{_}5283{_}"Oh, hurry, Uncle Pros!"
10068-8{_}5284{_}she sobbed.
10068-8{_}5285{_}"Let me come back and help you."
10068-8{_}5286{_}But Passmore stumbled across the remaining space; mutely, with drawn face and loud, labouring breath he lifted Gray and thrust him any fashion into the tonneau, climbing blindly after.
10068-8{_}5287{_}The pursuit on the hill above broke into the open.
10068-8{_}5288{_}Johnnie moved the levers as Gray had shown her how to do, and with a bound of the great machine, they were off.
10068-8{_}5289{_}Stoddard, dazed, bruised, abraded, was back in the tonneau struggling up with Uncle Pros's assistance.
10068-8{_}5290{_}He could not help her.
10068-8{_}5291{_}She must know for herself and do the right thing.
10068-8{_}5292{_}The track led through the bushes, as they had found it that morning.
10068-8{_}5293{_}It was fairly good, but terribly steep.
10068-8{_}5294{_}She noted that the speed lever was at neutral.
10068-8{_}5295{_}She slipped it over to the first speed; the car was already leaping down the hill at a tremendous pace; yet those yelling voices were behind, and her pushing fingers carried the lever through second to the third speed without pausing.
10068-8{_}5296{_}Under this tremendous pressure the car jumped like a nervous horse, lurched drunkenly down the short way, but reeled successfully around the turn at the bottom.
10068-8{_}5297{_}Johnnie knew this was going too fast.
10068-8{_}5298{_}She debated the possibility of slackening the speed a bit as they struck the highway, such as it was.
10068-8{_}5299{_}Uncle Pros, yet gasping, was trying to help Gray into the seat; but with his hampering manacles and the jerking of the car, the younger man was still on his knees, when the chase burst through the bushes, scarcely more than three hundred feet behind them.
10068-8{_}5300{_}There was a hoarse baying of men's voices; there were four of them running hard, and two carried guns.
10068-8{_}5301{_}The noise of the machine, of course, prevented its occupants from distinguishing any word, but the menace of the open pursuit was apparent.
10068-8{_}5302{_}"Johnnie!"
10068-8{_}5303{_}cried Gray.
10068-8{_}5304{_}"Oh, this won't do!
10068-8{_}5305{_}For God's sake, Mr. Passmore, help me over there.
10068-8{_}5306{_}They wouldn't want to hurt her--but they're going to shoot.
10068-8{_}5307{_}She--"  The old man thrust Gray down, with a hand on his shoulder.
10068-8{_}5308{_}"You keep out o' range," he shouted close to Gray's ear.
10068-8{_}5309{_}"They won't aim to hit Johnnie; but you they'll pick off as far as they can see ye.
10068-8{_}5310{_}Bend low, honey," to the girl in the driver's seat.
10068-8{_}5311{_}"But freeze to it.
10068-8{_}5312{_}Johnnie ain't no niece of mine if she goes back on a friend."
10068-8{_}5313{_}The girl in front heard neither of them.
10068-8{_}5314{_}There was a bellowing detonation, and a spatter of shot fell about the flying car.
10068-8{_}5315{_}"That ain't goin' to hurt nobody," commented Pros philosophically.
10068-8{_}5316{_}"It's no more than buck-shot anyhow."
10068-8{_}5317{_}[Illustration: THE CAR WAS ALREADY LEAPING DOWN THE HILL AT A TREMENDOUS PACE]  But on the word followed a more ominous crack, and there was the whine of a bullet above them.
10068-8{_}5318{_}"My God, I can't let her do this," Gray protested.
10068-8{_}5319{_}But Johnnie turned over her shoulder a shining face from which all weariness had suddenly been erased, a glorified countenance that flung him the fleeting smile she had time to spare from the machine.
10068-8{_}5320{_}"You're in worse danger right now from my driving than you are from their guns," she panted.
10068-8{_}5321{_}As she spoke there sounded once more the ripping crack of a rifle, the singing of a bullet past them, and with it the flatter, louder noise of the shot-gun was repeated.
10068-8{_}5322{_}Her eye in the act of turning to her task, caught the silhouette of old Gideon Himes's uncouth figure relieved against the noonday sky, as he sprang high, both arms flung up, the hands empty and clutching, and pitched headlong to his face.
10068-8{_}5323{_}But her mind scarcely registered the impression, for a rifle ball struck the shaly edge of a bluff under which the road at this point ran, and tore loose a piece of the slate-like rock, which glanced whirling into the tonneau and grazed Gray Stoddard's temple.
10068-8{_}5324{_}He fell forward, crumpling down into the bottom of the vehicle.
10068-8{_}5325{_}"On--go on, honey!"
10068-8{_}5326{_}yelled Pros, motioning vehemently to the girl.
10068-8{_}5327{_}"Don't look back here--I'll tend to him"; and he stooped over the motionless form.
10068-8{_}5328{_}Then came the roaring impression of speed, of rushing bushes that gathered themselves and ran back past the car while, working under full power, it stood stationary, as it seemed to Johnnie, in the middle of a long, dusty gray ribbon that was the road.
10068-8{_}5329{_}The cries of the men behind them, all sounds of pursuit, were soon left so far in the distance that they were unheard.
10068-8{_}5330{_}"Ain't this rather fast?"
10068-8{_}5331{_}shouted Uncle Pros, who had lifted Stoddard's bleeding head to his knee and, crouched on the bottom of the tonneau, was shielding the younger man from further injury as the motor lurched and pitched.
10068-8{_}5332{_}"Yes, it's too fast," Johnnie screamed back to him.
10068-8{_}5333{_}"I'm trying to go slower, but the foot-brake won't hold.
10068-8{_}5334{_}Uncle Pros, is he hurt?
10068-8{_}5335{_}Is he hurt bad?"
10068-8{_}5336{_}"I don't think so, honey," roared the old man stoutly, guarding Gray's inert body with his arm.
10068-8{_}5337{_}Then, stretching up as he kneeled, and leaning forward as close to her ear as he could get: "But you git him to Cottonville quick as you can.
10068-8{_}5338{_}Don't you werry about goin' slow, unlessen you're scared yourself.
10068-8{_}5339{_}Thar ain't no tellin' who might pop up from behind these here bushes and take a chance shot at us as we go by."
10068-8{_}5340{_}Johnnie worked over her machine wildly.
10068-8{_}5341{_}Gray had told her of the foot-brake only; but her hand encountering the lever of the emergency brake, she grasped it at a hazard and shoved it forward, as the god of luck had ordered, just short of a zigzag in the steep mountain road which, at the speed they had been making, would have piled them, a mass of wreckage, beneath the cliff.
10068-8{_}5342{_}The sudden, violent check--shooting along at the speed they were, it amounted almost to a stoppage--gave the girl a sense of power.
10068-8{_}5343{_}If she could do that, they were fairly safe.
10068-8{_}5344{_}With the relief, her brain cleared; she was able to study the machine with some calmness.
10068-8{_}5345{_}Gray could not help her--out of the side of her eye she could see where he lay inert and senseless in Passmore's hold.
10068-8{_}5346{_}The lives of all three depended on her cool head at this moment.
10068-8{_}5347{_}She remembered now all that Stoddard had said the morning he taught her to run the car.
10068-8{_}5348{_}With one movement she threw off the switch, thus stopping the engine, entirely.
10068-8{_}5349{_}They must make it to Cottonville running by gravity wherever they could; since she had no means of knowing that there was sufficient gasoline in the tank, and it would not do to be overtaken or waylaid.
10068-8{_}5350{_}On and on they flew, around quick turns, along narrow ways that skirted tall bluffs, over stretches of comparatively level road, where Johnnie again switched on the engine and speeded up.
10068-8{_}5351{_}They were skimming down from the upper Unakas like a great bird whose powerful wings make nothing of distance.
10068-8{_}5352{_}But Johnnie's heart was as lead when she glanced back at the motionless figure in the tonneau, the white, blood-streaked face that lay on her uncle's arm.
10068-8{_}5353{_}She turned doggedly to her steering-wheel and levers, and took greater chances than ever with the going, for speed's sake.
10068-8{_}5354{_}The boy they had talked with two hours before at the chip pile, met them afoot.
10068-8{_}5355{_}He leaped into the bushes to let them pass, and stared after them with dilated eyes.
10068-8{_}5356{_}Johnnie never knew what he shouted.
10068-8{_}5357{_}They only saw his mouth open and working.
10068-8{_}5358{_}Mercifully, so far, they had met no vehicles.
10068-8{_}5359{_}But now the higher, wilder mountains were behind them, there was an occasional horseman.
10068-8{_}5360{_}As they neared Cottonville, and teams were numerous on the road, Johnnie, jealously unwilling to slacken speed, kept the horn going almost continuously.
10068-8{_}5361{_}People in wagons and buggies, or on foot, drawn out along the roadside, cupped hands to lips and yelled startled inquiries.
10068-8{_}5362{_}Johnnie bent above the steering-wheel and paid no attention.
10068-8{_}5363{_}Uncle Pros tried to answer with gesticulation or a shouted word, and sometimes those he replied to turned and ran, calling to others.
10068-8{_}5364{_}But it was black Jim, riding on Roan Sultan, out with the searchers, who saw and understood.
10068-8{_}5365{_}He looked down across the great two-mile turn beyond the Gap, and sighted the climbing car.
10068-8{_}5366{_}Where he stood it was less than an eighth of a mile below him; he could almost have thrown a stone into it.
10068-8{_}5367{_}He bent in his saddle, shaded his eyes, and gazed intently.
10068-8{_}5368{_}"Fo' God!"
10068-8{_}5369{_}he muttered under his breath.
10068-8{_}5370{_}"That's Mr. Gray hisself!
10068-8{_}5371{_}Them's the clothes he was wearin'!"
10068-8{_}5372{_}Whirling his horse and digging in the spurs, he rattled pell-mell down the opposite steep toward Cottonville, shouting as he went.
10068-8{_}5373{_}"They've done got him--they've found him!
10068-8{_}5374{_}Miss Johnnie Consadine's a-bringin' him down in his own cyar!"
10068-8{_}5375{_}At the Hardwick place, where the front lawn sloped down with its close-trimmed, green-velvet sward, stood two horses.
10068-8{_}5376{_}Charlie Conroy had come out as soon as the alarm was raised to help with the search.
10068-8{_}5377{_}He and Lydia had ridden together each day since.
10068-8{_}5378{_}Moving slowly along a quiet ravine yesterday, out of sight and hearing of the other searchers, Conroy had found an intimate moment in which to urge his suit.
10068-8{_}5379{_}She had begged a little time to consider, with so encouraging an aspect that, this morning, when he came out that they might join the party bound for the mountains, he brought the ring in his pocket.
10068-8{_}5380{_}The bulge of the big diamond showed through her left-hand glove.
10068-8{_}5381{_}She had taken him at last.
10068-8{_}5382{_}She told herself that it was the only thing to do.
10068-8{_}5383{_}Harriet Hardwick, who had returned from Watauga, since her sister would not come to her, stood in the door of the big house regarding them with a countenance of distinctly chastened rejoicing.
10068-8{_}5384{_}Conroy's own frame of mind was evident; deep satisfaction radiated from his commonplace countenance.
10068-8{_}5385{_}He was to be Jerome Hardwick's brother-in-law, an intimate member of the mill crowd.
10068-8{_}5386{_}He was as near being in love with Lydia Sessions at that moment as he ever would be.
10068-8{_}5387{_}As for Lydia herself, the last week had brought that thin face of hers to look all of its thirty odd years; and the smile which she turned upon her affianced was the product of conscientious effort.
10068-8{_}5388{_}She was safely in her saddle, and Conroy had just swung up to his own, when Jim came pelting down the Gap road toward the village.
10068-8{_}5389{_}They could see him across the slope of the hill.
10068-8{_}5390{_}Conroy cantered hastily up the street a bit to hear what the boy was vociferating.
10068-8{_}5391{_}Lydia's nerves quivered at sight of him returning.
10068-8{_}5392{_}"Hurrah!
10068-8{_}5393{_}Hurrah!"
10068-8{_}5394{_}shouted Conroy, waving his cap.
10068-8{_}5395{_}"Lord, Lord; Did you hear that, Lydia?
10068-8{_}5396{_}Hoo-ee, Mrs. Hardwick!
10068-8{_}5397{_}Did you hear what Jim's saying?
10068-8{_}5398{_}They've got Gray!
10068-8{_}5399{_}Johnnie Consadine's bringing him--in his own car."
10068-8{_}5400{_}Then turning once more to his companion: "Come on, dear; we'll ride right down to the hospital.
10068-8{_}5401{_}Jim said he was hurt.
10068-8{_}5402{_}That's where she would take him.
10068-8{_}5403{_}That Johnnie Consadine of yours is the girl--isn't she a wonder, though?"
10068-8{_}5404{_}Lydia braced herself.
10068-8{_}5405{_}It had come, and it was worse than she could have anticipated.
10068-8{_}5406{_}She cringed inwardly in remembrance; she wished she had not let Conroy make that pitying reference--unreproved, uncorrected--to Stoddard's being a rejected man.
10068-8{_}5407{_}But perhaps they were bringing Gray in dead, after all--she tried not to hope so.
10068-8{_}5408{_}The auto became visible, a tiny dark speck, away up in the Gap.
10068-8{_}5409{_}Then it was sweeping down the Gap road; and once more Conroy swung his cap and shouted, though it is to be questioned that any one marked him.
10068-8{_}5410{_}Below in the village the noisy clatter brought people to door and casement.
10068-8{_}5411{_}At the Himes boarding-house, a group had gathered by the gate.
10068-8{_}5412{_}At the window above, in an arm-chair, sat a thin little woman with great dark eyes, holding a sick child in her lap.
10068-8{_}5413{_}The sash was up, and both were carefully wrapped in a big shawl that was drawn over the two of them.
10068-8{_}5414{_}"Sis' Johnnie is comin' back; she sure is comin' back soon," Laurella was crooning to her baby.
10068-8{_}5415{_}"And we ain't goin' to work in no cotton mill, an' we ain't goin' to live in this ol' house any more.
10068-8{_}5416{_}Next thing we're a-goin' away with Sis' Johnnie and have a fi-ine house, where Pap Himes can't come about to be cross to Deanie."
10068-8{_}5417{_}High up on Unaka Mountain, where a cluttered mass of rock reared itself to front the noonday sun, an old man's figure, prone, the hands clutched full of leaf-mould, the gray face down amid the fern, Gideon Himes would never offer denial to those plans, nor seek to follow to that fine house.
10068-8{_}5418{_}The next moment an automobile flashed into sight coming down the long lower slope from the Gap, the horn blowing continuously, horsemen, pedestrians, buggies and wagons fleeing to the roadside bushes as it roared past in its cloud of dust.
10068-8{_}5419{_}"Look, honey, look--yon's Sis' Johnnie now!"
10068-8{_}5420{_}cried Laurella.
10068-8{_}5421{_}"She's a-runnin' Mr. Stoddard's car.
10068-8{_}5422{_}An' thar's Unc' Pros ... Is--my Lord!

10068-8{_}5424{_}Lydia and Conroy, hurrying down the street, drew up on the fringes of the little crowd that had gathered and was augmenting every moment, and Johnnie's face was turned to Stoddard in piteous questioning.
10068-8{_}5425{_}His eyes were open now.
10068-8{_}5426{_}He raised himself a bit on her uncle's arm, and declared in a fairly audible voice:  "I'm all right.
10068-8{_}5427{_}I'm not hurt."

10068-8{_}5431{_}she moaned.

10068-8{_}5440{_}"Pony!

10068-8{_}5445{_}piped Lissy from the porch.

10068-8{_}5448{_}asked Johnnie.
10068-8{_}5449{_}"We must get Mr. Stoddard on to his house."
10068-8{_}5450{_}The women and children drew back, the crowd ahead parted, and the car got under way once more.
10068-8{_}5451{_}The entire press of people followed in its wake, surged about it, augmenting at every corner.
10068-8{_}5452{_}"I'm afraid my horse won't stand this sort of thing," Lydia objected, desperately, reining in.
10068-8{_}5453{_}Conroy glanced at her in surprise.
10068-8{_}5454{_}Bay Dick was the soberest of mounts.
10068-8{_}5455{_}Then he looked wistfully after the crowd.

10068-8{_}5459{_}"I'll go with you."
10068-8{_}5460{_}One might as well have it done and over with.
10068-8{_}5461{_}And they hurried on to make up for lost time.
10068-8{_}5462{_}They saw the car turn in to the street which led to the Hardwick factory.
10068-8{_}5463{_}Somebody had hurried ahead and told MacPherson and Jerome Hardwick; and just as they came in sight, the office doors burst open and the two men came running hatless down the steps.
10068-8{_}5464{_}Suddenly the factory whistles roared out the signal that had been agreed upon, which bellowed to the hills the tidings that Gray Stoddard was found.
10068-8{_}5465{_}Three long calls and a short one--that meant that he was found alive.
10068-8{_}5466{_}As the din of it died down, Hexter's mills across the creek took up the message, and when they were silent, the old Victory came in on their heels, bawling it again.
10068-8{_}5467{_}Every whistle in Cottonville gave tongue, clamouring hoarsely above the valley, and out across the ranges, to the hundreds at their futile search, "Gray Stoddard is found.
10068-8{_}5468{_}Stoddard is found.
10068-8{_}5469{_}Alive.
10068-8{_}5470{_}He is brought in alive."
10068-8{_}5471{_}MacPherson ran up to one side of the car and Hardwick to the other.

10068-8{_}5473{_}inquired the Scotchman, his hands stretched out.
10068-8{_}5474{_}"Can you get out and come in?"
10068-8{_}5475{_}Hardwick demanded eagerly.
10068-8{_}5476{_}On the instant, the big gates swung wide, the factory poured out a tide of people as though the building had been afire.
10068-8{_}5477{_}At sight of Stoddard, the car, and Johnnie, a cheer went up, spontaneous, heart-shaking.
10068-8{_}5478{_}"My God--look at that!"
10068-8{_}5479{_}MacPherson's eyes had encountered the shackles on Stoddard's wrists.
10068-8{_}5480{_}"Lift him down--lift him out," cried Jerome Hardwick.
10068-8{_}5481{_}With tears on his tanned cheeks the Scotchman complied; and Hardwick's eyes, too, were wet as he saw it.
10068-8{_}5482{_}"We'll have those things off of him in no time," he shouted.

10068-8{_}5484{_}Send some of the mechanics here.
10068-8{_}5485{_}Where's Shade Buckheath?"
10068-8{_}5486{_}A dozen pairs of hands were stretched up to assist MacPherson and Pros Passmore.
10068-8{_}5487{_}As many as could get to the rescued man helped.
10068-8{_}5488{_}And when the crowd saw that shackled figure raised, and heard in the tense silence the clinking sound of the chains, a low groan went through it; more than one woman sobbed aloud.
10068-8{_}5489{_}But at this Gray raised his head a bit, and once more declared in a fairly strong voice:  "I'm not hurt, people--only a little crack on the head.
10068-8{_}5490{_}I'm all right--thanks to her," and he motioned toward the girl in the car, who was watching anxiously.
10068-8{_}5491{_}Then the ever thickening throng went wild; and as Gray was carried up the steps and disappeared through the office doors, it turned toward the automobile, surging about the car, a sea of friendly, admiring faces, most of them touched with the tenderness of tears, and cheered its very heart out for Johnnie Consadine.
10068-8{_}5492{_}CHAPTER XXV  THE FUTURE  "Gray!"
10068-8{_}5493{_}it was Uncle Pros's voice, and Uncle Pros's face looked in at the office door.
10068-8{_}5494{_}"Could I bother you a minute about the sidewalk in front of the place up yon?
10068-8{_}5495{_}Mr. Hexter told me you'd know whether the grade was right, and I could let the workmen go ahead."
10068-8{_}5496{_}Stoddard swung around from his desk and looked at the old man.
10068-8{_}5497{_}"Come right in," he said.
10068-8{_}5498{_}"I'm not busy--I'm just pretending this morning.
10068-8{_}5499{_}MacPherson won't give me anything to do.
10068-8{_}5500{_}He persists in considering me still an invalid."
10068-8{_}5501{_}Uncle Pros came slowly in and laid his hat down gingerly before seating himself.
10068-8{_}5502{_}He was dressed in the garb which, with money, he would always have selected--the village ideal of a rich gentleman's wear--and he looked unbelievably tall and imposing in his black broadcloth.
10068-8{_}5503{_}When the matter of the patent was made known to Jerome Hardwick, a company was hastily formed to take hold of it, which advanced the ready money for Johnnie and her family to place themselves.
10068-8{_}5504{_}Mrs. Hexter, who had been all winter in Boston, had decided, suddenly, to go abroad; and when her husband wired her to know if he might let the house to the Consadine-Passmore household, she made a quick, warm response.
10068-8{_}5505{_}So they were domiciled in a ready-prepared home of elegance and beauty.
10068-8{_}5506{_}Though the place at Cottonville had been only a winter residence with Mrs. Hexter, she was a woman of taste, and had always had large means at her command.
10068-8{_}5507{_}With all a child's plasticity, Laurella dropped into the improved order of things.
10068-8{_}5508{_}Her cleverness in selecting the proper wear for herself and children was nothing short of marvellous; and her calm acceptance of the new state of affairs, the acme of good breeding.
10068-8{_}5509{_}Johnnie immediately set about seeing that Mavity Bence and Mandy Meacham were comfortably provided for in the old boarding-house, where she assured Gray they could do more good than many Uplift clubs.
10068-8{_}5510{_}"We'll have a truck-patch there, and a couple of cows and some chickens," she said.
10068-8{_}5511{_}"That'll be good for the table, and it'll give Mandy the work she loves to do.
10068-8{_}5512{_}Aunt Mavity can have some help in the house--there's always a girl or two breaking down in the mills, who would be glad to have a chance at housework for a while."
10068-8{_}5513{_}Now Pros looked all about him, and seemed in no haste to begin, though Gray knew well there was something on his mind.
10068-8{_}5514{_}Finally Stoddard observed, smiling:  "You're the very man I wanted to see, Uncle Pros.
10068-8{_}5515{_}I rang up the house just now, but Johnnie said you had started down to the mills.
10068-8{_}5516{_}What do you think I've found out about our mine?"
10068-8{_}5517{_}Certainly the old man looked very tall and dignified in his new splendours; but now he was all boy, leaning eagerly forward to half whisper:  "I don't know--what?"
10068-8{_}5518{_}Stoddard's face was scarcely less animated as he searched hastily in the pigeon-holes of his desk.
10068-8{_}5519{_}The patent might have a company to manage its affairs, but the mine on Big Unaka was sacred to these two, in whom the immortal urchin sufficiently survived to make mine-hunting and exploiting delectable employment.
10068-8{_}5520{_}"Why, Uncle Pros, it isn't silver at all.
10068-8{_}5521{_}It's--" Gray looked up and caught the woeful drop of the face before him, and hastened on to add, "It's better than silver--it's nickel.
10068-8{_}5522{_}The price of silver fluctuates; but the world supply of nickel is limited, and nickel's a sure thing."
10068-8{_}5523{_}Pros Passmore leaned back in his chair, digesting this new bit of information luxuriously.
10068-8{_}5524{_}"Nickel," he said reflectively.
10068-8{_}5525{_}And again he repeated the word to himself.
10068-8{_}5526{_}"Nickel.
10068-8{_}5527{_}Well, I don't know but what that's finer.
10068-8{_}5528{_}Leastways, it's likelier.
10068-8{_}5529{_}To say a silver mine, always seemed just like taking money out of the ground; but then, nickels are money too--and enough of 'em is all a body needs."
10068-8{_}5530{_}"These people say the ore is exceptionally fine."
10068-8{_}5531{_}Stoddard had got out the letter now and was glancing over it.
10068-8{_}5532{_}"They're sending down an expert, and you and I will go up with him as soon as he gets here.
10068-8{_}5533{_}There are likely to be other valuable minerals as by-products in a nickel mine.
10068-8{_}5534{_}And we want to build an ideal mining village, as well as model cotton mills.
10068-8{_}5535{_}Oh, we've got the work cut out for us and laid right to hand!
10068-8{_}5536{_}If we don't do our little share toward solving some problems, it will be strange."
10068-8{_}5537{_}"Cur'us how things turns out in this world," the old man ruminated.
10068-8{_}5538{_}"Ever sence I was a little chap settin' on my granddaddy's knees by the hearth--big hickory fire a-roarin' up the chimbly, wind a-goin' 'whooh!'
10068-8{_}5539{_}overhead, an' me with my eyes like saucers a-listenin' to his tales of the silver mine that the Injuns had--ever sence that time I've hunted that thar mine."
10068-8{_}5540{_}He laughed chucklingly, deep in his throat.
10068-8{_}5541{_}"Thar wasn't a wild-catter that could have a hideout safe from me.
10068-8{_}5542{_}They just had to trust me.
10068-8{_}5543{_}I crawled into every hole.
10068-8{_}5544{_}I came mighty near seein' the end of every cave--but one.
10068-8{_}5545{_}And that cave was the one whar my Mammy kept her milk and butter--the springhouse whar they put you in prison.
10068-8{_}5546{_}Somehow, I never did think about goin' to the end of that.
10068-8{_}5547{_}Looked like it was too near home to have a silver mine in it; and thar the stuff lay and waited for the day when I should take a notion to find a pretty rock for Deanie, and crawl back in thar and keep a crawlin', till I just fell over it, all croppin' out in the biggest kind of vein."
10068-8{_}5548{_}Gray had heard Uncle Pros tell the story many times, but it had a perennial charm.
10068-8{_}5549{_}"Then I lost six months--plumb lost 'em, you know.
10068-8{_}5550{_}And time I come to myself, Johnnie an' me was a-huntin' for you.
10068-8{_}5551{_}And there we found you shut in that thar same cave; and I was so tuck up with that matter that I never once thought, till I got you home, to wonder did Buckheath and the rest of 'em know that they'd penned you in the silver mine.
10068-8{_}5552{_}I ain't never asked you, but you'd have knowed if they had."
10068-8{_}5553{_}"I should have known anything that Rudd Dawson or Groner or Venters knew," Gray said, "but I'm not sure about Buckheath or Himes.
10068-8{_}5554{_}However, Himes is dead, and Buckheath--I don't suppose anybody in Cottonville will ever see him again."
10068-8{_}5555{_}Pros's face changed instantly.
10068-8{_}5556{_}He leaned abruptly forward and laid a hand on the other's knee.
10068-8{_}5557{_}"That's exactly what I came down here to speak with you about, Gray," he said.
10068-8{_}5558{_}"They've fetched Shade Buckheath in--now, what do you make out of that?"
10068-8{_}5559{_}Stoddard shoved the letter from the Eastern mining man back in its pigeon-hole.
10068-8{_}5560{_}"Well," he said slowly, "I didn't expect that.
10068-8{_}5561{_}I thought of course Shade was safely out of the country.
10068-8{_}5562{_}I--Passmore, I'm sorry they've got him."
10068-8{_}5563{_}After a little silence he spoke again.
10068-8{_}5564{_}"What do I make of it?
10068-8{_}5565{_}Why, that there are some folks up on Big Unaka who need pretty badly to appear as very law-abiding citizens.
10068-8{_}5566{_}I'll wager anything that Groner and Rudd Dawson brought Shade in."
10068-8{_}5567{_}Uncle Pros nodded seriously.
10068-8{_}5568{_}"Them's the very fellers," he said.
10068-8{_}5569{_}"Reckon they've talked pretty free to you.
10068-8{_}5570{_}I never axed ye, Gray--how did they treat ye?"
10068-8{_}5571{_}"Dawson was the best friend I had," Stoddard returned promptly.
10068-8{_}5572{_}"When I got to the big turn on Sultan--coming home that Friday morning --Buckheath met me, and asked me to go down to Burnt Cabin and help him with a man that had fallen and hurt himself on the rocks.
10068-8{_}5573{_}Dawson told me afterward that he and Jesse Groner were posted at the roadside to stop me and hem me in before I got to the bluff.
10068-8{_}5574{_}I've described to you how Buckheath tried to back Sultan over the edge, and I got off on the side where the two were, not noticing them till they tied me hand and foot.
10068-8{_}5575{_}They almost came to a clinch with Buckheath then and there.
10068-8{_}5576{_}You ought to have heard Groner swear!
10068-8{_}5577{_}It was like praying gone wrong."
10068-8{_}5578{_}"Uh-huh," agreed Pros, "Jess is a terrible wicked man--in speech that-a-way--but he's good-hearted."
10068-8{_}5579{_}"That first scrimmage showed me just what the men were after," Stoddard said.
10068-8{_}5580{_}"Buckheath plainly wanted me put out of the way; but the others had some vague idea of holding me for a ransom and getting money out of the Hardwicks.
10068-8{_}5581{_}Dawson complained always that he thought the mills owed him money.
10068-8{_}5582{_}He said they must have sold his girl's body for as much as a hundred dollars, and he felt that he'd been cheated.
10068-8{_}5583{_}Oh, it was all crazy stuff!
10068-8{_}5584{_}But he and the others had justified themselves; and they had no notion of standing for what Buckheath was after.
10068-8{_}5585{_}I was one of the cotton-mill men to them; they had no personal malice.
10068-8{_}5586{_}"Through the long evenings when Groner or Dawson or Will Venters was guarding me--or maybe all three of them--we used to talk; and it surprised me to find how simple and childish those fellows were.
10068-8{_}5587{_}They were as kind to me as though I had been a brother, and treated me courteously always.
10068-8{_}5588{_}"Little by little, I got at the whole thing from them.
10068-8{_}5589{_}It seems that Buckheath took advantage of the feeling there was in the mountains against the mill men on account of the hospital and some other matters.
10068-8{_}5590{_}He went up there and interviewed anybody that he thought might join him in a vendetta.
10068-8{_}5591{_}I imagine he found plenty of them that were ready to talk and some that were willing to do; but it chanced that Dawson and Jesse Groner were coming down to Cottonville that morning I passed Buckheath at the Hardwick gate, and he must have cut across the turn and followed me, intending to pick a quarrel.
10068-8{_}5592{_}Then he met Dawson and Groner and framed up this other plan with their assistance.
10068-8{_}5593{_}"Uncle Pros, I want you to help me out.
10068-8{_}5594{_}If Buckheath has to stand trial, how are we--any of us--going to testify without making it hard on the Dawson crowd?
10068-8{_}5595{_}I expect to live here the rest of my days.
10068-8{_}5596{_}Here's this mine of ours.
10068-8{_}5597{_}And right here I mean to build a big mill and work out my plans.
10068-8{_}5598{_}I think you know that I hope to marry a mountain wife, and I can't afford to quarrel with those folks."
10068-8{_}5599{_}Uncle Pros's chin dropped to his breast, his eyes half closed as he sat thinking intently.
10068-8{_}5600{_}"Well," he said finally, "they won't have nothing worse than manslaughter against Shade.
10068-8{_}5601{_}It can't be proved that he intended to shoot Pap--'cause he didn't.
10068-8{_}5602{_}If he was shootin' after us--there's the thing we don't want to bring up.
10068-8{_}5603{_}You was down in the bottom of the cyar, an' I had my back to him, and so did Johnnie, and we don't know anything about what was done--ain't that so?
10068-8{_}5604{_}As for you, you've already told Mr. Hardwick and the others that you was taken prisoner and detained by parties unknown.
10068-8{_}5605{_}Johnnie an' me was gettin' you out of the springhouse and away in the machine.
10068-8{_}5606{_}Then Gid and Shade comes up, and thinkin' we're the other crowd stealin' the machine--they try to catch us and turn loose at us--that makes a pretty good story, don't it?"
10068-8{_}5607{_}"It does if Dawson and Groner and Venters agree to it," Stoddard laughed.
10068-8{_}5608{_}"But somebody will have to communicate with them before they tell another one--or several others."
10068-8{_}5609{_}"I'll see to that, Gray," Pros said, rising and preparing to go.
10068-8{_}5610{_}"Boy," he looked down fondly at the younger man, and set a brown right hand on his shoulder, "you never done a wiser thing nor a kinder in your life, than when you forgave your enemies that time, I'll bet you could ride the Unakas from end to end, the balance o' your days, the safest man that ever travelled their trails."
10068-8{_}5611{_}"Talking silver mine?"
10068-8{_}5612{_}inquired MacPherson, putting his quizzical face in at the door.
10068-8{_}5613{_}"No," returned Stoddard.
10068-8{_}5614{_}"We were just mentioning my pestilent cotton-mill projects.
10068-8{_}5615{_}By this time next year, you and Hardwick will be wanting to have me abated as a nuisance."
10068-8{_}5616{_}"No, no," remonstrated MacPherson, coming in and leaning with affectionate familiarity on the younger man's chair.
10068-8{_}5617{_}"There's no pestilence in you, Gray.
10068-8{_}5618{_}You couldn't be a nuisance if you tried.
10068-8{_}5619{_}People who will work out their theories stand to do good in the world; it's only the fellows who are content with bellowing them out that I object to."
10068-8{_}5620{_}"Better be careful!"
10068-8{_}5621{_}laughed Stoddard.
10068-8{_}5622{_}"We'll make you vice-president of the company."
10068-8{_}5623{_}"Is that an offer?"
10068-8{_}5624{_}countered MacPherson swiftly.
10068-8{_}5625{_}"I've got a bit of money to invest in this county; and Hardwick has ever a new brother-in-law or such that looks longingly at my shoes."
10068-8{_}5626{_}"You'd furnish the conservative element, surely," debated Stoddard.
10068-8{_}5627{_}"I'd keep you from bankruptcy," grunted the Scotchman, as he laid a small book on Gray's desk.
10068-8{_}5628{_}"I doubt not Providence demands it of me."
10068-8{_}5629{_}Evening was closing in with a greenish-yellow sunset, and a big full moon pushing up to whiten the sky above it.
10068-8{_}5630{_}It was late March now, and the air was full of vernal promise.
10068-8{_}5631{_}Johnnie stepped out on the porch and glanced toward the west.
10068-8{_}5632{_}She was expecting Gray that evening.
10068-8{_}5633{_}Would there be time before he came, she wondered, for a little errand she wanted to do?
10068-8{_}5634{_}Turning back into the hall, she caught a jacket from the hook where it hung and hurried down to the gate, settling her arms in the sleeves as she ran.
10068-8{_}5635{_}There would be time if she went fast.
10068-8{_}5636{_}She wished to get the little packet into which she had made Gray's letters months ago, dreading to look even at the folded outsides of them, tucking them away on the high shelf of her dress-closet at the Pap Himes boarding-house, and trying to forget them.
10068-8{_}5637{_}Nobody would know where to look but herself.
10068-8{_}5638{_}She got permission from Mavity to go upstairs.
10068-8{_}5639{_}Once there, the letters made their own plea; and alone in the little room that was lately her own, she opened the packet, carrying the contents to the fading light and glancing over sheet after sheet.
10068-8{_}5640{_}She knew them all by heart.
10068-8{_}5641{_}How often she had stood at that very window devouring these same words, not realizing then, as she did now, what deep meaning was in each phrase, how the feeling expressed increased from the first to the last.
10068-8{_}5642{_}Across the ravine, one of the loom fixers found the evening warm enough to sit on the porch playing his guitar.
10068-8{_}5643{_}The sound of the twanging strings, and the appealing vibration of his young voice in a plaintive minor air, came over to her.
10068-8{_}5644{_}She gathered the sheets together and pressed them to her face as though they were flowers, or the hands of little children.
10068-8{_}5645{_}"I've got to tell him--to-night," she whispered to herself, in the dusky, small, dismantled room.
10068-8{_}5646{_}"I've got to get him to see it as I do.
10068-8{_}5647{_}I must make myself worthy of him before I let him take me for his own."
10068-8{_}5648{_}She thrust the letters into the breast-pocket of her coat and ran downstairs.
10068-8{_}5649{_}Mavity Bence stood in the hall, plainly awaiting her.
10068-8{_}5650{_}"Honey," she began fondly, "I've been putting away Pap's things to-day--jest like you oncet found me putting away Lou's.
10068-8{_}5651{_}I came on this here."
10068-8{_}5652{_}And then Johnnie noticed a folded bandanna in her hands.
10068-8{_}5653{_}"You-all asked me to let ye go through and find that nickel ore, and ye brung it out in a pasteboard box; but this here is what it was in on the day your Uncle Pros fetched hit here, and I thought maybe you'd take a interest in having the handkercher that your fortune come down the mountains in."
10068-8{_}5654{_}"Yes, indeed, Aunt Mavity," said Johnnie, taking the bandanna into her own hands.
10068-8{_}5655{_}"Pap, he's gone," the poor woman went on tremulously, "an' the evil what he done--or wanted to do--is a thing that I reckon you can afford to forget.
10068-8{_}5656{_}You're a mighty happy woman, Johnnie Consadine; the Lord knows you deserve to be."
10068-8{_}5657{_}She stood looking after the girl as she went out into the twilit street.
10068-8{_}5658{_}Johnnie was dressed as she chose now, not as she must, and her clothing showed itself to be of the best.
10068-8{_}5659{_}Anything that might be had in Wautaga was within her means; and the tall, graceful figure passing so quietly down the street would never have been taken for other than a member of what we are learning to call the "leisure class."
10068-8{_}5660{_}When the shadows at the end of the block swallowed her up, Mavity turned, wiping her eyes, and addressed herself to her tasks.
10068-8{_}5661{_}"I reckon Lou would 'a' been just like that if she'd 'a' lived," she said to Mandy Meacham, with the tender fatuity of mothers.
10068-8{_}5662{_}"Johnnie seems like a daughter to me--an' I know in my soul no daughter could be kinder.
10068-8{_}5663{_}Look at her makin' me keep every cent Pap had in the bank, when Laurelly could have claimed it all and kep' it."
10068-8{_}5664{_}"Yes, an' addin' somethin' to it," put in Mandy.
10068-8{_}5665{_}"I do love 'em both--Johnnie an' Deanie.
10068-8{_}5666{_}Ef I ever was so fortunate as to get a man and be wedded and have chaps o' my own, I know mighty well and good I couldn't love any one of 'em any better than I do Deanie.
10068-8{_}5667{_}An' yet Johnnie's quare.
10068-8{_}5668{_}I always will say that Johnnie Consadine is quare.
10068-8{_}5669{_}What in the nation does she want to go chasin' off to Yurrup for, when she's got everything that heart could desire or mind think of right here in Cottonville?"
10068-8{_}5670{_}That same question was being put even more searchingly to Johnnie by somebody else at the instant when Mandy enunciated it.
10068-8{_}5671{_}She had found Gray waiting for her at the gate of her home.
10068-8{_}5672{_}"Let's walk here a little while before we go in," he suggested.
10068-8{_}5673{_}"I went up to the house and found you were out.
10068-8{_}5674{_}The air is delightful, and I've got something I want to say to you."
10068-8{_}5675{_}He had put his arm under hers, and they strolled together down the long walk that led to the front of the lawn.
10068-8{_}5676{_}The evening air was pure and keen, tingling with the breath of the wakening season.
10068-8{_}5677{_}"Sweetheart," Gray broke out suddenly, "I've been thinking day and night since we last talked together about this year abroad that you're planning.
10068-8{_}5678{_}I certainly don't want to put my preferences before yours.
10068-8{_}5679{_}I only want to be very sure that I know what your real preferences are," and he turned and searched her face with a pair of ardent eyes.
10068-8{_}5680{_}"I think I ought to go," the girl said in a very low voice, her head drooped, her own eyes bent toward the path at her feet.
10068-8{_}5681{_}"Why?"
10068-8{_}5682{_}whispered her lover.
10068-8{_}5683{_}"I--oh, Gray--you know.
10068-8{_}5684{_}If we should ever be married--well, then," in answer to a swift, impatient exclamation, "when we are married, if you should show that you were ashamed of me--I think it would kill me.
10068-8{_}5685{_}No, don't say there's not any danger.
10068-8{_}5686{_}You might have plenty of reason.
10068-8{_}5687{_}And I--I want to be safe, Gray--safe, if I can."
10068-8{_}5688{_}Gray regarded the beautiful, anxious face long and thoughtfully.
10068-8{_}5689{_}Yes, of course it was possible for her to feel that way.
10068-8{_}5690{_}Assurance was so deep and perfect in his own heart, that he had not reflected what it might lack in hers.
10068-8{_}5691{_}"Dear girl," he said, pausing and making her look at him, "how little you do know of me, after all!
10068-8{_}5692{_}Do I care so much for what people say?
10068-8{_}5693{_}Aren't you always having to reprove me because I so persistently like what I like, without reference to the opinions of the world?
10068-8{_}5694{_}Besides, you're a beauty," with tender brusqueness, "and a charmer that steals the hearts of men.
10068-8{_}5695{_}If you don't know all this, it isn't from lack of telling.
10068-8{_}5696{_}Moreover, I can keep on informing you.
10068-8{_}5697{_}A year of European travel could not make you any more beautiful, Johnnie--or sweeter.
10068-8{_}5698{_}You may not believe me, but there's little the 'European capitals' could add to your native bearing--you must have learned that simple dignity from these mountains of yours.
10068-8{_}5699{_}Of course, if you wanted to go for pleasure--" His head a little on one side, he regarded her with a tender, half-quizzical smile, hoping he had sounded the note that would bring him swift surrender.
10068-8{_}5700{_}"It isn't altogether for myself--there are the others," Johnnie told him, lifting honest eyes to his in the dim moonlight.
10068-8{_}5701{_}"They're all I had in the world, Gray, till you came into my life, and I must keep my own.
10068-8{_}5702{_}I belong to a people who never give up anything they love."
10068-8{_}5703{_}Stoddard dropped an arm about his beloved, and turned her that she might face the windows of the house behind them, bending to set his cheek against hers and direct her gaze.
10068-8{_}5704{_}"Look there," he whispered, laughingly.
10068-8{_}5705{_}She looked and saw her mother, clad in such wear as Laurella's taste could select and Laurella's beauty make effective.
10068-8{_}5706{_}The slight, dark little woman was coming in from the dining room with her children all about her, a noble group.
10068-8{_}5707{_}"Your mother is much more the fine lady than you'll ever be, Johnnie Stoddard," Gray said, giving her the name that always brought the blood to the girl's cheek and made her dumb before him.
10068-8{_}5708{_}"You know your Uncle Pros and I are warmly attached to each other.
10068-8{_}5709{_}"What is it you'd be waiting for, girl?
10068-8{_}5710{_}Why, Johnnie, a man has just so long to live on this earth, and the years in which he has loved are the only years that count--would you be throwing one of these away?
10068-8{_}5711{_}A year--twelve months--three hundred and sixty-five days--cast to the void.
10068-8{_}5712{_}You reckless creature!"
10068-8{_}5713{_}He cupped his hands about her beautiful, fair face and lifted it, studying it.
10068-8{_}5714{_}"Johnnie--Johnnie--Johnnie Stoddard; the one woman out of all the world for me," he murmured, his deep voice dropping to a wooing cadence.
10068-8{_}5715{_}"I couldn't love you better--I shall never love you less.
10068-8{_}5716{_}Don't let us foolishly throw away a year out of the days which will be vouchsafed us together.
10068-8{_}5717{_}Don't do it, darling--it's folly."
10068-8{_}5718{_}Hard-pressed, Johnnie made only a sort of inarticulate response.
10068-8{_}5719{_}"Come, love, sit a moment with me, here," pleaded Gray, indicating a small bench hidden among the evergreens and shrubs at the end of the path.
10068-8{_}5720{_}"Sit down, and let's reason this thing out."
10068-8{_}5721{_}"Reasoning with you," began Johnnie, helplessly, "isn't--it isn't reasonable!"
10068-8{_}5722{_}"It is," he told her, in that deep, masterful tone which, like a true woman, she both loved and dreaded.
10068-8{_}5723{_}"It's the height of reasonableness.
10068-8{_}5724{_}Why, dear, the great primal reason of all things speaks through me.
10068-8{_}5725{_}And I won't let you throw away a year of our love.
10068-8{_}5726{_}Johnnie, it isn't as though we'd been neighbours, and grown up side by side.
10068-8{_}5727{_}I came from the ends of the earth to find you, darling--and I knew my own as soon as I saw you."
10068-8{_}5728{_}He put out his arms and gathered her into a close embrace.
10068-8{_}5729{_}For a space they rested so, murmuring question and reply, checked or answered by swift, sweet kisses.
10068-8{_}5730{_}"The first time I ever saw you, love...."  "Oh, in thoze dusty old shoes and a sunbonnet!
10068-8{_}5731{_}Could you love me then, Gray?"
10068-8{_}5732{_}"The same as at this moment, sweetheart.
10068-8{_}5733{_}Shoes and sunbonnets--I'm ashamed of you now, Johnnie, in earnest.
10068-8{_}5734{_}What do such things matter?"
10068-8{_}5735{_}"And that morning on the mountain, when we got the moccasin flowers," the girl's voice took up the theme.
10068-8{_}5736{_}"I--it was sweet to be with you--and bitter, too.
10068-8{_}5737{_}I could not dream then that you were for me.
10068-8{_}5738{_}And afterward--the long, black, dreadful time when you seemed so utterly lost to me--"  At the mention of those months, Gray stopped her words with a kiss.
10068-8{_}5739{_}"Mine," he whispered with his lips against hers, "Out of all the world--mine."
